shelter, and veterinary care when needed to prevent suffering, or to cruelly or
unnecessarily expose any such animal in hot, stormy, cold or inclement weather,
or to carry any such animal in or upon any vehicle in a cruel or inhumane
manner.
      1.   The term "shelter", as it applies to pets, shall mean a
moistureproof structure of suitable size to accommodate the pet and allow
retention of body heat, made of durable material with a solid floor raised at
least two inches (2") from the ground and with the entrance protected from
direct wind and rain.
      2.   Such structure shall be provided with sufficient quantity of
suitable bedding to provide insulation and protection against cold or dampness.
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, instigate or permit any
dogfight, cockfight or other combat between animals or between animals and
humans.
   D.   No owner of an animal shall abandon such animal where it may become a
public charge or may suffer injury, hunger or exposure.
   E.   No person shall give away any dog, cat or other live animal, fish,
reptile or bird as a prize for or an inducement to enter any contest, game or
other competition; as an inducement to enter a place of amusement; or as an
incentive to enter into any business agreement whereby the offer was for the
purpose of attracting trade. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   An owner or keeper of any dog, cat, or other animal shall exercise
proper care and control of such dog, cat, or other animal to prevent such
animal from committing any of the following:
      1.   Bite or attack anyone when unprovoked;
      2.   Destroy private property of others;
      3.   Scatter refuse;
      4.   Chase vehicles;
      5.   Create unreasonable annoyance or discomfort to others; or
      6.   Cause unsanitary conditions within village limits.
   B.   Any owner or keeper who violates subsection A of this section shall be
fined no less than three hundred dollars ($300.00) and no more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00).
   C.   No owner or keeper of any dog, cat, or other animal which has attacked
or bitten anyone when unprovoked shall keep such dog, cat, or other animal
within village limits.
   D.   Upon the filing of a complaint of a violation of subsection C of this
section, the village president or the chief of police is authorized to order
the animal involved to be impounded, and held in confinement at the owner's
expense in addition to any penalties resulting as a resolution of the
complaint. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
ARTICLE A. DOGS AND CATS
SECTION:
5-1A-1: Animal Control Officer
5-1A-2: License And Registration Required
5-1A-3: Rabies Inoculation Required
5-1A-4: Display Of License Tag Or Microchip
5-1A-5: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
5-1A-6: Dog Nuisances Declared
5-1A-7: Impoundment And Redemption Procedures
5-1A-8: Records Kept
5-1A-9: Dog Bites; Rabies Suspects
5-1A-10: Penalties
5-1A-1: ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER:
   A.   Appointment: An animal control officer may be appointed by the village
president, by and with the consent of the board of trustees. The animal control
officer shall be the chief of police unless other appointment is made by the
village president, by and with the consent of the board of trustees.
   B.   Duties And Powers: The duties and the powers of the animal control
officer are:
      1.   The animal control officer shall be authorized to make all necessary
arrests in carrying out the provisions of this article.
      2.   The animal control officer is hereby charged with the duty of
impounding all dogs running at large in violation of the provisions of this
article.
      3.   Respond in a timely manner to complaints or incidents of violations
of this article.
      4.   Capture/apprehend stray dogs or cats that have been involved in a
bite incident.
      5.   Keep a monthly summary. Turn in these reports to the village clerk
monthly. Complete animal incident reports and turn these in to the village
clerk after each incident.
      6.   Attend required meetings and activities as directed by the village
board.
      7.   Cooperate with county and state law enforcement agencies regarding
animal concerns.
      8.   Ensure that all animal control equipment belonging to the village,
including cages, kennels and live traps, are properly maintained and cleaned.
      9.   If a live trap is necessary to catch a cat involved in a bite
incident, such trap must be humanely set and checked every twelve (12) hours or
sooner.
      10.   Maintain Illinois state licensed and approved impoundment
facilities or contract for services that meet those established standards that
will provide and care for impounded animals. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-
1-2006)
5-1A-2: LICENSE AND REGISTRATION REQUIRED:
   A.   No dog over sixteen (16) weeks of age shall be permitted to be or
remain in the village without being licensed as hereinafter provided.
   B.   All dogs kept in the village shall be registered with Lee County animal
control in accordance with Lee County animal control ordinances and state of
Illinois statutes.
   C.   Application for a license from Lee County animal control must be made
within thirty (30) days after obtaining a dog sixteen (16) weeks of age or at
the time the animal reaches the age of sixteen (16) weeks, whichever is longer.
This requirement will not apply to a nonresident keeping a dog within the
village not longer than thirty (30) days, nor to a resident of the village
temporarily keeping an animal for not longer than thirty (30) days.
   D.   The village clerk shall maintain a record of the identifying numbers of
all tags (and/or microchips) issued by Lee County animal control to residents
of the village of Franklin Grove, and shall make this record available to the
public within a reasonable time upon request.
   E.   No person may use any license for any other animal than the animal for
which it was issued. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1A-3: RABIES INOCULATION REQUIRED:
It shall be the duty of the owner or person in custody of any dog kept in the
village to have the dog inoculated against rabies at sixteen (16) weeks of age
and once per year thereafter. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1A-4: DISPLAY OF LICENSE TAG OR MICROCHIP:
It shall be the duty of the owner to cause the license tag or an approved
microchip issued by Lee County animal control to be securely attached around
the dog's neck (tag), or under the skin in the neck area (chip) and kept there
at all times during the license period. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-
2006)
5-1A-5: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Running At Large: It is unlawful for the owner or keeper of any dog to
permit such animal to run at large within the village limits. The owner or
keeper of any dog shall not permit such animal to go beyond the premises of the
owner or keeper unless such dog is securely leashed or otherwise securely
restrained.
   B.   Dangerous Or Sick Dogs Running At Large: No vicious, dangerous, or
ferocious dog, or dog sick with, or liable to communicate hydrophobia or other
contagious or infectious diseases shall be permitted to run at large within the
village.
   C.   Disturbing The Peace: No person owning or keeping any dog shall permit
such dog to disturb the peace and quiet of the neighborhood by barking, making
other loud or unusual noises, or by running across or through cultivated
gardens or fields.
   D.   Removal Of Waste: The owner or keeper of a dog must remove immediately
any waste left by the dog on any property within the village limits other than
the property of the owner or keeper of said dog. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff.
1-1-2006)
5-1A-6: DOG NUISANCES DECLARED:
Any dog found in the village either without a license or running at large under
conditions set forth above shall be declared to be a nuisance and shall be
impounded as hereinafter provided. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1A-7: IMPOUNDMENT AND REDEMPTION PROCEDURES:
   A.   Public Notice Of Impoundment: Public notice of the impounding of any
dog shall be given by posting one copy of the impounding notice on the front
window of the village hall not more than twenty four (24) hours after animal is
impounded.
   B.   Impounding Notice: The notice shall provide a description of the dog,
the date of impounding, and the procedure for redeeming the impounded animal.
Redemption of the dog requires that all fees relating to the impoundment be
paid before the animal is released to include, but not be limited to, fines,
boarding fees, veterinary fees, licensing fees, and transportation fees.
   C.   Disposition Of Impounded Dogs: All dogs impounded by the village shall
be transferred as soon as possible to the custody of the Lee County animal
control officer. All dogs requiring holding until transfer can be made shall be
impounded in a state approved holding facility provided by the village or to
such a service as contracted for by the village.
   D.   Impoundment Authority: Any police officer, animal control officer, or
elected officer of the village is authorized to impound any dog found to be in
any manner in violation of this code.
   E.   Licensed Dogs Impounded: It shall be the duty of the animal control
officer, or his designee, to cause notice to be served in person, by telephone,
or by certified mail upon the registered owner of any licensed dog impounded
under the provisions of this article, and to post the notice of impoundment if
the owner cannot be reached in person or by telephone.
   F.   Redemption Of Dogs: The owner or owners of any dogs impounded hereunder
may redeem the same by paying all the costs, charges, and penalties assessed,
if any, that have accrued up to the time of making the redemption. When all
accrued fees have been paid, the animal control officer may authorize the
release of the dog to the owner thereof. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-
2006)
5-1A-8: RECORDS KEPT:
   A.   Immediately after impounding any dog hereunder, it shall be the duty of
the animal control officer to enter upon the records of the police department,
in a book to be kept by him for such purpose, the date of impounding, a
description of the dog impounded and a record as to whether such dog has been
licensed and tagged by the provisions of this article.
   B.   It shall be the duty of the village clerk to maintain a fee schedule of
costs associated with impounding a dog under the provisions of this code, and
to make the schedule available to the general public upon request. (Ord. 657-
05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1A-9: DOG BITES; RABIES SUSPECTS:
Whenever any dog bites a person, the owner of said dog shall immediately notify
the chief of police who shall order the dog held on the owner's premises or
shall have it impounded for a period of two (2) weeks. The dog shall be
examined immediately after it has bitten anyone and again at the end of the two
(2) week period. If, at the end of two (2) weeks, a veterinarian is convinced
that the dog is then free from rabies, the dog shall be released from
quarantine or from the pound, as the case may be. If the dog dies in the
meanwhile, its head shall be sent to the state department of health for
examination for rabies. (Ord. 657-05, 12-12-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
5-1A-10: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and fined not less than three hundred dollars ($300.00) nor more
than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense, plus any fees
incurred. (Ord. 662-05, 11-14-2005)
ARTICLE B. LIVESTOCK AND FOWL
SECTION:
5-1B-1: Definitions
5-1B-2: Livestock And Fowl Prohibited
5-1B-3: Nonconforming Uses
5-1B-4: Additional Restrictions
5-1B-5: Inspection, Notice
5-1B-6: Abatement Procedures
5-1B-7: Responsibility Of Property Owner
5-1B-8: Enforcement
5-1B-9: Penalties
5-1B-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
herein ascribed to them:
FOWL: Any species of chicken, turkey, pheasant, duck, geese and any other
species of bird, privately or commercially raised or produced in the village.
LIVESTOCK: Any species of horse, mule, donkey, burro, cattle, sheep, swine or
goats. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
5-1B-2: LIVESTOCK AND FOWL PROHIBITED:
Livestock and fowl shall not be raised, maintained, bred, housed, stabled,
pastured or allowed to feed, run or graze upon any property within the village.
(Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
5-1B-3: NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   Existing Nonconforming Uses: The lawful use of property, buildings and
structures existing at the time of the effective date hereof, although such use
does not conform to the provisions hereof, may be continued, but if such
nonconforming use is discontinued for a period in excess of ninety (90) days,
then use of the premises shall be in conformity with the provisions of this
article. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
   B.   Restoration Of Damaged, Nonconforming Building Or Structure: No
building or structure which has been devoted to a nonconforming use which has
been damaged by fire or other causes to the extent of twenty five percent (25%)
of its value, shall be repaired or rebuilt except in conformity with this
article. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
   C.   Conveyance Of Nonconforming Use: No right or privilege of a
nonconforming use shall pass with the conveyance of title by a nonconforming
user to grantee of said user. A nonconforming use shall cease with respect to
this article upon a conveyance by a nonconforming user to a grantee. (Ord. 487,
9-2-1980)
5-1B-4: ADDITIONAL RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Increase In Number Of Animals: It shall be unlawful to increase in
number the kind or quantity of livestock or fowl presently living within the
village as of the effective date hereof.
   B.   Animal Houses: No building or structure shall be erected,
reconstructed, enlarged or structurally altered for use as a barn, house, shed
or otherwise in which to house, feed, raise or maintain livestock or fowl
within the village.
   C.   Animal Premises: No premises shall be maintained in the village upon
which offal, manure, animal fecal matter or diseased or dead animals are
contained so as to create, cause or maintain a public nuisance, or which shall
endanger the health of the community or any of the persons within it. (Ord.
487, 9-2-1980)
   D.   Removal Of Waste: The owner of a horse must remove immediately any
waste matter left by the horse on any property within village limits.
   E.   Sidewalks: No horse shall be permitted on any sidewalk within village
limits. (Ord. 541, 7-1-1991)
5-1B-5: INSPECTION, NOTICE:
The village police, or any other village official, shall be empowered to give
notice to any person owning or in control of any property within the village,
which notice shall be given in writing by ordinary U.S. mail or in person,
requiring the said owner or person in control to permit inspection of the
premises containing any livestock or fowl within the village. The purpose of
the inspection shall be to obtain a count of the number of livestock or fowl
upon the said premises as of the date of the inspection. The notice requiring
the inspection shall be mailed or served not less than three (3) days prior to
the inspection date. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
5-1B-6: ABATEMENT PROCEDURES:
   A.   Notice To Abate: The village police, or any other village officials,
are hereby authorized and empowered to notify the person owning or in control
of any property to remove any livestock or fowl within the village in violation
of this article. Such notice shall be given personally or by certified or
registered mail, return receipt requested, to the residence or usual place of
business of such person. Proof of said notice so mailed shall be proof of
receipt thereof as provided herein.
   B.   Failure To Abate: After the expiration of ten (10) days from the
receipt of the notice provided for in subsection A of this section, if the
person so notified has failed, neglected or refused to comply with the
directions of such notice, the village police officer or village officials are
hereby authorized and empowered to pay for the removal and disposal of such
livestock or fowl, or to order the removal and disposal by the village.
   C.   Removal And Disposal Costs: In the event the village is required to
remove and dispose of the livestock or fowl, the owner or person in control of
the premises, whomsoever shall have been notified, shall be liable to the
village for the expense incurred by the village. A statement shall be rendered
to the person liable for the cost thereof and if not paid, suit shall be
instituted. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
5-1B-7: RESPONSIBILITY OF PROPERTY OWNER:
No owner of property within the village shall allow or permit lessees or users
of owner's property to violate this article. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980)
5-1B-8: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the village police to enforce this article. (Ord. 487,
9-2-1980)
5-1B-9: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates the provisions of this article or who fails, neglects
or refuses to comply with the notice provided for in subsection 5-1B-6A of this
article shall, upon conviction, be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code, and each day any such violation shall continue shall
constitute a separate offense. The penalty specified in this section shall be
in addition to the liability for expense provided for in subsection 5-1B-6C of
this article. (Ord. 487, 9-2-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
ARTICLE C. BEES
SECTION:
5-1C-1: Keeping Bees Prohibited
5-1C-2: Beehives Declared A Nuisance
5-1C-3: Penalty
5-1C-1: KEEPING BEES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to keep or harbor any bees in the village. (Ord. 445, 8-7-
1972)
5-1C-2: BEEHIVES DECLARED A NUISANCE:
Any beehive used or occupied by bees is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and
it shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any such hive in the village. (Ord.
445, 8-7-1972)
5-1C-3: PENALTY:
Whoever shall be guilty of keeping or harboring bees or keeping or maintaining
any beehive in violation of this article, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 445, 8-7-1972)
ARTICLE D. VICIOUS DOGS
SECTION:
5-1D-1: Declaration Of Purpose
5-1D-2: Legislative Intent
5-1D-3: Definitions
5-1D-4: Keeping Of Vicious Dogs Prohibited
5-1D-5: Failure To Comply
5-1D-1: DECLARATION OF PURPOSE:
The findings of the village board set forth in the preambles to ordinance 528
are incorporated herein as if fully set forth. (Ord. 528, 1-9-1989)
5-1D-2: LEGISLATIVE INTENT:
This article is adopted pursuant to the powers granted to municipalities in 65
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-1-1, 5/11-5-6 and 5/11-20-9, as amended, and
510 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/24, as amended. (Ord. 528, 1-9-1989)
5-1D-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this article the following terms and phrases shall have the
meaning set forth in this section:
BITE: To seize or cut with the teeth.
CONFINEMENT STRUCTURE: A securely locked pen, kennel or structure designed and
constructed for the keeping of a vicious dog and shall be designed, constructed
and maintained in accordance with the standards herein. Such pen, kennel or
structure must have secure sides and a secure top attached to the sides. All
structures used to confine registered vicious dogs must be locked with a key or
combination lock when such animals are within the structure. Such structures
must have a secure bottom or floor attached to the sides of the pen or the
sides of the pen must be embedded in the ground no less than two feet (2'). All
structures erected to house vicious dogs must comply with all zoning and
building regulations of the village. All such structures must be adequately
lighted, ventilated and kept in a clean and sanitary condition.
FIGHT: A prearranged conflict between two (2) or more animals but does not
include a conflict that is unorganized or accidental.
K-9 PATROL DOG OR POLICE DOG: A professionally trained dog used by law
enforcement officers for law enforcement purposes and activities.
LEASH: A cord, chain, rope, strap or other physical restraint having a tensile
strength of not less than three hundred (300) pounds.
MUZZLE: A device constructed of strong, soft material or a metal muzzle. The
muzzle must be made in a manner which will not cause injury to the dog or
interfere with its vision or respiration, but must prevent it from biting any
person or animal.
NIP: To pinch or squeeze with teeth with no breaking of skin tissue.
RUNNING AT LARGE: The failure to confine a vicious dog in accordance with the
terms of this article.
VICIOUS DOG: Any animal that has without provocation, attacked a human being or
other animal, or dog that by its behavior or physical condition constitutes an
immediate and serious physical or health threat to human beings or animals, or
any dog which has previously attacked or bitten any human being or other animal
on two (2) or more reported occasions.
VILLAGE: The village of Franklin Grove, Illinois. (Ord. 528, 1-9-1989; amd.
Ord. 730-12, 12-10-2012)
5-1D-4: KEEPING OF VICIOUS DOGS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to keep, harbor, own or in any way possess within the
corporate limits of the village any vicious dog; provided, that vicious dogs
residing in the village on the date of passage of this article may be kept
within the village subject to the standards and requirements including
licensing requirements, herein set forth.
Vicious dogs residing in the village at the time of passage of this article may
be kept by their owners within the village, subject to the following standards:
   A.   Sale Or Transfer Of Ownership Prohibited: No person shall sell, barter
or in any other way dispose of a vicious dog registered within the village
unless the recipient person resides permanently in the same household and on
the same premises as the registered owner of such vicious dog; provided, that
the registered owner of a vicious dog may sell or otherwise dispose of a
vicious dog or the offspring of such a vicious dog to persons who do not reside
within the village.
   B.   Animals Born Of Vicious Dogs: All offspring born of vicious dogs
registered within the village must be removed from the village within six (6)
weeks of the birth of such animal.
   C.   Irrebuttable Presumptions: There shall be an irrebuttable presumption
that any dog registered with the village as a vicious dog is in fact a vicious
dog subject to the requirements of this article.
   D.   Licensing Of Vicious Dogs:
      1.   No person shall possess any vicious dog for a period of more than
forty eight (48) hours without having first obtained a license therefor from
the village.
      2.   An application for a license to possess a vicious dog shall be filed
with the village clerk on a form prescribed and provided by the village clerk
and shall be accompanied by all of the following:
         a.   Verification of the identity of the owner and current address by
providing a photostatic copy of the owner's driver's license.
         b.   Proof of ownership of the vicious dog.
         c.   A copy of the current immunization and health record of the
vicious dog prepared by a veterinarian licensed to practice in the state of
Illinois.
         d.   A certificate of insurance evidencing coverage in an amount not
less than one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) providing coverage for any
injury, damage or loss caused by the vicious dog.
         e.   Two (2) photographs of the vicious dog to be licensed, taken not
less than one month before the date of the application. One photograph shall
provide a front view of the vicious dog and shall clearly show the face and
ears of the vicious dog. One photograph shall show a side view of the vicious
dog.
         f.   A license fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00).
         g.   Such other information as may be required by the village clerk.
      3.   Upon receipt of an application, the village clerk shall forward such
application to the police department which shall cause an inspection of the
premises on which the vicious dog shall be kept to determine that all
provisions of this article relating to confinement and posting of signs have
been complied with by the applicant. Upon completion of the inspection, the
police department shall notify the village clerk in writing of the results of
its inspection.
      4.   Upon receipt of the results of the police department inspection, the
village clerk shall notify the applicant of the approval or denial of the
license. In the event that the license is denied, the notification shall be
provided in writing and the reasons for such denial shall be stated. Upon
approval, the village clerk shall issue a license to the applicant.
   E.   Confinement Of Vicious Dogs: No person shall possess any vicious dog
unless the vicious dog is confined in accordance with this section.
      1.   Confinement Indoors: No vicious dog may be kept on a porch, patio or
in any part of a house or structure that would allow the vicious dog to exit
the structure on its own volition. No vicious dog shall be kept in a house or
structure when the windows are open or when screen windows or screen doors are
the only obstacle preventing the vicious dog from exiting the structure.
      2.   Confinement In An Exterior Yard: No person shall permit a vicious
dog to go outside a confinement structure, house or other structure unless the
vicious dog is securely restrained with a leash no longer than four feet (4')
in length and fitted with a muzzle. No person shall permit a vicious dog to be
kept on a leash unless a person is in physical control of the leash. No leash
restraining any vicious dog shall be attached to any inanimate object,
including, but not limited to, trees, posts, stakes and buildings.
   F.   Reporting Requirements Of Licensee: Any person holding a license
pursuant to this article shall report the incidence of any of the following
events:
      1.   The sale, barter, exchange, gift or death of any vicious dog shall
be reported within forty eight (48) hours.
      2.   The escape from confinement of any vicious dog shall be reported
upon discovery of the escape.
      3.   The biting or nipping of any person or animal by a vicious dog shall
be reported upon occurrence.
      4.   The birth of any offspring of a vicious dog shall be reported within
forty eight (48) hours of the birth of the offspring.
      5.   The permanent removal of any vicious dog from the territorial limits
of the municipality shall be reported within forty eight (48) hours of such
removal by surrender of the license of the owner to the village clerk.
Except as provided in subsection F5 of this section, the report of any incident
required to be reported under this section shall be made to the police
department of the village.
   G.   Sign Required: All persons possessing a vicious dog shall display in a
prominent place on the premises where a vicious dog is to be kept a sign which
is printed with the letters not less than four inches (4") in height using the
words "Beware Of Dog -- Vicious". A similar sign shall be posted on any
confinement structure.
   H.   Fighting Prohibited: No person shall fight or bait, conspire to fight
or bait, or keep, train or transport for the purpose of fighting or baiting,
any vicious dog.
   I.   Impoundment Of Vicious Dog: Any vicious dog which by its actions is a
"vicious dog" as defined herein shall be subject to immediate impoundment by
the police department in a humane facility for the keeping of dogs. If the
incident giving rise to the impoundment has resulted in an injury to a person,
upon impoundment by the police department, the chief of police or his designee
shall notify the rabies control administrator of the county pursuant to 510
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/12, as amended, and shall transfer control of the
vicious dog to the administrator in accordance with 510 Illinois Compiled
Statutes 5/13, as amended.
   J.   Impoundment Of Vicious Dog Running At Large: Any vicious dog found to
be running at large by any member of the police department of the municipality
shall be presumed to be in violation of this section and shall be subject to
impoundment by the police department in a humane facility for the keeping of
dogs.
   K.   Redemption Or Impounded Vicious Dog: An owner of a vicious dog holding
a license pursuant to this article may redeem an impounded vicious dog if: 1) a
vicious dog has been impounded pursuant to subsection J of this section, or 2)
a vicious dog has not caused an injury to person, subject to the following
conditions:
      1.   Proof of a valid license issued by the municipality under this
article.
      2.   Payment of the cost of keeping the vicious dog during the period of
impoundment.
An owner of a vicious dog which has caused an injury to a person resulting in
the impoundment of the vicious dog shall be entitled to redeem the vicious dog
in accordance with 510 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/13, as amended.
   L.   Revocation Of License: A license granted pursuant to this article shall
be automatically revoked upon any violation by the licensee and the license fee
shall be retained by the village.
   M.   Exceptions: This article shall not apply to any "K-9 patrol dogs" or
"police dogs" as defined herein.
   N.   Penalties: Upon conviction of a violation of this article, the court
shall assess a fine of not less than one hundred twenty five dollars ($125.00)
nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense. Each day a
violation occurs shall constitute a separate offense.
Upon a finding by the court that a licensee has violated subsection A, B, D, E,
F, G, or H of this section, the court shall enter an order revoking the license
and ordering the former holder of the license to remove the vicious dog from
the village. (Ord. 528, 1-9-1989; amd. Ord. 730-12, 12-10-2012)
5-1D-5: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
It shall be unlawful for the owner, keeper or harborer of a vicious dog
registered with the village to fail to comply with the requirements and
conditions set forth in this article. Any vicious dog found to be the subject
of a violation of this article shall be subject to immediate seizure and
impoundment. In addition, failure to comply will result in the revocation of
the license of such animal resulting in the immediate removal of the animal
from the village. (Ord. 528, 1-9-1989; amd. Ord. 730-12, 12-10-2012)
CHAPTER 2
MISCELLANEOUS OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-2-1: Illinois Criminal Code Adopted
5-2-2: Offenses Against Public Peace
5-2-3: Distribution And Use Of Tobacco; Minors
5-2-4: Curfew For Minors
5-2-5: Assembly/Loitering/Trespass; Prohibited Acts
5-2-6: Gang Activity
5-2-7: Vandalism
5-2-8: Disorderly Conduct
5-2-9: Skateboards Banned
5-2-1: ILLINOIS CRIMINAL CODE ADOPTED:
   A.   The provisions of the Illinois criminal code of 1961, as amended 1 ,
are hereby adopted in full and as subsequently amended.
   B.   Any person convicted of a violation of any section or provision of the
Illinois criminal code of 1961 as charged under this code shall be punished by
a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00) for any one offense.
   C.   Enforcement of all provisions of this section shall be by the police
department of the village. (Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
 
Notes
1 1. 720 ILCS 5/1 et seq.
5-2-2: OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person in the village to commit:
      1.   Unlawful Conduct: Disturb, tend to disturb or aid in disturbing the
peace of others by violent, tumultuous, offensive or obstreperous conduct, and
no person shall knowingly permit such conduct upon any premises owned or
possessed by him or under his control.
      2.   Assault: Assault, beat, strike, wound, imprison or inflict violence
on another where the circumstances show malice, or assault another with intent
to commit any misdemeanor or felony. Nor shall any person assault another with
a lethal weapon, instrument or thing with intent to commit upon the person of
another any bodily injury where no considerable provocation appears or where
the circumstances of the assault show malice.
      3.   Fighting: Fight another person.
      4.   Fighting Words: No person shall, in the presence or hearing of
another, curse or abuse such other person, or use any violent abusive language
to such person concerning himself, any of his relations, or his ethnic group,
or otherwise use such language under circumstances reasonably calculated to
provoke a breach of the peace. (Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
5-2-3: DISTRIBUTION AND USE OF TOBACCO; MINORS:
   A.   Illegal Distribution Of Cigarettes Or Other Tobacco Products: No
manufacturer, producer, distributor, wholesaler, or retailer of cigarettes or
other tobacco products, or any agent, employee or representative of a
manufacturer, producer, distributor, wholesaler or retailer of cigarettes or
other tobacco products shall do any of the following:
      1.   Give, sell or otherwise distribute cigarettes or other tobacco
products to any minor;
      2.   Give, sell or distribute cigarettes or other tobacco products in any
place that does not have posted in a conspicuous place a sign stating that
giving, selling or otherwise distributing cigarettes or other tobacco products
to a person under eighteen (18) years of age is prohibited by law;
      3.   Give, sell or distribute cigarettes or other tobacco products to any
person without first verifying, via a photo identification such as a driver's
license, that the person is eighteen (18) years old or older.
   B.   Vending Machines Prohibited: The sale or distribution of cigarettes or
any tobacco product via use of a vending machine is prohibited.
      1.   No person or business entity of any type shall permit, facilitate or
condone the sale or distribution of any cigarette or other tobacco product, via
a vending machine, at his or her establishment.
      2.   Exceptions:
         a.   An employer may provide cigarette or other tobacco product
vending machines for employees at the work establishment if the vending
machines are not accessible to the public, and persons under eighteen (18)
years of age are not employees of the establishment.
         b.   Licensed liquor establishments may provide tobacco products
vending machines if the machines are not accessible to minors.
   C.   Cigarette Purchase, Possession Or Smoking By Minors Prohibited: No
person under eighteen (18) years of age shall purchase, possess or consume in
any manner or form cigarettes or any tobacco product.
      1.   Possession is not an offense if the person under eighteen (18) years
of age was in possession of an unopened container or containers of the
cigarette or other tobacco product while performing their specified duties at a
lawful place of employment.
      2.   No parent, legal guardian, or caretaker shall permit, allow, condone
or facilitate a child under eighteen (18) years of age to purchase, possess or
consume in any manner of form cigarettes or any tobacco products.
   D.   Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of
this section shall be fined not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more
than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense, and a separate offense
shall be deemed committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or
continues. (Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
5-2-4: CURFEW FOR MINORS 1 :
   A.   Age And Hour Restrictions: It shall be unlawful for any person less
than eighteen (18) years of age to be present upon any public assembly,
building, place, street, or highway in the village at the following times
unless accompanied by a parent, legal guardian or other responsible companion
at least eighteen (18) years of age unless engaged in a business or occupation
which the laws of the state authorize a person less than eighteen (18) years of
age to perform:
Between 12:01 A.M. and 6:00 A.M. on Saturday;
Between 12:01 A.M. and 6:00 A.M. on Sunday; and
Between 11:00 P.M. on Sunday to Thursday, inclusive, and 6:00 A.M. on the
following day.
   B.   Standard Time: Time referred to herein is based upon the prevailing
standard of time, whether Central Standard Time or Central daylight saving
time, generally observed at that hour by the public in the village, prima facie
the time then observed in the village hall.
   C.   Detaining Child: Every member of the police force, while on duty, is
hereby authorized to detain any such minor wilfully violating the provisions of
subsection A of this section until the parent or guardian of the child shall
take him or her into custody, but such officer shall immediately upon taking
custody of such child communicate with the parent or guardian or other person
having custody of such minor.
   D.   Permitting Child To Violate Curfew: It shall be unlawful for anyone
having the legal care and custody of any person as described above to allow or
permit such person to go or be upon any public street, alley or other public
place in the village in the nighttime as restricted in subsection A of this
section, except in case of necessity. (Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 3-2-9 of this code.
5-2-5: ASSEMBLY/LOITERING/TRESPASS; PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   No person shall loiter in or around or obstruct free access to or free
use of public buildings, stores or shops, public streets or public ways in the
village, or obstruct corridors, stairways or doorways so as to prevent free
access by members of the public, officers, employees, occupants, or any other
persons;
   B.   No person shall, by his presence or in consort with others, interfere
with or interrupt the conduct of pedestrian movement, motor vehicular traffic
or business in such stores or shops or in the offices located in any such
buildings in the village.
   C.   No person shall sit, lie, stand, kneel or recline on any improvement
such as walls, retaining fixtures, sidewalks, and curbing or on any such
improvement which is not specifically provided for or intended for such purpose
or use in any public place in the village.
   D.   A person commits a violation if he singly or in consort with others
loiters or prowls in a place, at a time or in a manner not usual for law
abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant alarm for the safety of
persons or property in the vicinity. Among the circumstances which may be
considered in determining whether such alarm is warranted are:
      1.   The actor takes flight upon appearance of a peace officer;
      2.   Refuses to identify himself; or
      3.   Manifestly endeavors to conceal himself or any object.
   E.   Unless flight by the actor or other circumstances make it
impracticable, a peace officer shall, prior to any arrest for an offense under
this section, afford the actor the opportunity to dispel any alarm which would
otherwise be warranted by requesting him to identify himself and explain his
presence and conduct.
   F.   No person shall be convicted of an offense under this section if a
peace officer did not comply with the preceding sentence, or if it appears that
the explanation given by the actor was true and, if believed by the police
officer at the time, would have dispelled the alarm.
   G.   This section shall not be construed to prohibit innocent public
assembly, political, religious or civil demonstrations, gatherings or
activities, but rather to prohibit conduct calculated to do harm to the persons
or property of others and to the rights and freedom of others. (Ord. 566, 7-10-
1995)
5-2-6: GANG ACTIVITY:
   A.   Temporary Questioning Without Arrest: A police officer, after having
identified himself as a police officer, may stop any person in a public place
for a reasonable period of time when the person is wearing known gang colors,
emblems or other gang insignia, or appears to be engaged in communicating gang
related messages through the use of hand signals or other means of
communication, and the officer reasonably infers from the circumstances that
the person is committing, is about to commit or has committed any offense set
forth in the ordinances of the village. Once stopped, the officer may demand
the name and address of the person and an explanation of his actions. Such
detention and temporary questioning will be conducted in the vicinity of where
the person was stopped.
   B.   Search For Weapons: When a police officer has stopped a person for
temporary questioning pursuant to subsection A of this section and the officer
reasonably suspects that he or another officer is in danger of attack, he may
search the person for weapons. If an officer discovers a weapon, he may take it
until the completion of the questioning, at which time he shall return the
weapon, if lawfully possessed, or arrest the person so questioned.
   C.   Graffiti Prohibited:
      1.   Graffiti in public view is hereby declared to be a nuisance as set
forth in the ordinances of the village and subject to the provisions of village
ordinances regarding nuisances and the abatement thereof.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place graffiti upon the real
or personal, public or private property of another.
      3.   It shall be unlawful for the owner and/or occupant of fixed real or
personal property which is in public view to place or give permission for the
placement of any graffiti on such property without first having obtained a
properly issued sign permit.
      4.   It shall be unlawful for any person to possess, while in any public
building or public facility or while on private property, a spray paint
container, paint, ink, or marking pen which contains a nonwater soluble fluid,
brush, applicator, or any other material for marking, scratching or etching
with the intent to use such material in violation of subsection C2 and/or C3 of
this section.
      5.   It shall be unlawful for any person or known street gang associate
to display, demonstrate, communicate or "throw" street gang hand signs in any
public place within the village. A person will be considered in violation of
this section if such facts cause a reasonable person to conclude the activity
is related to street gang activity.
   D.   Penalties:
      1.   The penalty for violation of subsection C2 of this section shall be
a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00). In addition to said fine, the offender may be required by
the court to pay restitution to the property owner for the costs of restoring
the property to its state prior to the application of graffiti.
      2.   The penalty for violation of subsection C3 of this section shall be
a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00) and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day
during which a violation occurs or continues.
      3.   The penalty for violation of subsection C4 of this section shall be
a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00).
      4.   The penalty for violation of subsection C5 of this section shall be
a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00).
      5.   Any person convicted of a violation of subsection C2, C3, C4 or C5
of this section, who is found to have been a member of a gang as defined by
section
1-3-2 of this code or a candidate for membership in a gang at the time the
offense was committed and who is found to have violated said subsection in
conjunction with gang related activities, shall be subject to a fine of not
less than two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00) in addition to other penalties provided in this section.
(Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
5-2-7: VANDALISM:
   A.   All acts of vandalism are hereby declared to be unlawful.
      1.   The wilful or malicious damaging or defacing, within the corporate
limits of the village, another person's real or personal property, without the
owner's consent is hereby declared unlawful.
      2.   The wilful or malicious entry into, or the obtaining control over
any motor vehicle, bicycle or water craft of another person, without the other
person's consent is hereby declared unlawful. (Ord. 566, 7-10-1995)
5-2-8: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
It shall be unlawful to commit an act of disorderly conduct by any person in
the village. A person shall be guilty of disorderly conduct if, with the
purpose of causing public danger, alarm, disorder, nuisance, or if his conduct
is likely to cause public danger, alarm, disorder or nuisance, he commits any
of the following acts in a public place:
   A.   Commits an act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another whereby
that other is placed in danger or fear for the safety of his life or health;
   B.   Commits an act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another whereby
the property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged;
   C.   Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct so
as to endanger the life, health or property of another;
   D.   Interferes with another's lawful occupation or pursuits by acts of
violence, angry threats, or abusive conduct;
   E.   Obstructs, whether singly or together with other persons, the flow of
vehicular or pedestrian traffic and refuses to clear such public way when
ordered to do so by the police department or other lawful authority;
   F.   Resists or obstructs the performance of duties by the police department
or any other authorized village official;
   G.   Incites, attempts to incite or is involved in attempting to incite a
riot or unlawful disturbance;
   H.   Use of abusive language or threats to any member of the police
department, any other authorized village official who is engaged in the lawful
performance of his duties, or any other person when such words have a direct
tendency to cause acts of violence. Words merely causing displeasure, annoyance
or resentment are not prohibited;
   I.   Damages, befouls or disturbs public property or the property of another
so as to create a hazardous, unhealthy or physically offensive condition;
   J.   Makes or causes to be made any loud, boisterous and unreasonable noise
or disturbance to the annoyance of any other persons nearby, or near to any
public highway, road, street, lane, alley, park, square or common, whereby the
public peace is broken or disturbed, or the traveling public annoyed;
   K.   Fails to obey a lawful order to disburse by a police officer where one
or more persons are committing acts of disorderly conduct in the immediate
vicinity, and the public health and safety is threatened;
   L.   Uses abusive or obscene language or makes an obscene gesture in public;
   M.   Assembles with three (3) or more persons for the purpose of using force
or violence to disturb the public peace;
   N.   Appears in any public place and is manifestly under the influence of
alcohol, narcotics or other drug, not therapeutically administered, to the
degree that he may endanger himself or other persons or property, or alarm or
disturb other persons in his vicinity;
   O.   Transmits in any manner to any police officer, public officer or public
employee a report to the effect that an offense has been committed, knowing at
the time of such transmission that there is no reasonable ground for believing
that such an offense has been committed;
   P.   Uses paint or other medium in any way to deface, damage or destroy
property; or
   Q.   No person shall cast or throw any stone, snowball, iceball, disk shaped
object, Frisbee, stick or other projectile at, on, or into any public street,
walkway, parking area, vehicle, building or adjoining premises. (Ord. 566, 7-
10-1995)
5-2-9: SKATEBOARDS BANNED:
   A.   Definition: A "skateboard" is a single platform mounted on wheels which
is propelled solely by human power.
   B.   Prohibited: The use of skateboards is banned on village sidewalks,
streets and all village owned properties, including Atlasta park, and on any
private property which is posted "No Skateboarding".
   C.   Penalty: Violation of this section is subject to a fine of no less than
one hundred dollars ($100.00) and no more than five hundred dollars ($500.00).
(Ord. 638-03, 11-10-2003)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC DEFINITIONS AND GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Definitions
6-1-2: Traffic Signs And Signals
6-1-3: Animals And Bicycles
6-1-4: Exemptions To Traffic Laws
6-1-5: Speed Limits
6-1-6: Vehicle Weight And Load
6-1-7: Penalties
6-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
Whenever the following terms are used in this title, they shall have the
meanings respectively ascribed to them in this section:
ALLEY: A public way within a block generally giving access to the rear of lots
or buildings and not used for general traffic circulation.
BICYCLES: Every device propelled by human power upon which any person may ride,
having two (2) tandem wheels, either of which is more than twenty inches (20")
in diameter.
CROSSWALK: That portion of the roadway included within the prolongation of the
sidewalk lines at street intersections.
DRIVER: Every person who drives or is in actual physical control of a vehicle.
EMERGENCY VEHICLE: Police vehicles, vehicles of the fire protection district,
ambulances, vehicles carrying a state, county or municipal officer or employee
in response to an emergency call and emergency vehicles of public service
corporations on an emergency call.
FARM TRACTOR: Every motor vehicle designed and used primarily as a farm
implement for drawing plows, mowing machines and other implements of husbandry.
IMPROVED HIGHWAY: A roadway of concrete, brick, asphalt, macadam or gravel.
INTERSECTION: The area embraced within the prolongation of the property lines
of two (2) or more streets which join at an angle, whether or not such streets
cross.
LOADING ZONES: The space adjacent to a curb reserved for the exclusive use of
vehicles during the loading or unloading of passengers or materials.
MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle which is self-propelled and every vehicle which is
propelled by electric power obtained from overhead wires, but not operated upon
rails.
MOTORCYCLE: Every motor vehicle having a saddle for the use of the rider and
designed to travel with not more than three (3) wheels in contact with the
ground, but excluding a tractor.
PARK: To stand a vehicle, whether occupied or not, for a period of time greater
than is reasonably necessary for the actual loading or unloading of persons.
(Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-1-2: TRAFFIC SIGNS AND SIGNALS:
   A.   Conformance With State Standards: All signs and signals established by
direction of the governing body shall conform to the "Illinois State Manual Of
Uniform Traffic Control Devices For Streets And Highways".
   B.   Obedience To Traffic Signs And Signals: It shall be unlawful for the
driver of any vehicle to disobey the instructions of any traffic sign or signal
placed in view by the authority of the Village President and Board of Trustees,
or in accordance with the laws of the State, excepting on direction of a police
officer.
   C.   Injury To Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to deface,
injure, move or interfere with any official traffic sign or signal. (Ord. 503,
9-6-1983)
6-1-3: ANIMALS AND BICYCLES:
Every person riding a bicycle or an animal, or driving an animal drawing a
vehicle upon a street, shall be subject to the provisions of this title
applicable to the driver of a vehicle, except those provisions which can have
no application to one riding a bicycle or driving or riding an animal; provided
that, except in business districts, bicycles may be driven on sidewalks. (Ord.
503, 9-6-1983)
6-1-4: EXEMPTIONS TO TRAFFIC LAWS:
The provisions of this title regulating movement or parking of vehicles shall
not apply to the driver of any authorized emergency vehicle when responding to
an emergency call, but such driver when approaching shall slow down as
necessary for safety but may proceed cautiously past a red light or stop sign
or signal. At other times, drivers of authorized emergency vehicles shall stop
in obedience to a stop sign or signal. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-1-5: SPEED LIMITS:
On Illinois Route 38, the Lincoln Highway, through the Village of Franklin
Grove, a speed limit of thirty five (35) miles per hour is adopted as a prima
facie speed limit at all places on said route in the Village. (Ord. 659-05, 1-
8-2007)
6-1-6: VEHICLE WEIGHT AND LOAD 1 :
   A.   Weight And Load Limits Established: No person shall operate any vehicle
having any axle load in excess of sixteen thousand (16,000) pounds and/or
having a gross weight in excess of fifty four thousand (54,000) pounds on any
highways within the Village except when the above limits will be reduced during
the spring breakup period.
   B.   Reduction Of Weight And Load Limits:
      1.   The Village Board of Trustees may reduce the weight limitations on
highways found incapable of supporting vehicles with axle loads of sixteen
thousand (16,000) pounds.
      2.   During the season of the year when the frost is leaving the ground,
the load limit on all Village roads shall be reduced to the following gross
weights:
 
2 axles, single rear tire        7,000 pounds
2 axles, dual rear tires         16,000 pounds
3 or more axles, dual rear tires 25,000 pounds
 
   C.   Signs To Be Posted: The Village Trustee having charge of the streets,
roads and highways and in control of the Village is directed to erect and
maintain signs designating the provisions of this section at each end of that
portion of any highway affected by this section.
   D.   Enforcement: The Board of Trustees or any police officer of the Village
is hereby authorized and empowered to enforce the provisions of this section
and upon said highway being posted by signs limiting gross weights of vehicles
pursuant to this section, it shall be his duty to prosecute all violations of
this section. (Ord. 465, 3-22-1976)
   E.   Engine Braking: No person shall operate or cause to be used or
operated, within the limits of the Village, any engine braking system that
emits an excessive noise, except in the case of emergency. For purposes of this
section, "engine brake" is defined to include any mechanical exhaust device
designed to aid in the braking or deceleration of any vehicle by converting
engine power to compressed air. The Chief of Police shall provide notice of
said prohibition by posting clearly visible signs at all truck routes entering
the Village stating:
EXCESSIVE ENGINE BRAKING NOISE PROHIBITED
(Ord. 755-17, 1-9-2017)
 
Notes
1 1. See section 6-2-4 of this title.
6-1-7: PENALTIES:
Any person who is in violation of this title shall be subject to a penalty as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983; amd. 1987 Code)
CHAPTER 2
STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING
SECTION:
6-2-1: No Parking Places
6-2-2: General Parking Restrictions
6-2-3: Parking During Snow Removal
6-2-4: Parking Heavy Vehicles
6-2-5: Time Limit Parking
6-2-6: Signs To Be Posted
6-2-7: Towing Illegally Parked Vehicles
6-2-8: Vehicle Ownership Prima Facie Proof
6-2-9: Parking On Highway
6-2-1: NO PARKING PLACES:
At any time, it shall be unlawful to permit any vehicle to stand in any of the
following places, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or
in compliance with the directions of a police officer or traffic control
devices:
   A.   In any intersection.
   B.   In a crosswalk.
   C.   Upon any bridge or viaduct or in any subway or tunnel or the approach
thereto.
   D.   Between the safety zone and the adjacent curb or within thirty feet
(30') of a point of the curb immediately opposite the end of a safety zone.
   E.   Within thirty feet (30') of a traffic signal, beacon or sign on the
approaching side.
   F.   Within twenty feet (20') from the intersection or crosswalk.
   G.   At any place where the standing of a vehicle will reduce the usable
width of the roadway for moving traffic to less than eighteen feet (18').
   H.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
   I.   At any place where the vehicle would block the use of a driveway.
   J.   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of the railroad grade
crossing.
   K.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire station
and on the side of the street opposite the entrance of such station within
seventy five feet (75') of such entrance when properly signposted.
   L.   On any sidewalk or parkway.
   M.   At any place where official signs prohibit parking. (Ord. 503, 9-6-
1983)
6-2-2: GENERAL PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Loading Zones: It shall be unlawful for the driver of a vehicle to
stand a passenger vehicle for a period of time longer than is necessary for the
loading or unloading of passengers, not to exceed thirty (30) minutes, in any
place designated by the village president and board of trustees as a loading
zone and marked as such.
   B.   Alleys: No person shall park a vehicle within an alley in such manner
or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet (10') of the
width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic, and no person
shall stop, stand or park a vehicle within an alley in such a position as to
block the driveway entrance to any abutting property.
   C.   Private Property: It shall be unlawful to park any motor vehicle on any
private property without the consent of the owner of the property. (Ord. 503,
9-6-1983)
6-2-3: PARKING DURING SNOW REMOVAL:
   A.   Interference With Snow Removal:
      1.   After an accumulation of three inches (3") or more of snow has
occurred and until both sides of the street, alley or public way have been
plowed, it shall be unlawful to allow any vehicle to remain parked from the
same side of a public street, alley or public way for more than twelve (12)
hours after the opposite side of the street, alley or public way upon which the
vehicle is parked has had the snow plowed by the village. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
      2.   It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle on Elm Street between
Highway 38 and Brown Street at any time within twelve (12) hours after a
snowfall of three inches (3") or more has occurred. (Ord. 452, 3-4-1974, eff.
3-4-1974)
   B.   Towing Vehicle, Costs: Any motor vehicle parked or standing in
violation of this section may be towed or moved to another location or to a
village impoundment area by a village vehicle or private towing service. No
vehicles towed to a village impoundment area shall be released to the owner,
lienholder or other person entitled to possession unless proper proof of
entitlement to possession is first furnished to the village and all storage
charges and towing charges incurred by the village are paid to the village.
   C.   Nonliability Of Village Or Towing Service: The owner and lienholder of
vehicles parked or standing in violation of this section shall not be entitled
to any claim for damages to any motor vehicle unless wilful and wanton
misconduct shall be established. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-2-4: PARKING HEAVY VEHICLES 1 :
   A.   Weight Restrictions: No person shall park any vehicle weighing ten (10)
tons or more on a street, alley or other public roadway within the village.
   B.   Dismantled Or Separated Vehicles: Any part of a vehicle which has been
detached from another part of the vehicle when parked on a street, alley or
other public roadway within the village shall be considered over ten (10) tons
if the vehicle has a total weight of ten (10) tons or more before the vehicle
is dismantled or separated.
   C.   Removal And Impoundment Of Vehicles: The village police force is
authorized to remove or have removed any vehicle or part of a vehicle which
reasonably appears to be in violation of this section. Such vehicle shall be
impounded until lawfully claimed or disposed of in accordance with 625 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/4-201. Any claimant of a vehicle impounded under this
subsection shall pay reasonable storage and towing fees before the vehicle
shall be returned to such claimant. (Ord. 514, 8-5-1985)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 6-1-6 of this title.
6-2-5: TIME LIMIT PARKING:
It shall be unlawful for any person except the driver of an emergency vehicle
to park on Elm Street between the Chicago and Northwestern Railroad tracks and
South Street between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) P.M. and five o'clock
(5:00) A.M. for a period of time exceeding one hour. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-2-6: SIGNS TO BE POSTED:
The chief of police or any person authorized by the village president and board
of trustees shall cause signs to be posted in such areas where parking is
limited or prohibited, indicating such limitations or prohibitions. (Ord. 503,
9-6-1983)
6-2-7: TOWING ILLEGALLY PARKED VEHICLES:
The police department and all members thereof assigned to traffic duty are
hereby authorized to remove and tow away or have removed and towed away by
commercial towing service, any car or other vehicle illegally parked in any
place where such parked vehicle creates or constitutes a traffic hazard, blocks
the use of the fire hydrant or may obstruct the movement of any emergency
vehicles; or any vehicle which has been parked on any public street or other
public place for a period of twenty four (24) consecutive hours.
Cars so towed away shall be stored on any village property or in a public
garage or parking lot and shall be returned to the owner or operator thereof
after payment of the expenses incurred by the village in removing and storing
such vehicles. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-2-8: VEHICLE OWNERSHIP PRIMA FACIE PROOF:
Whenever any vehicle shall have been parked in violation of any of the
provisions of this title prohibiting or restricting parking, the person in
whose name the vehicle is registered shall be prima facie responsible for such
violation and is subject to the penalty therefor. (Ord. 503, 9-6-1983)
6-2-9: PARKING ON HIGHWAY:
   A.   Parking Permitted: Automobiles, trucks and other vehicles shall be
permitted to park on Lincoln Highway (IL Route 38) in designated parking lanes
within the corporate limits of the village. Parking shall be parallel parking
only, diagonal parking being hereby expressly prohibited. Such parallel parking
shall be so executed that the wheels of the vehicles nearest the curb shall be
not farther away from the curb than twelve inches (12"). Parking will not be
permitted within the limits of intersections as determined by the state from
intersection studies.
   B.   Penalties: Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the
provisions of this section shall be fined not less than one hundred dollars
($100.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense.
   C.   Effective Date: This section is prepared in connection with the
proposed improvement of Lincoln Highway FAP 567 (IL Route 38) known as state
section 12R-RS, and shall go into full force and effect at the time of the
completion of said improvement. (Ord. 599, 4-12-2000)
CHAPTER 3
ABANDONED, JUNKED VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-3-1: Definitions
6-3-2: Abandonment Of Vehicles
6-3-3: Junked, Disabled Vehicles
6-3-4: Notice To Abate
6-3-5: Impoundment
6-3-6: Payment Of Expenses For Impoundment
6-3-7: Penalties
6-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: A vehicle remaining at any place within the village for such
time as to cause such vehicle reasonably to appear to be abandoned, shall be
deemed abandoned.
JUNK MOTOR VEHICLE OR DISABLED MOTOR VEHICLE: Any vehicle, including trailers,
which is without currently valid license plates and in either wrecked,
discarded, dismantled, inoperative or abandoned condition.
PERSON IN CONTROL: Any of the following: owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or
otherwise, singular or plural. (Ord. 481, 12-3-1979)
6-3-2: ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES:
Abandonment of any motor vehicle by any person in the open, on streets, alleys
or on private property for a period of more than seven (7) days is hereby
declared to constitute a public nuisance. (Ord. 534, 10-2-1989)
6-3-3: JUNKED, DISABLED VEHICLES:
   A.   Parking And Storing Prohibited: Junked or disabled motor vehicles may
not be parked, stored or left in the open on private property unless it is
necessary for the operation of a business enterprise lawfully conducted
thereon.
   B.   Motor Vehicle Parts: Storing, placing or allowing to remain in the
open, on streets, alleys or private property of motor vehicle bodies, parts,
equipment, motors and materials for a period of more than forty eight (48)
hours in any one calendar month is hereby prohibited unless necessary for the
operation of a business enterprise lawfully conducted thereon.
   C.   Nuisance Declared: Parking or storing of junked or disabled motor
vehicles and the storing or allowing same to remain in the open, of motor
vehicle bodies, parts, equipment, motors and materials in violation of
subsections A and B of this section is hereby declared to constitute a public
nuisance. (Ord. 481, 12-3-1979)
6-3-4: NOTICE TO ABATE:
   A.   The village officials are hereby authorized and empowered to notify the
person in control of any private property to relocate any junked or disabled
vehicles parked or stored in violation of subsection 6-3-3A of this chapter to
a completely enclosed location on the property or otherwise to remove the same
from the premises.
   B.   The village officials are also hereby authorized and empowered to
notify the person in control of any private property to relocate any motor
vehicle bodies, parts, equipment, motors and materials stored, placed or
allowed to remain in the open in violation of subsection 6-3-3B of this chapter
to a completely enclosed location on the property or otherwise to remove the
same from the premises.
   C.   The village officials are further hereby authorized and empowered to
notify the person in control of any private property to relocate any abandoned
motor vehicle in violation of section
6-3-2 of this chapter to a completely enclosed location on the property or
otherwise to remove the same from the premises.
Such notice shall be given by personal service or certified or registered mail,
return receipt requested, to the residence or usual place of business of such
person. Proof of said notice so mailed shall be proof of receipt thereof as
provided in section
6-3-5 of this chapter. (Ord. 481, 12-3-1979)
6-3-5: IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   After the expiration of ten (10) days from the receipt of the notice
provided for in section
6-3-4 of this chapter, if the person so notified has failed, neglected or
refused to comply with the directions of such notice, the village officials are
hereby authorized and empowered to pay for the removal and disposal of such
vehicles, bodies, parts and the like, or to order the removal and disposal by
the village.
   B.   The village officials are empowered, without further notice, to remove
and impound or cause to be impounded any abandoned motor vehicle, the person in
control of which cannot, in the exercise of due diligence, be determined or
found. Such vehicle as provided in this subsection shall be impounded until
lawfully claimed or disposed of in accordance with Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/4-201. Any claimant of a vehicle impounded under this subsection shall pay
reasonable storage and towing fees before the vehicle shall be returned to such
claimant. (Ord. 481, 12-3-1979)
6-3-6: PAYMENT OF EXPENSES FOR IMPOUNDMENT:
In the event the village is required to remove and dispose of the vehicles,
bodies, parts and the like, the person in control of the premises as heretofore
defined, shall be liable to the village for the expense incurred by the
village. A statement shall be rendered to the person liable for the cost
thereof and if not paid, suit shall be instituted therefor. (Ord. 481, 12-3-
1979)
6-3-7: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates the provisions of section
6-3-2 or
6-3-3 of this chapter, or who fails, neglects or refuses to comply with the
notice provided for in section
6-3-4 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than three
hundred dollars ($300.00) and not more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00). The penalty specified in this section shall be in addition to the
liability for expenses provided for in section
6-3-6 of this chapter. (Ord. 662-05, 11-14-2005)
CHAPTER 4
SNOWMOBILES
SECTION:
6-4-1: Operation Of Snowmobiles
6-4-2: Speed
6-4-3: Hours Of Operation
6-4-4: Unattended Vehicles
6-4-5: Traffic Regulations
6-4-6: Penalties
6-4-1: OPERATION OF SNOWMOBILES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a snowmobile within the village
of Franklin Grove, except on the following designated streets:
   A.   State Street from the village limit on the south to Lahman Street;
   B.   Brown Street in its entirety;
   C.   Lahman Street from State Street to Spring Street;
   D.   Spring Street from Lahman Street to the southerly right of way of the
Chicago and Northwestern Railroad;
   E.   Elm Street, only to cross the Chicago and Northwestern Railroad double
tracks;
   F.   North/south alley, between N. Elm Street and N. Walnut Street, to North
Street.
   G.   North Street from alley in subsection F of this section to north/south
alley between N. Walnut Street and N. Sycamore Street;
   H.   North/south alley between N. Walnut and N. Sycamore to Illinois Route
38 across from Casey's;
   I.   Hughes Street from S. Walnut to the village limit to the east. (Ord.
617-02, 1-14-2002)
6-4-2: SPEED:
It shall be unlawful to operate a snowmobile within the village of Franklin
Grove at a speed in excess of fifteen (15) miles per hour. (Ord. 617-02, 1-14-
2002)
6-4-3: HOURS OF OPERATION:
It shall be unlawful to operate a snowmobile in the village of Franklin Grove
except as follows:
   A.   Between the hours of eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and eleven thirty
o'clock (11:30) P.M. on Sunday through Thursday;
   B.   Between the hours of eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. Friday and one o'clock
(1:00) A.M. Saturday;
   C.   Between the hours of eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. Saturday and one o'clock
(1:00) A.M. Sunday. (Ord. 617-02, 1-14-2002)
6-4-4: UNATTENDED VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful for the owner or operator of a snowmobile to leave or
allow a snowmobile to be or remain unattended on any public property while the
motor is running or with the keys for starting the vehicle left in the ignition
switch. (Ord. 617-02, 1-14-2002)
6-4-5: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS:
Each operator of a snowmobile shall strictly observe all traffic signs, signals
and all other rules and regulations applicable to motor vehicles and, in
addition thereto, shall yield the right of way to all other traffic at
intersections. (Ord. 617-02, 1-14-2002)
6-4-6: PENALTIES:
Every person convicted for a violation of any provision of this chapter shall
be punished by a fine of not less than seventy five dollars ($75.00) and not
more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense. (Ord. 617-02, 1-14-
2002)
CHAPTER 5
ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLES (ATVs)
SECTION:
6-5-1: Prohibited
6-5-1: PROHIBITED:
It shall be illegal to operate, drive, or cause to be driven any all-terrain
vehicles (ATVs) on the streets, public rights of way, or any public parks or
properties within the village limits. Operation of all-terrain vehicles by
emergency services personnel while engaged in response to an emergency does not
constitute a violation of this section. (Ord. 682-07, 6-11-2007, eff. 7-1-2007)
CHAPTER 6
GOLF CARTS
SECTION:
6-6-1: Prohibited
6-6-2: Definition
6-6-3: Requirements
6-6-4: Permits
6-6-5: Violation
6-6-1: PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a golf cart on the roadways
within the village of Franklin Grove, except as provided in this chapter. (Ord.
700-09, 11-9-2009, eff. 1-1-2010)
6-6-2: DEFINITION:
A "golf cart" is a nonhighway vehicle as defined in the Illinois vehicle code.
(Ord. 700-09, 11-9-2009, eff. 1-1-2010)
6-6-3: REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   No golf cart shall be operated on a village roadway unless at a minimum
it conforms to all the requirements of the Illinois vehicle code and has in
good operational order the following:
      1.   Brakes;
      2.   Steering apparatus;
      3.   Tires;
      4.   Rearview mirror;
      5.   Red reflectorized warning devices in the front and rear;
      6.   A slow moving emblem on the rear of the golf cart which emblem shall
conform to the Illinois vehicle code;
      7.   A headlight that emits a white light visible from a distance of five
hundred feet (500') to the front;
      8.   A taillight that emits a red light visible from at least one hundred
feet (100') from the rear;
      9.   Brake lights and turn signals; and
      10.   Seat belts.
   B.   No person shall operate a golf cart unless such person conforms to all
requirements of the Illinois vehicle code and conforms to the following:
      1.   Has proof on his or her person of current liability insurance;
      2.   Has a current valid driver's license;
      3.   Has a permit issued by the village of Franklin Grove.
   C.   No person shall operate a golf cart in violation of the following:
      1.   A golf cart may not be operated in excess of the posted speed limit
and in no event may it be operated in excess of twenty five (25) miles per
hour.
      2.   No person shall operate a golf cart in violation of any of the laws
of the state of Illinois, or of any ordinance of this village. (Ord. 700-09,
11-9-2009, eff. 1-1-2010)
6-6-4: PERMITS:
   A.   No person shall operate a qualified golf cart without first obtaining a
permit from the village clerk as provided herein. Permits shall be granted
annually from the date designated on the permit. The village clerk may issue
such a permit for any date approved of and designated by the village board of
trustees. The cost of the permit is twenty dollars ($20.00). A temporary permit
for up to three (3) days may be issued at a cost of ten dollars ($10.00), good
for the days designated.
   B.   Every application for a permit shall be made on a form supplied by the
village clerk or a designee and shall contain the following information:
      1.   Name and address of applicant;
      2.   Name of liability insurance carrier;
      3.   The serial number, make, model and description of golf cart;
      4.   Signed waiver of liability by applicant releasing the village and
agreeing to indemnify and hold the village harmless from any and all future
claims resulting from the operation of their golf carts on village streets; and
      5.   Photocopy of applicable liability insurance coverage card
specifically for the vehicle to be operated pursuant to the permit.
   C.   The village clerk may suspend or revoke a permit granted hereunder upon
a finding that the holder thereof has violated any provision of this chapter or
there is evidence that permittee cannot safely operate a qualified golf cart on
the designated roadways.
   D.   The village clerk shall be authorized to issue a permit on only such
days as may be approved by the village board of trustees. (Ord. 700-09, 11-9-
2009, eff. 1-1-2010)
6-6-5: VIOLATION:
Any failure of an individual to abide by this chapter or otherwise secure a
permit provided herein when operating a golf cart upon the roadways of the
village shall subject the violator to a fine of one hundred fifty dollars
($150.00) if paid to the village clerk within ten (10) days of the issuance of
a citation. If the fine of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) is not paid
within ten (10) days, charges may be filed for an ordinance violation and a
penalty imposed of no less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) and a
maximum of five hundred dollars ($500.00) per violation. (Ord. 700-09, 11-9-
2009, eff. 1-1-2010)
CHAPTER 7
NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-7-1: Operation Of Non-Highway Vehicles
6-7-2: Definitions
6-7-3: Regulation Of Non-Highway Vehicles
6-7-4: Insurance Requirements
6-7-5: Seatbelts Required
6-7-6: Permit Required
6-7-7: Violations
6-7-8: Prohibition Of Recreational Off-Highway Vehicles
6-7-1: OPERATION OF NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLES:
The use of specified non-highway vehicles on the streets, roadways and alleys
of the Village shall be permissible subject to the provisions of this chapter.
Non-highway vehicles may not be used on any toll road, interstate highway,
controlled access highway or other highway or road under the jurisdiction of
the State, except permitted crossing as hereafter set forth in this chapter.
(Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms and phrases shall have the
meanings set forth in this section:
NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLE: Any recreational off-highway vehicle not specifically
designed to be used on a public highway. For purposes of this chapter, non-
highway vehicles shall not include all-terrain vehicles, off-highway vehicles
and all as defined in the Illinois Vehicle Code.
RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY VEHICLE: Any motorized off-highway device designed to
travel primarily off-highway, sixty four inches (64") or less in width, having
a manufacturer's dry weight of two thousand (2,000) pounds or less, traveling
on four (4) or more non-highway tires, designed with a non-straddle seat and a
steering wheel for steering control, except equipment such as lawnmowers. (Ord.
753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-3: REGULATION OF NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLES:
   A.   All non-highway vehicles shall be operated only on streets where the
posted speed limit is thirty five (35) miles per hour or less. The foregoing
provision shall not prohibit a non-highway vehicle from crossing a road or
street at an intersection where the road or street has a posted speed limit of
more than thirty five (35) miles per hour.
   B.   A person may not operate a non-highway vehicle upon any street, highway
or roadway unless he or she: 1) is eighteen (18) years of age or older; and 2)
has a valid driver's license issued in his or her name by the Illinois
Secretary of State or such other applicable foreign jurisdiction.
   C.   No person operating a non-highway vehicle shall make a direct crossing
upon or across any toll road, interstate highway, or controlled access highway.
A person may make a direct crossing of any other highway under the jurisdiction
of the State at an intersection of the highway with another public street,
road, or highway.
   D.   No non-highway vehicle may be operated on a roadway unless, at a
minimum, it has the following: brakes, a steering apparatus, tires, a rearview
mirror, red reflectorized warning devices in the front and rear, a slow moving
emblem, as required of other vehicles in section 12-709 of the Illinois Vehicle
Code, on the rear of the non-highway vehicle, a headlight that emits a white
light visible from a distance of five hundred feet (500') to the front, a tail
lamp that emits a red light visible from at least one hundred feet (100') from
the rear, brake lights, and turn signals. When operated on a roadway, a non-
highway vehicle shall have its headlight and tail lamps lighted as required by
section 12-201 of the Illinois Vehicle Code.
   E.   A person who drives or is in actual physical control of a non- highway
vehicle on a roadway while under the influence is subject to sections 11-500
through 11-502 of the Illinois Vehicle Code and all other applicable laws.
   F.   The operation of a non-highway vehicle upon any street, roadway or
alley is subject to the provisions of chapter 11 of the Illinois Vehicle Code
concerning the Rules of the Road and all applicable Village ordinances, as the
same may be amended from time to time.
   G.   No non-highway vehicle shall be operated on any Village sidewalks or
