other surfaces other than Village streets as otherwise allowed therein. (Ord.
753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-4: INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS:
Any person who operates a non-highway vehicle on a street, highway, or roadway
of the Village shall be subject to the mandatory insurance requirements under
article VI of chapter 7 of the Illinois Vehicle Code. (Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-5: SEATBELTS REQUIRED:
During the operation of a non-highway vehicle, the operator and all passengers
shall wear a seatbelt. (Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-6: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   No person shall operate a non-highway vehicle on the Village's streets,
roadway or alleys without first obtaining an annual permit from the Village as
provided herein. A permit shall be valid, unless suspended or revoked, for a
period of one (1) year. The annual cost of the permit shall be twenty dollars
($20.00). If a person has a valid permit for the non-highway vehicle from the
Dixon Park District for OHV use on the Stengel Trail, there shall be no cost.
Every non-highway vehicle shall be required to have a permit.
   B.   Every application for a permit shall be made on a form supplied by the
Village and shall contain the following information:
      1.   Name and address of applicant;
      2.   Name of insurance carrier and policy number and/or a photocopy of
applicable liability insurance coverage card issued specifically for the non-
highway vehicle to be operated pursuant to the permit;
      3.   The serial number, make, and model and description of the non-
highway vehicle;
      4.   A certification from the applicant that the non-highway vehicle
satisfies the requirements of this chapter and the Illinois Vehicle Code; and
      5.   Such other information as the Village may require, including a
release and waiver of liability signed by applicant releasing the Village and
its employees, and agreeing to indemnify and hold the Village harmless,
including the costs of defense, from any and all claims, penalties, costs,
judgments, settlements or causes of action resulting or arising from the
operation of applicant's non-highway vehicle on Village streets.
   C.   Each person operating a non-highway vehicle shall carry the permit
issued by the Village at all times during the operation of said vehicle.
      1.   A permit number will be assigned by the Village. It is the
applicant's responsibility to mark their non-highway vehicle with a three inch
(3") assigned permit number. The permit number must be securely mounted and
unobstructed and visible from the rear. (Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-7: VIOLATIONS:
   A.   The Village may suspend or revoke a permit granted hereunder upon a
finding that the operator of such non-highway vehicle has violated any
provision of this chapter or there is a finding that the applicant or operator
thereof cannot safely operate a non- highway vehicle on Village streets.
   B.   Additionally, a violation of any provision of this chapter shall be
punishable by payment of a fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00)
and not more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) plus the Village's
enforcement costs incurred, including its attorney fees, for each offense. Any
second or subsequent offense shall result in the revocation of the Village
permit for a period of no less than one (1) nor more than three (3) years. To
the extent that any violation of this chapter may also constitute a violation
of a criminal statute of the State of Illinois, the violator shall also be
subject to criminal prosecution and all other penalties as permitted by law.
(Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
6-7-8: PROHIBITION OF RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY VEHICLES:
   A.   The use of recreational off-highway vehicles is not authorized by this
chapter. (Ord. 753-17, 2-13-2017)
TITLE 7
Public Ways And Property
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Supervision
7-1-2: Excavations And Trimming Trees
7-1-2-1: Permit Requirements
7-1-2-2: Barricades And Lights
7-1-2-3: Backfilling Excavations
7-1-2-4: Penalties
7-1-3: Encroachments
7-1-1: SUPERVISION:
All public streets, alleys, sidewalks and other public ways shall be under the
supervision of the street and alley committee. It shall have supervision over
all work thereon, and the cleaning thereof, and shall be charged with the
enforcement of all ordinance provisions relating to such public places (except
traffic ordinances) and is hereby authorized to enforce such ordinances. (Ord.
397B, 11-2-1959)
7-1-2: EXCAVATIONS AND TRIMMING TREES:
7-1-2-1: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permits Required:
      1.   Excavations: It shall be unlawful to make or cause to be made any
excavation in or across or to tunnel under the curb, gutter or roadway of any
street or sidewalk or any village property within the corporate limits of the
village without having first secured a permit therefor from the village clerk.
      2.   Tree Trimming: It shall be unlawful to trim trees, parts of which
may fall on village sidewalks, streets or other village property without first
having secured a permit therefor from the village clerk. (Ord. 397B, 11-2-1959)
   B.   Approval Required: No permit shall be issued except on approval of a
member of the committee of streets and alleys or on order of the president of
the board of trustees or the chief of police.
   C.   Bond And Insurance: Each application shall be accompanied by a cash
bond or a bond with a corporate surety or such surety as shall be approved by a
member of the committee or the village president or the chief of police. The
bond shall be in such amount, not less than ten dollars ($10.00) nor more than
one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), as may be determined and approved by the
member of the committee or the village president or the chief of police, and
shall be conditioned to indemnify the village for any liability, loss or damage
resulting from the work undertaken or the manner of doing the same and for the
restoration of the street, alley, sidewalk, curb or gutter or other village
property as hereinafter provided. In addition, each such applicant shall
furnish evidence acceptable to the member of the committee or the village
president or the chief of police of satisfactory public liability insurance in
limits of at least twenty five thousand dollars ($25,000.00) for injuries to
each person, fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) for injuries in each accident
and five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) for damage to property in each accident,
covering all damages occasioned by or in any manner resulting from such work.
(Ord. 397B, 11-2-1959; amd. 1987 Code)
7-1-2-2: BARRICADES AND LIGHTS:
Before and during construction and excavation and tree trimming, the applicant
shall at all times maintain proper barricades and lights. It shall be unlawful
to disturb or interfere with any such barricades or lights. (Ord. 397B, 11-2-
1959)
7-1-2-3: BACKFILLING EXCAVATIONS:
All excavations shall be promptly backfilled by applicant, and the surface
restored to the exact type of surface and thickness as prior to excavation.
Where the excavation is within the surface area of any street or sidewalk, it
shall be backfilled in the following manner: the trench or excavated area must
be filled by using sand or stone screenings in layers not to exceed six inches
(6") in depth, and each layer shall be thoroughly compacted by wetting with
water and tamping by the use of ramming tools or hand tampers. (Ord. 397B, 11-
2-1959)
7-1-2-4: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any provision of this section
7-1-2 shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 397B, 11-2-1959)
7-1-3: ENCROACHMENTS:
   A.   Definitions:
ENCROACHMENT: Any building, fence, sign, or any other structure or object of
any kind (with the exception of utilities and public road signs), which is
placed, located or maintained in, on, or over any portion of the roadway right
of way.
ROADWAY RIGHT OF WAY: Those areas existing or acquired by dedication or by fee
simple for highway purposes; also, the areas acquired by temporary easement
during the time the easement is in effect.
   B.   Encroachments Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to erect or cause to be erected, to retain or cause to be retained,
an "encroachment" (hereinabove defined), within the limits of the roadway right
of way.
   C.   Limitation Of Application: This section is intended to and shall be in
addition to all other ordinances, rules and regulations concerning
encroachments and shall not be construed as repealing or rescinding any other
ordinance or part of any ordinance unless in direct conflict therewith.
   D.   Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall
be fined not less than seventy five dollars ($75.00) nor more than one hundred
fifty dollars ($150.00) for each offense, and a separate offense shall be
deemed committed for each and every day during which a violation continues or
exists. (Ord. 601, 4-12-2000)
ARTICLE A. STREET AND SIDEWALK GRADES
SECTION:
7-1A-1: Base Line
7-1A-2: Grade Points, Establishing Street Grades
7-1A-3: Grades Of Certain Streets And Sidewalks Enumerated
7-1A-1: BASE LINE:
For the purpose of establishing grades in the streets and avenues in the
village, the following line is hereby adopted and shall be taken as the base
line: an imaginary, horizontal line fifty feet (50') below the water table on
the northwest corner of the Presbyterian church to the southeast corner of the
intersection of Walnut Street and South Street in the village. (Ord. 157, 8-5-
1901)
7-1A-2: GRADE POINTS, ESTABLISHING STREET GRADES:
Whenever a point is given by numbers as a grade point, it shall mean such
number of feet and one-hundredths of a foot above the base line established in
and by section
7-1A-1 of this article. The grade of the center of the streets and avenues and
of the outer edge of the respective sidewalks shall be a straight line between
such grade points. (Ord. 157, 8-5-1901)
7-1A-3: GRADES OF CERTAIN STREETS AND SIDEWALKS ENUMERATED:
   A.   Elm Street: The grade of Elm Street at the centerline of said street,
from the south boundary line of block 30, in Lahman's addition, to the south
boundary line of the C. & N.W. railroad grounds, shall be as follows:
      At the intersection with the westerly extension of the south boundary
line of block 30 in Lahman's addition   43.50
      At the intersection with the south line of Lahman Street   45.60
      At the intersection with the north line of Lahman Street   45.70
      At the intersection with the south line of South Street   47.20
      At the intersection with the north line of South Street   47.20
      At a point 340 feet north of the north line of South Street   47.20
      At the intersection with the south boundary line of the C. & N.W.
railroad grounds   45.90
   B.   South Street: The grade of South Street at the centerline of said
street, from the east line of Elm Street to the west line of Walnut Street
shall be as follows:
      At the intersection with the east line of Elm Street   47.20
      At the intersection with the west line of Walnut Street   47.20
   C.   Sidewalks On Elm Street:
      1.   The grade for the outer (easterly) edge of the sidewalk on the west
side of Elm Street, from the north line of South Street to the south boundary
line of the C. & N.W. railroad grounds shall be as follows:
         At the intersection with the north line of South Street   47.10
         At a point 50 feet north of the north line of South Street   48.60
         At a point 250 feet north of the north line of South Street   48.60
         At a point 345 feet north of the north line of South Street   47.70
         At the intersection with the south boundary line of the C. & N.W.
railroad grounds   45.80
      2.   The grade for the outer (westerly) edge of the sidewalk on the east
side of Elm Street from the north line of South Street to the south boundary
line of the C. & N.W. railroad grounds shall be as follows:
         At the intersection with the north line of South Street   47.20
         At the intersection with the south line of the alley in block
10   48.10
         At the intersection with the north line of the alley in block
10   48.40
         At the intersection with the south line of Whitney Street   48.10
         At the intersection with the north line of Whitney Street   47.20
         At a point 340 feet north of the north line of South Street   47.00
         At the intersection with the south boundary line of the C. & N.W.
railroad grounds   45.90
   D.   Other Sidewalk Grades: The grade for the outer edge of sidewalks on all
the beforenamed streets, with exception of those for which special sidewalk
grades are established in subsection C of this section, shall be governed by
and correspond with the grades established for the center of streets in front
of said walks. All walks shall be laid with a pitch of one-fourth inch (1/4")
to the foot, sloping from the property line to the outer edge of the walk.
(Ord. 157, 8-5-1901)
ARTICLE B. SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION
SECTION:
7-1B-1: Special Sidewalk Construction Ordinance
7-1B-2: Supervision Of Construction
7-1B-3: Construction Specifications
7-1B-4: Contract For Construction
7-1B-5: Bills For Construction Costs; Special Taxes
7-1B-6: Voluntary Sidewalk Construction Assistance
7-1B-1: SPECIAL SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION ORDINANCE:
Whenever the village president and board of trustees shall provide by ordinance
for the construction of any sidewalk in the village, said ordinance shall
define the location of each sidewalk and prescribe its width and that the cost
thereof, unless otherwise provided in said ordinance, shall be paid by special
taxation of the lot or parcel of land touching upon the line of the sidewalk or
sidewalks in proportion to its respective frontage on said sidewalk. (Ord. 185,
8-6-1906)
7-1B-2: SUPERVISION OF CONSTRUCTION:
The materials for and the construction of all sidewalks shall be under the
supervision and subject to the approval of the committee on streets and alleys.
(Ord. 185, 8-6-1906)
7-1B-3: CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Preparatory to the construction of sidewalks, the surface shall be
brought to a subgrade at a depth of ten inches (10") below the surface of the
sidewalk when finished; upon said subgrade shall be laid a foundation six
inches (6") thick of cinders or sand which shall be flooded and thoroughly
rolled or tamped in such manner as to procure a compact and solid foundation
with a firm and even surface; upon this a concrete foundation three and one-
fourth inches (31/4") thick, after being compressed, shall be laid.
   B.   The concrete shall be composed of one part best Portland cement, two
(2) parts clean, sharp sand, and five (5) parts broken stone or gravel, all by
bulk. The concrete shall be thoroughly mixed and immediately spread in the
walk, compacted by ramming, and divided into blocks to conform to finished
surface and shall be covered with a coat of best Portland cement sufficient to
ensure a perfect union with the wearing surface.
   C.   Upon the concrete base thus prepared there shall be spread immediately
a finish coat three-fourths inch (3/4") thick composed of one part of the best
Portland cement and one part of clean, sharp sand, both by bulk, which shall be
spread, floated and trowelled to a smooth surface and cut into blocks four feet
(4') square before it has begun to set. (Ord. 185, 8-6-1906)
7-1B-4: CONTRACT FOR CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Authority To Issue Contract, Costs: In case of default of the owner or
owners of any lot or parcel of land to construct a sidewalk as required by the
provisions of this article and the special ordinance, the village shall enter
into a contract for the furnishing of said materials and the construction of
said sidewalk, and the cost thereof shall be paid and collected by special
taxation of the lot or parcel of land touching upon the line of the sidewalk in
the manner provided for in the act of the general assembly of the state of
Illinois entitled "an act to provide additional means for the construction of
sidewalks" in force July 1, 1875, as amended 1 .
   B.   Bidding Procedures:
      1.   Contracts Over Five Hundred Dollars: All contracts for the
construction of sidewalks as hereinbefore provided, when the expense thereof
shall exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) shall be let to the lowest
responsible bidder in the following manner:
         a.   Notice For Bids: Notice shall be given by the committee on
streets and alleys of the village by advertisement in some newspaper of general
circulation in the village that bids will be received for the construction of
said sidewalk in accordance with the ordinance therefor. Such notice shall
state the time of opening said bids, not more than ten (10) days and not less
than five (5) days thereafter.
         b.   Guarantee Of Performance: All proposals or bids shall be
accompanied by cash or a check payable to the order of the committee and
certified by a responsible bank for the amount, which shall not be less than
ten percent (10%) of the aggregate of the proposal.
         c.   Contract Approvals: All contracts shall be approved by the
chairman of the street and alley committee.
      2.   Contracts Of Five Hundred Dollars Or Less: All contracts for the
construction of sidewalks when the expense thereof shall be five hundred
dollars ($500.00) or less shall be let to the lowest responsible bidder in the
following manner: notice shall be given by the committee on streets and alleys
by posting four (4) notices in the vicinity of the proposed sidewalk. Such
notice shall state that bids will be received for the construction of said
sidewalk and the time of opening said bids, not more than ten (10) nor less
than five (5) days thereafter. (Ord. 185, 8-6-1906)
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/11-84-1 et seq.
7-1B-5: BILLS FOR CONSTRUCTION COSTS; SPECIAL TAXES:
   A.   Bills Filed; Special Taxes Assessed: Within thirty (30) days after the
construction of the sidewalk or sidewalks provided for by the special ordinance
in pursuance of the contract made as aforesaid, a bill of the cost of such
sidewalk showing in separate items the cost of construction and supervision
thereof, a list of the lots or parcels of land touching upon the line of said
sidewalk or sidewalks, the names of the parties who paid the last general taxes
on the respective lots and parcels and the frontage of each lot and parcel of
land, shall be prepared by the street and alley committee of the village and
filed in its office, and thereupon, if the owner of any lot, block, tract or
parcel of land has failed, neglected or refused to construct said sidewalk or
sidewalks in accordance with the provisions of this article and the special
ordinance, the street and alley committee shall prepare a special tax list
against said lots, blocks, tracts and parcels of land in front of or touching
upon which the sidewalk has not been constructed, ascertaining by computation
the amount of special tax to be charged against each of said lots, blocks,
tracts and parcels of land on account of the construction of the sidewalk
according to the frontage thereof, which tax list shall be filed in the office
of the street and alley committee within thirty (30) days after the filing of
the bill of the cost. The street and alley committee shall thereupon issue
warrants directed to the village treasurer for the collection of the amounts of
special tax so ascertained and appearing from said tax list to be due from the
respective lots, blocks and parcels of land touching upon the line of the
sidewalk, and the treasurer shall proceed to collect the warrants in the manner
provided by law.
   B.   Authority To Collect Special Tax: The village treasurer is hereby
designated and authorized to make collection of this special tax so levied as
aforesaid.
   C.   Unpaid Special Taxes, Report To County: Upon the failure to collect
such special tax, the village treasurer shall, on or before April 1 of each
year, make out a report of all unpaid special taxes in writing to the county
collector of Lee County and of all lots or parcels of land upon which such
special tax shall be unpaid, with the names of the respective owners thereof,
so far as the same are known to the treasurer, together with the amount due and
unpaid upon each tract and a copy of this article and of the special ordinance
ordering the construction of the sidewalks, which said report shall be
accompanied by the oath of the officer that the list is a correct return of the
lots and parcels of land on which the special tax remains due and unpaid and
that the amounts therein stated, nor any part thereof, have not been collected.
(Ord. 185, 8-6-1906)
7-1B-6: VOLUNTARY SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION ASSISTANCE:
   A.   Sidewalk assistance construction funds are provided upon the condition
of their availability. The village board is under no obligation to provide
assistance beyond specified allocations, and may discontinue the assistance
program at any time, being obligated only to fund previously approved
applications. Applications for assistance must be presented in writing prior to
construction.
   B.   Qualifying sidewalks must be public walkways lying along village
streets. (Sidewalks from buildings or structures to or away from the public
walkways do not qualify for village assistance.) Basic sidewalk assistance
incentive is established at one dollar ($1.00) per square foot (August 1,
1994). Projects requiring five hundred dollars ($500.00) or more assistance
must be submitted to the village board for prior approval. No more than one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) may be approved per site (separate property tax
parcel) per calendar year. The village streets and alleys supervisor shall
inspect all projects when application for assistance is made and after
construction to insure uniformity and compliance prior to release of assistance
funds.
   C.   Sidewalks constructed along public ways within the village must meet
the following minimum standards established by the village board to be eligible
for assistance funding:
      1.   Concrete shall be of a six (6) bag per cubic yard quality.
      2.   Minimum concrete shall be four (4) mean inches thick expanded to six
(6) mean inches in areas crossed by vehicular traffic.
      3.   Minimum width shall be forty eight inches (48"), expanded to sixty
inches (60") in areas requiring handicap accessibility.
      4.   All new sidewalks must meet old sidewalks at grade level.
      5.   Sidewalk surfaces must be within one inch (1") of level of
surrounding area.
      6.   Sidewalk surface must have a downward slope to the outside (toward
street) of one-fourth inch (1/4") per foot width.
      7.   Break joints shall be placed each four (4) running feet and
expansion joints as needed. (Ord. 560, 7-11-1994)
ARTICLE C. OBSTRUCTIONS
SECTION:
7-1C-1: Declared
7-1C-2: Impediments
7-1C-3: Permit Required
7-1C-4: Violation And Penalty
7-1C-5: Abatement
7-1C-1: DECLARED:
It shall be unlawful for an owner, occupant, lessee, or agent in possession or
control of property to place, park, or otherwise allow any obstruction of any
kind that results in impeding the free flow of traffic on public roadways
within the village, without a permit from the village authorities. Such
impediments include, but are not limited to, inoperable motor vehicles,
unattached trailers, and trash receptacles and/or dumpsters. (Ord. 672-06, 1-8-
2007)
7-1C-2: IMPEDIMENTS:
   A.   Garbage Receptacles And/Or Dumpsters: A garbage receptacle and/or
dumpster may be placed at the edge of a public roadway if it is being utilized
to dispose of garbage due to construction, remodeling, or demolition, and if:
      1.   There is insufficient space on the property that is being served by
the use of the unit;
      2.   A permit has been issued by the village zoning officer to the
property owner or occupant of the property that is being served by the unit;
      3.   It is placed at least one hundred feet (100') from any intersection;
      4.   It is placed immediately adjacent to the boundary of the property
that is being served by the unit;
      5.   It is not placed on any portion of another property owner's land,
unless that property owner has given written permission to the property owner
or occupant seeking the placement of the unit;
      6.   It is located so as not to impair or obstruct the sightline of
traffic;
      7.   It does not reduce the width of the public roadway for travel to
less than twenty four feet (24');
      8.   Appropriate safety markings, symbols, or signs are applied to the
unit at its corners located closest to public roadways; and
      9.   All garbage is placed fully within the walls of the unit and it does
not release noxious or offensive odors. (Ord. 672-06, 1-8-2007)
7-1C-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   A permit may be issued by the village zoning officer to an owner,
occupant, lessee, or agent in possession or control of property.
   B.   A permit may be issued for no more than twenty one (21) consecutive
days.
   C.   A permit may, but is not required to, be renewed by the village zoning
officer.
   D.   The cost of a permit shall be fifty dollars ($50.00), and there shall
be no charge for renewal of a permit.
   E.   An application for a permit hereunder shall state the period of time
for which the unit will be utilized, the type of unit which will be utilized,
and the name, address, and phone number of the person applying for such permit.
(Ord. 672-06, 1-8-2007)
7-1C-4: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
Any person violating this provision shall be fined not less than one hundred
fifty dollars ($150.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for
each offense. Each day that a violation is found to exist shall constitute a
separate offense. A violation of this provision shall result in the immediate
revocation of a permit issued hereunder. (Ord. 672-06, 1-8-2007)
7-1C-5: ABATEMENT:
   A.   Summary Abatement: The village president may summarily order the police
or other village official or contracted private business to immediately remedy
a violation of this article whenever it is the opinion of the village president
that the violation creates the imminent threat of serious injury to persons or
serious damage to property.
   B.   Nonsummary Abatement:
      1.   The village president or any police officer of the village may serve
or cause to be served a notice in writing upon any owner, occupant, lessee or
agent in possession or control of any real or personal property within the
limits of the village, or notice may be affixed to the property upon which a
violation exists; and the notice shall specifically state the nature of the
violation and shall inform the person so notified to remedy the violation
within a specified time as may be reasonable.
      2.   If the person so notified does not remedy the violation within the
specified time, the village president is authorized to:
         a.   Order village employees to remedy the violation or to contract
for it to be done privately.
         b.   Authorize the village attorney to seek an injunction and other
relief of the continuation of the violation in a court of competent
jurisdiction.
         c.   Seek such other and further relief as may be provided by law.
   C.   Abatement Costs And Expenses: All costs and expenses incurred in
remedying a violation of this article, whether summary or nonsummary, and
whether incurred by the village or any contracted private business, shall be
paid by the owner of the property upon which such violation exists, and any
occupant, lessee and agent in possession or control of the property shall be
jointly and severally liable. The village or contracted private business may
collect by judgment and may file a notice of lien in the office of the county
recorder of deeds, which notice shall consist of a sworn statement setting out
a description of the real estate sufficient for identification thereof, the
amount of money representing the costs and expenses incurred or payable for the
service, and the date or dates when such costs or expenses were incurred by the
village. (Ord. 672-06, 1-8-2007)
CHAPTER 2
MUNICIPAL WATER AND SEWER
ARTICLE A. COMBINED WATERWORKS AND SEWERAGE SYSTEM
SECTION:
7-2A-1: Systems Combined
7-2A-1: SYSTEMS COMBINED:
The existing waterworks system in its entirety, together with all additions,
improvements and extensions thereto that may hereafter be made, and the
proposed sanitary sewerage system of the village in its entirety, together with
all additions, improvements and extensions thereto that may hereafter be made,
are hereby declared to be a combined system, and said combined waterworks and
sewerage system shall be maintained and operated as a single utility, and a
charge or rate shall be established for the use of such combined system which
shall be reasonable and commensurate with the service performed by said
combined system, and shall be sufficient to maintain, operate, provide an
adequate depreciation fund and pay the principal and interest on any revenue
bonds which may be issued, which by their terms are made payable from the
revenues of such combined system. (Ord. 392, 5-4-1959)
ARTICLE B. WATER USE AND SERVICE
SECTION:
7-2B-1: Sewer And Water Committee
7-2B-2: Responsibility For Waterworks System, Authority To Abandon Mains
7-2B-3: Service Connections And Repairs
7-2B-4: Meters
7-2B-5: Use Of Fire Hydrants
7-2B-6: Unlawful Use Of Water
7-2B-7: Cross Connections
7-2B-7-1: Definitions
7-2B-7-2: Compliance With Existing Laws
7-2B-7-3: Cross Connections Prohibited
7-2B-7-4: Local Cross Connection Control Program
7-2B-7-5: Existing Cross Connections
7-2B-7-6: Secondary Water Sources
7-2B-7-7: Inspections
7-2B-7-8: Discontinuance Of Water Service
7-2B-8: Shutting Off Water
7-2B-9: Authority To Change Rates And Regulations
7-2B-1: SEWER AND WATER COMMITTEE:
A committee of three (3) village trustees shall be appointed annually by the
president of the board to be known as the sewer and water committee, and said
committee shall have the supervision, control and management, subject to the
board, of the maintenance, enlargement and operation of the waterworks system
of the village, the extension of such system, the selling of water therefrom
and the preservation of the property thereunto belonging. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940;
amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-2: RESPONSIBILITY FOR WATERWORKS SYSTEM, AUTHORITY TO ABANDON MAINS:
All water mains, service pipes, hydrants, shutoff valves, cocks and connections
lying and being within any street or alley in the village shall belong to and
be supplied and maintained by the village only and the village shall have the
right at any time to abandon or replace any part of such system. In case of any
such abandonment of a water main, the village shall connect the property to be
supplied with water by means of a suitable main or service pipe extending from
the nearest water main to the lot line of the property. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940;
amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-3: SERVICE CONNECTIONS AND REPAIRS:
   A.   Water Service Connections: The sewer and water department will make the
necessary service connection at the water main, the cost of which is to be paid
by the owner or contractor. The cost is to be regulated by the sewer and water
department in accordance with the prevailing cost of labor 1  and materials at
the time of installation or replacement. The owner shall lay and maintain the
service pipe from the water main to the premises and shall install on every
service pipe a curb stop and curb box as specified by the sewer and water
department. (Ord. 509, 12-3-1984; amd. 1987 Code)
All water connections shall be made only by a licensed plumber of the state.
(Ord. 327, 1-2-1940)
   B.   Repairs: When a leak or break occurs in a water service anywhere
between the water main and the premises, the property owner is responsible for
repair or replacement. If the property owner has not taken any action within
twenty four (24) hours after the owner has been notified, the sewer and water
department shall disconnect the service.
   C.   Street Excavations: The responsibility of the owner, whether in new
construction or in repair and replacement of water service, shall include the
cost of repairing any village street required to be excavated for said
installation or repairs. (Ord. 509, 12-3-1984; amd. 1987 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  1-8-2 of this code.
7-2B-4: METERS:
No water shall be furnished or supplied to any consumer or water taker (except
when purchased or taken from the fire hydrants direct, as provided in section
7-2B-5 of this article) unless the same be measured and registered by a water
meter.
   A.   Responsibility For Meters, Approvals: All water meters shall be
provided and owned by the village, and any such meter may be obtained from the
village but shall at all times be subject to the approval and inspection of the
sewer and water committee.
No new water meter shall be installed without the prior approval of the sewer
and water committee thereof. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940; amd. 1987 Code)
   B.   Reading Meters: The meters shall be read quarter-yearly by the
superintendent of water and sewer department. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940; amd. Ord.,
7-7-1986)
   C.   Meters In Buildings With Multiple Users:
      1.   Houses or housing units containing two (2) or more dwelling units,
or buildings containing two (2) or more separate water users, shall be supplied
with separate meters for each dwelling unit or water service user occupying the
building, unless the building owner shall, in writing, request the use of one
common meter. In the latter case, the owner and each user shall be jointly
liable for the whole meter charge and the collector shall not be required to
apportion such charges in any event. The village shall be under no obligation
to alter existing metering devices in place on the date of adoption of
ordinance 96-573.
      2.   Buildings containing more than two (2) dwelling units or water
service users supplied with one common meter for all units in the building
shall have a rate determined by assessing one-half (1/2) the minimum rate for
individual users, as established in subsection 7-2D-2A of this chapter, per
using unit in the building combined with water used above one thousand (1,000)
cubic feet charged at the rate established in subsection 7-2D-2A of this
chapter.
      3.   Each metered supply line to a water service customer shall have a
control device (valve) installed in the supply line directly preceding each
meter for the purpose of turning on or shutting off water supply. When a
commercial or residential building, serving more than one water service
customer, is served by one or more metered service lines, each metered service
line shall have such a device installed directly preceding the meter for the
purpose of removal and replacement of said meter as necessary. (Ord. 96-573, 4-
8-1996, eff. 5-1-1996)
   D.   Meters To Be Sealed, Tampering With Prohibited: All meters shall be
properly sealed by the chief of police and they shall be kept free from
breakage or injury, and any breakage of or tampering with such seal of such
water meter shall be punishable, upon conviction thereof, with a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code, or with the shutting off of water to the said property, or
both. (1987 Code)
7-2B-5: USE OF FIRE HYDRANTS:
   A.   Water may be drawn from any of the hydrants in the streets in case of
fire by the Franklin Grove fire protection district of Lee and Ogle Counties.
Sales for private use for construction, sprinkling or other purposes may also
be made from any fire hydrant at the appropriate meter rates, as measured by
the village.
   B.   No person shall open or interfere with the fire hydrants without
permission of the sewer and water committee. (1987 Code)
7-2B-6: UNLAWFUL USE OF WATER:
Any person taking water from the system without paying the rates specified in
article D of this chapter or without the prior permission of the sewer and
water committee as to those taking the same hereafter for properties not
heretofore served, shall be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7: CROSS CONNECTIONS:
7-2B-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this section the following definitions shall apply:
BACKFLOW: Water of questionable quality, wastes or other contaminants entering
a public water supply system due to a reversal of flow.
CROSS CONNECTION: A connection or arrangement of piping or appurtenance in
which a backflow could occur.
SAFE AIR GAP: The minimum distance of a water inlet or opening above the
maximum high water level or overflow rim in a fixture, device or container to
which public water is furnished which shall be at least two (2) times the
inside diameter of the water inlet pipe but shall not be less than one inch
(1") and need not be more than twelve inches (12").
SECONDARY WATER SUPPLY: A water supply system maintained in addition to a
public water supply, including, but not limited to, water systems from ground
or surface sources not meeting the requirements of act 98 of the public acts of
1913, as amended, being sections 325.201 to 325.214 of the compiled laws of
1948, or water from a public water supply which in any way has been treated,
processed or exposed to any possible contaminant or stored in other than an
approved storage facility.
SUBMERGED INLET: A water pipe or extension thereto from a public water supply
terminating in a tank, vessel, fixture or appliance which may contain water of
questionable quality, waste or other contaminant and which is unprotected
against backflow.
WATER UTILITY: The village of Franklin Grove sewer and water department. (Ord.
488, 11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7-2: COMPLIANCE WITH EXISTING LAWS:
A connection with a public water supply system shall comply with the existing
laws and rules and the provisions of the ordinances of the village. (Ord. 488,
11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7-3: CROSS CONNECTIONS PROHIBITED:
Cross connections of the public water supply system and any other water supply
system or source, including, but not limited to, the following, are prohibited:
   A.   Between a public water supply system and a secondary water supply.
   B.   By submerged inlet.
   C.   Between a lawn sprinkling system and the public water supply system.
   D.   Between a public water supply and piping which may contain sanitary
waste or a chemical contaminant.
   E.   Between a public water supply system and piping immersed in a tank or
vessel which may contain a contaminant. (Ord. 488, 11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7-4: LOCAL CROSS CONNECTION CONTROL PROGRAM:
The village has adopted all provisions of section
7-2B-7 as its comprehensive control program for the elimination and prevention
of all cross connections, removal of all existing cross connections and
prevention of all future cross connections to the village water supply.
   A.   Plumbing of each new service shall be installed in accordance with the
requirements of the Illinois state plumbing code.
   B.   Water customers shall correct plumbing code violations which are a
threat to the public water supply whenever such violations are discovered.
Corrective measures pertaining to established cross connections shall be
applicable.
   C.   The village water and sewer committee chairman shall conduct, or cause
to be conducted, an initial survey of new water services and a survey of all
water services every two (2) years. This survey shall be used to develop an
inventory of the way the customers use water. Where potentially hazardous
conditions are suspected, the water customer shall be requested to have a
licensed plumber, who has been approved as a backflow control device inspector,
either:
      1.   Inspect the plumbing and test and maintain all cross connection
control devices annually.
      2.   Install a fixed air gap or a reduced pressure zone (RPZ) backflow
preventer on the service line to the premises. This air gap or RPZ must be
maintained, inspected and tested annually.
   D.   A written record of the village cross connection surveys shall be
maintained which includes:
      1.   The name and location of each customer required to have an annual
inspection.
      2.   The date each cross connection device was installed.
      3.   The annual test results for each cross connection control device and
a summary of any repairs and changes made. (Ord. 565, 7-10-1995)
7-2B-7-5: EXISTING CROSS CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Elimination Of Existing Cross Connections: Within one year from the
effective date hereof, all existing cross connections to the village water
supply systems shall be eliminated. The expenses of such elimination shall be
that of the owner of the property on which such cross connection exists.
If the cross connection has not been removed within the time as herein
specified, the village shall physically separate the village water supply from
the on site piping system in such manner that the two (2) systems cannot be
connected by any unauthorized person.
   B.   Corrections And Protective Devices: Any user of the village water
supply shall obtain written approval from the sewer and water department of any
proposed corrective action or protective device before using or installing it.
The total time allowed for completion of the necessary corrections shall be
contingent upon the degree of hazard involved and include the time required to
obtain and install equipment. (Ord. 488, 11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7-6: SECONDARY WATER SOURCES:
   A.   Piping Identification: When a secondary water source is used in
addition to the village water supply, exposed village water and secondary water
piping shall be identified by distinguishing colors or tags and so maintained
that each pipe may be readily traced in its entirety. It will be necessary to
protect the village water supply at the service connection in a manner
acceptable to the sewer and water department.
   B.   Private Water Storage Tanks: A private water storage tank supplied from
the village water supply system shall be deemed a secondary water supply unless
it is designed and approved for potable water usage. (Ord. 488, 11-3-1980; amd.
1987 Code)
7-2B-7-7: INSPECTIONS:
The village sewer and water department or any representative thereof, shall
have the authority to inspect any premises to determine the presence of an
existing cross connection and to order the elimination of such cross
connection. (Ord. 488, 11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-7-8: DISCONTINUANCE OF WATER SERVICE:
The sewer and water department is hereby authorized to discontinue water
service after a reasonable notice to any person owning any property where a
cross connection in violation of this section exists. The sewer and water
department may take such other precautionary measures as necessary to eliminate
any danger of the contamination of the village water supply systems. Water
service to such property shall not be restored until such cross connection has
been eliminated. (Ord. 488, 11-3-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2B-8: SHUTTING OFF WATER:
   A.   Discontinuance Of Service: The rules, regulations and water rates
herein named shall be considered a part of the contract with every person
supplied with water through such waterworks system, and binding upon such water
users, and whenever any of such rules, regulations or rates shall be violated
by any such users, then the water shall be shut off from the building or place
of such violation and shall not be let on again except by order of the
committee and upon the payment of the expense of shutting off and turning on
such water, which charge shall be as provided in article D of this chapter, and
the further payment of any water rate charge which may then be in arrears, as
against such property. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940; amd. Ord. 395B, 6-1-1959)
   B.   Authority To Shut Off Water: In case of fire or fire alarm, or in
making repairs, replacements, extensions or making later connections to the
mains, pipes or water plant, the village reserves the right to shut off the
water at once with or without notice to users as long as may be necessary.
(Ord. 327, 1-2-1940)
7-2B-9: AUTHORITY TO CHANGE RATES AND REGULATIONS:
The village reserves the right at any time to change the water rates or
regulations. (Ord. 327, 1-2-1940)
ARTICLE C. SEWER USE AND SERVICE
SECTION:

7-2C-2: Use Of Public Sewers Required
7-2C-3: Private Systems

7-2C-4-2: Separate Sewers Required

7-2C-4-7: Excavations
7-2C-4-8: Surface Runoff
7-2C-4-9: Liability For Costs And Damages
7-2C-5: Discharge Of Effluent
7-2C-6: Prohibited Substances
7-2C-7: Materials Under Special Review
7-2C-8: Interceptors
7-2C-9: Preliminary Treatment
7-2C-10: Industrial Wastes
7-2C-11: Measurements, Tests And Analyses
7-2C-12: Special Agreements
7-2C-13: Industrial Cost Recovery
7-2C-14: Property Damage
7-2C-15: Inspections
7-2C-16: Violations And Penalties
7-2C-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this article shall be as follows:
ACT: The federal water pollution control act, as amended, 33 USC.
ADMINISTRATOR: The administrator of the U.S. environmental protection agency.
APPROVING AUTHORITY: The president and board of trustees of the village acting
by and through the sewer and water committee, or the person designated by it,
being its duly authorized agent or representative.
BOD (Denoting Biochemical Oxygen Demand): The quantity of oxygen utilized in
the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure
in five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C) expressed in milligrams
per liter.
BASIC USER CHARGE: The basic assessment levied on all users of the public sewer
system for operation, maintenance and replacement.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer or other
approved point of discharge beginning ten feet (10') (3.0 m) outside the inner
face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer which is designed and intended to receive wastewater,
storm, surface and ground water drainage.
COMPATIBLE POLLUTANT: Biochemical oxygen demand, suspended solids, pH and fecal
coliform bacteria, plus additional pollutants identified in the NPDES permit.
CONTROL MANHOLE: A structure located on a site from which industrial wastes are
discharged. Where feasible, the manhole shall have an interior drop. The
purpose of a control manhole is to provide access for a village representative
to sample and/or measure discharges.
DEBT SERVICE CHARGE: The amount to be paid each billing period for payment of
interest, principal and coverage of revenue bonds outstanding and shall be
computed by dividing the annual debt service charge by the number of users
connected to the wastewater facilities.
DIRECTOR: The chief administrative officer of the state of Illinois
environmental protection agency.
EASEMENT: An acquired legal right for the specific use of land owned by others.
EFFLUENT CRITERIA: Are defined in any applicable NPDES permit.
FEDERAL GRANT: The U.S. government participation in the financing of the
construction of treatment works as provided for by title II - grants for
construction of treatment works of the act.
FLOATABLE OIL: Oil, fat or grease in a physical state such that it will
separate by gravity from wastewater by treatment in an approved pretreatment
facility. A wastewater shall be considered free of floatable fat if it is
properly pretreated and the wastewater does not interfere with the collection
system.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL COST RECOVERY: Recovery from the industrial uses of a treatment
works of the grant amount allocable to treatment of wastes from such users
pursuant to section 204(b) of PL 92-500 and 40 CFR part 35.928(1) and (2).
INDUSTRIAL USER: For the purposes of industrial cost recovery, shall mean any
nongovernmental user of publicly owned treatment works identified in the
"Standard Industrial Classification Manual", 1972, office of management and
budget, as amended and supplemented, under the following divisions:
   Division A   -   Agriculture, forestry and fishing
   Division B   -   Mining
   Division D   -   Manufacturing
   Division E   -   Transportation, communications, electric, gas and sanitary
services
   Division I   -   Services
A user in the divisions listed may be excluded if it is determined by the sewer
and water committee that it will introduce primarily segregated domestic wastes
or wastes from sanitary conveniences.
Industrial user, for the purpose of developing the user charge system, may be a
manufacturing or process facility which is engaged in a productive and profit
making enterprise.
INDUSTRIAL WASTE: Any solid, liquid or gaseous substance discharged, permitted
to flow or escaping from any industrial, manufacturing, commercial or business
establishment or process or from the development, recovery or processing of any
natural resource as distinct from sanitary sewage.
INFILTRATION: The total quantity of water from both infiltration and inflow
without distinguishing the source.
INFLOW: The water discharged into a sewer system, including building drains and
sewers, from such sources as, but not limited to, roof leaders; cellar, yard
and area drains; foundation drains; unpolluted cooling water discharges; drains
from springs and swampy areas; manhole covers, cross connections from storm
sewers and combined sewers, catch basins, storm waters, surface runoff, street
wash waters or drainage. (Inflow does not include and is distinguished from
infiltration.)
MAJOR CONTRIBUTING INDUSTRY: An industrial user of the publicly owned treatment
works that: a) has a flow of fifty thousand (50,000) gallons or more per
average workday; b) has a flow greater than five percent (5%) of the flow
carried by the municipal system receiving the waste; c) has in its waste a
toxic pollutant in toxic amounts as defined in standards issued under section
307(a) of the act; or d) is found by the permit issuance authority, in
connection with the issuance of an NPDES permit to the publicly owned treatment
works receiving the waste, to have significant impact, either singly or in
combination with other contributing industries, on that treatment works or upon
the quality of effluent from that treatment works.
MILLIGRAMS PER LITER: A unit of the concentration of water or wastewater
constituent. It is 0.001 gram of the constituent in one thousand (1,000)
milliliter of water. It has replaced the unit formerly used commonly, parts per
million, to which it is approximately equivalent, in reporting the results of
water and wastewater analysis.
NPDES PERMIT: A permit issued under the national pollutant discharge
elimination system for discharge of wastewaters to the navigable waters of the
United States, pursuant to section 402 of PL 92-500.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface or ground water.
OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE COSTS: All costs, direct and indirect, (other than
debt service) to ensure adequate wastewater treatment on a continuing basis,
conforming with related federal, state and local requirements, and assuring
optimal long term facility management. (These costs include depreciation and
replacement.)
ppm: Parts per million by weight.
PERSON: Any and all persons, natural or artificial, including any individual,
firm, company, municipal or private corporation, association, society,
institution, enterprise, governmental agency or other entity.
pH: The logarithm (base 10) of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration
expressed in grams per liter of solution. It shall be determined by one of the
procedures outlined in standard methods.
POPULATION EQUIVALENT: A term used to evaluate the impact of industrial or
other waste on a treatment works or stream. One population equivalent is one
hundred (100) gallons of sewage per day containing 0.17 pounds of BOD and 0.20
pounds of suspended solids. The impact on a treatment works is evaluated as the
equivalent of the highest of three (3) parameters. Impact on a stream is the
higher of the BOD/suspended solids parameters.
PRETREATMENT: The treatment of wastewater from sources before introduction into
the wastewater treatment works.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") (1.27 cm) in any
dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer dedicated to or provided by or subject to the
jurisdiction of the village consisting of collector sewer, interceptor sewer,
forcemain and pumping station. It shall also include sewers within or outside
the village boundaries that serve one or more persons and ultimately discharge
into the village sanitary sewer system, even though those sewers may not have
been constructed with village funds.
REPLACEMENT: Expenditures for obtaining and installing equipment, accessories
or appurtenances which are necessary during the service life of the treatment
works to maintain the capacity and performance for which such works were
designed and constructed. The term "operation and maintenance" includes
replacement.
RESIDENTIAL OR COMMERCIAL USER, NONINDUSTRIAL USER: Any user of the treatment
works not classified as an industrial user or excluded as an industrial user as
provided for in this section.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer that conveys sewage or industrial wastes or a
combination of both, and into which storm, surface and ground waters or
unpolluted industrial wastes are not intentionally admitted.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
ground, surface and storm waters as may be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices, structures and equipment
for treating sewage.
SEWER: A pipe or conduit for conveying sewage or any other waste liquids,
including storm, surface and ground water drainage.
SEWER AND WATER COMMITTEE: Refers to a committee of three (3) trustees
appointed annually by the president of the village board. The sewer and water
committee shall have the supervision, control and management, subject to the
village board, of the maintenance, enlargement and operation of the combined
waterworks and sewerage system of the village, and the extension of such system
and the selling of water therefrom and the preservation of the property
thereunto belonging.
SEWERAGE: The system of sewers and appurtenances for the collection,
transportation and pumping of sewage.
SEWERAGE FUND: The principal accounting designation for all revenues received
and expenses incurred in the operation of the sewerage system.
SHALL/MAY: Shall is mandatory. May is permissible.
SIGNIFICANT INDUSTRY: Any industry that will contribute greater than ten
percent (10%) of the design flow and/or design pollutant loading of the
treatment works.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage or industrial wastes which, in
concentration of any given constituent or in quantity of flow, exceeds for any
period of duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times
the average twenty four (24) hour concentration of flows during normal
operation.
STANDARD METHODS: The examination and analytical procedures set forth in the
most recent edition of "Standard Methods For The Examination Of Water, Sewage
And Industrial Wastes", published jointly by the American Public Health
Association, the American Water Works Association and the Federation of Sewage
and Industrial Wastes Association.
STATE ACT: The Illinois antipollution bond act of 1970 1 .
STATE GRANT: The state of Illinois participation in the financing of the
construction of treatment works and provided for by the Illinois antipollution
bond act and for making such grants as filed with the secretary of the state of
Illinois.
STORM SEWER: A sewer that carries storm, surface and ground water drainage, but
excludes sewage and industrial wastes other than unpolluted cooling water.
STORM WATER RUNOFF: That portion of the rainfall that is drained into the
sewers.
SUPERINTENDENT: The person appointed by the village president and board of
trustees from time to time to oversee and/or perform the operation and
maintenance of the sewerage system.
SURCHARGE: The assessment, in addition to the basic user charge and debt
service charge, which is levied on those persons whose wastes are greater in
strength than the concentration values established as representative of normal
sewage.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in water, sewage or industrial wastes and which are removable by a
laboratory filtration device. Quantitative determination of suspended solids
shall be made in accordance with procedures set forth in "standard methods".
UNPOLLUTED WATER: Water of quality equal to or better than the effluent
criteria in effect or water that would not cause violation of receiving water
quality standards and would not be benefited by discharge to the sanitary
sewers and wastewater treatment facilities provided.
USEFUL LIFE: The estimated period during which the treatment works will be
operated and shall be thirty (30) years from the date of start up of any
wastewater facilities constructed with a federal or state grant.
USER CHARGE: A charge levied on users of waterworks and treatment works
facilities for the cost of operation and maintenance including replacement of
such works and the cost of any bond debt of such works and shall consist of
both basic user charges, surcharges and industrial charges, if any.
USER CLASS: The type of user, either "residential or commercial" or
"industrial", as defined herein.
VILLAGE: The village of Franklin Grove, and any reference to "within the
village" shall mean all territory within the perimeter of the village of
Franklin Grove boundaries.
WASTEWATER SERVICE CHARGE: The charge per quarterly period levied on all users
of the wastewater facilities. The service charge shall be computed as outlined
in article D of this chapter, and shall consist of the total of the basic user
charge and surcharge, if applicable.
WASTEWATER TREATMENT WORKS: An arrangement of devices and structures for
treating wastewater, industrial wastes and sludge; sometimes used as synonymous
with "wastewater treatment plant" or "sewage treatment plant" or "pollution
control plant".
WATER QUALITY STANDARDS: Are defined in the water pollution regulations of
Illinois.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 30 ILCS 405/1 et seq.
7-2C-2: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED:
   A.   Unlawful Deposition Of Wastes: It shall be unlawful for any person to
place, deposit or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary manner on public or
private property within the village, or in any area under the jurisdiction of
the village, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable
waste.
   B.   Unlawful Discharge Of Wastes: It shall be unlawful to discharge to any
natural outlet, watercourse or storm sewer within the village or in any area
under the jurisdiction of the village, any sewage or other polluted waters,
except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent
provisions of this article.
   C.   Unlawful Construction Of Private Facilities: Except as hereinafter
provided, it shall be unlawful to construct any privy, privy vault, septic
tank, cesspool or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage.
   D.   Mandatory Sewer Hook Up: The owner of all houses, buildings or
properties used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes,
situated within the village and abutting on any street, alley or right of way
in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary
sewer of the village, is hereby required, at his expense, to install suitable
toilet facilities therein, and to connect such facilities directly with the
proper public sewer in a manner approved by the superintendent or his
representative, within one hundred eighty (180) days after the official notice
to do so, provided that said public sewer is within one hundred feet (100')
(30.5 m) of the property line. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-3: PRIVATE SYSTEMS:
Where a sanitary sewer of the village is not available under the provisions of
subsection 7-2C-2D of this article, the building sewer shall be connected to a
private sewage disposal system complying with the provisions of this section.
   A.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   Permit Required: Before commencement of construction of a private
sewage disposal system, the owner shall first obtain a permit signed by the
sewer and water committee.
      2.   Application For Permits: The application for such permit shall be
made to the sewer and water committee on a special form furnished by the
village and shall be accompanied by plans, specifications and such other
information considered pertinent in the judgment of the sewer and water
committee.
      3.   Inspection: A permit for a private sewage disposal system shall not
become effective until installation is completed to the satisfaction of the
representative of the sewer and water department. He shall be allowed to
inspect the work at any stage of construction and, in any event, the applicant
for the permit shall notify the representative of the water and sewer
department when the work is ready for final inspection and before any
underground portions are covered. The inspection shall be made within four (4)
hours of the receipt of notice by the representative of the water and sewer
department, except for Sundays and holidays.
   B.   System Design:
      1.   The type, capacities, location and layout of a private sewage
disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the state of Illinois
private sewage disposal licensing act and code 1  and with the state of
Illinois environmental protection agency.
      2.   No permit shall be issued for any private sewage disposal system
employing insufficient subsurface soil absorption facilities.
      3.   No septic tank or cesspool shall be permitted to discharge into any
public sewer or natural outlet.
   C.   Connection To Sanitary Sewer Required: At such time as a public sewer
becomes available to a property served by a private sewage disposal system, as
provided in subsection 7-2C-2D of this article, a direct connection shall be
made to the public sewer of the village within ninety (90) days, in compliance
with this article, and any septic tanks, cesspools and similar private sewage
disposal facilities shall be abandoned and filled with suitable material.
   D.   Operation Of Private Systems: The owner shall operate and maintain the
private sewage disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, and at no
expense to the village.
   E.   Additional Requirements: No provision of this section shall be
construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed by
the county board of health. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 225 ILCS 225/1 et seq.
7-2C-4: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
7-2C-4-1: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Required: No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any
connections with or opening into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the village.
   B.   Classes Of Permits; Application: There shall be two (2) classes of
building sewer permits: for residential and commercial service, and for service
to establishments producing industrial wastes.
In either case, the owner or his agent shall make application on a special form
furnished by the village. The permit application shall be supplemented by any
plans, specifications or other information considered pertinent in the judgment
of the sewer and water committee. The industry, as a condition of permit
authorization, must provide information describing its wastewater constituents,
characteristics and type of activity.
   C.   Restrictions On Permits: A building sewer permit will only be issued
and a sewer connection shall only be allowed if it can be demonstrated that the
downstream sewerage facilities, including sewers, pump stations and wastewater
treatment facilities, have sufficient reserve capacity to adequately and
efficiently handle the additional anticipated waste load. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980;
amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-2: SEPARATE SEWERS REQUIRED:
A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building,
except that where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot
and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building
through an adjoining alley, court, yard or driveway, the building sewer from
the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole
considered as one building sewer. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-3: USE OF OLD BUILDING SEWERS:
Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they
are found, on examination and test by the representative of the sewer and water
department, to meet all requirements of this article. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd.
1987 Code)
7-2C-4-4: CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS:
The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building sewer, and
the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, jointing, testing
and backfilling the trench, shall all conform to the requirements of the
building and plumbing codes 1  or other applicable rules and regulations of the
village. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the
material and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the American
Society of Testing Materials, "Water Pollution Control Federation Manual Of
Practice No. 9", and "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main
Construction In Illinois" shall apply. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 8, chapter 1 of this code.
7-2C-4-5: BUILDING SEWER CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Connection Specifications: The connection of the building sewer into
the public sewer shall conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing
codes or other applicable rules and regulations of the village, or the
procedures set forth in the appropriate specifications of the American Society
of Testing Materials, "Water Pollution Control Federation Manual Of Practice
No. 9", and "Standards Specifications For Water And Sewer Main Construction In
Illinois". All such connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any
deviation from the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the
sewer and water committee before installation.
   B.   Inspection: The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify
the representative of the sewer and water department when the building sewer is
ready for inspection and connection to the public sewer. The sewer lateral from
the property line to the village sewer main shall remain uncovered for
inspection and the connection shall be made under the supervision of the
representative of the sewer and water department or his representative. (Ord.
483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-6: SEWAGE LIFT:
Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an
elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any building
drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage
carried by such building drain shall be lifted by a means which is approved in
accordance with subsection 7-2C-4-1A of this article and discharged to the
building sewer. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-7: EXCAVATIONS:
All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded
with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets,
sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the course of the
work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the village at no expense to
the village. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-8: SURFACE RUNOFF:
   A.   The maintenance and connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation
drains, areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff or ground water to a
building sewer or building drain which in turn is connected directly or
indirectly to a public sanitary sewer is prohibited.
   B.   Existing roof drains, footing tile or other illegal connections to the
public sanitary sewers shall be disconnected from said sewer within one year
after written notice from the village to do such work. The expense of such work
shall be paid by the property owner. The superintendent shall determine if the
disconnection has been made in a satisfactory fashion.
   C.   Existing roof drains discharging at the foundation wall shall be
extended by a suitable means, as approved by the superintendent, to a point at
least six feet (6') away from the foundation wall. This work shall be done and
paid for by the owner. All such roof drains must be extended away from the
footing wall within six (6) months after written notice from the village to do
such work. All new homes must provide the extended roof drains as a part of the
construction phase.
   D.   Violators may be subject to fines per section
7-2C-16 of this article. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-4-9: LIABILITY FOR COSTS AND DAMAGES:
   A.   All costs and expenses incident to the installation and connection of
the building sewer shall be borne by the owner of the property to be served or
the applicant for the service.
   B.   The owner or applicant shall indemnify the village from any loss or
damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the
building sewer.
   C.   All connections shall be authorized only when the same shall not damage
or interfere with the use of the village sewer system by other users of the
system.
   D.   The person making the connections shall be liable for the cost of any
lift station and shall not install any sewer or make a connection which shall
overload an existing lift station without making provisions for increased
capacity of the lift station sufficient to accommodate the use of the sewer to
be connected. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-5: DISCHARGE OF EFFLUENT:
   A.   Discharge Into Sanitary Sewers Prohibited: No person shall discharge or
cause to be discharged any storm water, surface water, ground water, roof
runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated cooling water or unpolluted
industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer.
   B.   Use Of Storm Sewers And Combined Sewers: Storm water and all other
unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to such sewers as are specifically
designated as combined sewers or storm sewers or to a natural outlet approved
by the representative of the sewer and water department. Industrial cooling
water or unpolluted process waters may be discharged on approval of the
representative of the sewer and water department to a storm sewer or natural
outlet. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
   C.   Unlawful Storm Water Drain Connection:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to connect
or cause to be connected, any drain carrying, or to carry, any toilet, sink,
basement, septic tank, cesspool, industrial waste, or any fixture or device
discharging polluting substances, to any storm water drain in the village of
Franklin Grove.
      2.   Any person, firm or corporation violating this subsection C shall be
fined not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than seven hundred
fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense, and a separate offense shall be
deemed committed for each and every day during which a violation continues or
exists. (Ord. 600, 4-12-2000)
7-2C-6: PROHIBITED SUBSTANCES:
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following
described waters or wastes to any public sewers:
   A.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
   B.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids or
gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a
hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant.
   C.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment
and personnel of the sewage works.
   D.   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the
proper operation of the sewage works such as, but not limited to, ashes,
cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar,
plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and
fleshings, entrails and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole
or ground by garbage grinders. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-7: MATERIALS UNDER SPECIAL REVIEW:
   A.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the following
described substances, materials, waters or wastes if it appears likely, in the
opinion of the sewer and water committee, that such wastes can harm either the
sewers, sewage treatment process or equipment; have an adverse effect on the
receiving stream; or can otherwise endanger life, limb, public property or
constitute a nuisance. In forming his opinion as to the acceptability of these
wastes, the superintendent will give consideration to such factors as the
quantities of subject wastes in relation to flows and velocities in the sewers,
materials of construction of the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment
process, capacity of the sewage treatment plant, degree of treatability of
wastes in the sewage treatment plant and maximum limits established by
regulatory agencies. The substances prohibited are:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65°C).
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous materials; or
oils, whether emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter
(100 mg/l) or containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at
temperatures between thirty two (32) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit
(150°F) (0° and 65°C).
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/
4) horsepower (0.76 hp metric) or greater shall be subject to the review and
approval of the sewer and water committee.
      4.   Any waters or wastes containing strong acid, iron pickling wastes or
concentrated plating solutions, whether neutralized or not.
      5.   Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc or
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting an excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the sewer and water committee for such materials.
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste or odor
producing substances in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be
established by the sewer and water committee as necessary, after treatment of
the composite sewage, to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other
public agencies of jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters.
      7.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentration as may exceed limits established by the sewer and water committee
in compliance with applicable state or federal regulations.
      8.   Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of 9.5.
      9.   Any mercury or any of its compounds in excess of 0.0005 mg/l as Hg
at any time except as permitted by the sewer and water committee in compliance
with applicable state and federal regulations.
      10.   Any cyanide in excess of 0.025 mg/l at any time except as permitted
by the sewer and water committee in compliance with applicable state and
federal regulations.
      11.   Materials which exert or cause:
         a.   Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids (such as, but
not limited to, fullers earth, lime slurries and lime residues) or of dissolved
solids (such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride and sodium sulfate);
         b.   Excessive discoloration (such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions);
         c.   Unusual BOD, chemical oxygen demand or chlorine requirements in
such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works.
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous materials; or
oils, whether emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter
(100 mg/l) or containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at
temperatures between thirty two (32) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit
(150°F) (0° and 65°C).
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/
4) horsepower (0.76 hp metric) or greater shall be subject to the review and
approval of the sewer and water committee.
   B.   If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be discharged
to the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or possess the
characteristics enumerated in subsection A of this section, and/or which are in
violation of the standards for pretreatment provided in chapter 1, EPA rules
and regulations, and any amendments thereto, and which in the judgment of the
sewer and water committee may have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works,
processes, equipment or receiving waters or which otherwise create a hazard to
life or constitute a public nuisance, the sewer and water committee may:
      1.   Reject the wastes;
      2.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers;
      3.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/or
      4.   Require payment to cover the added costs of handling and treating
the wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges, under the provisions
of subsection 7-2C-11B of this article.
If the sewer and water committee permits the pretreatment or equalization of
waste flows, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be
subject to the review and approval of the sewer and water committee, and
subject to the requirements of all applicable codes, ordinances and laws. (Ord.
483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-8: INTERCEPTORS:
Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the
sewer and water committee, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid
wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or
other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required
for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a
