type and capacity approved by the sewer and water committee and shall be
located as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection.
(Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-9: PRELIMINARY TREATMENT:
Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided, they
shall be continuously maintained in satisfactory and effective operation by the
owner at his expense. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-10: INDUSTRIAL WASTES:
Each new industry shall be required to install a control manhole and, when
required by the sewer and water committee, the owner of any property serviced
by a building sewer carrying industrial and/or domestic wastes shall install a
suitable control manhole together with such necessary meters and other
appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and
measurement of the wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and
safely located, and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by
the sewer and water committee. The manhole shall be installed by the owner at
his expense and shall be maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at
all times. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-11: MEASUREMENTS, TESTS AND ANALYSES:
   A.   The owner of any property served by a building sewer carrying
industrial wastes shall provide laboratory measurements, tests and analyses of
waters and wastes to illustrate compliance with this article and any special
conditions for discharge established by the sewer and water committee or
regulatory agencies having jurisdiction over the discharge. The number, type
and frequency of laboratory analyses to be performed by the owner shall be as
stipulated by the sewer and water committee, but no less than once per year the
industry must supply a complete analysis of the constituents of the wastewater
discharge to assure that compliance with the federal, state and local standards
are being met. The owner shall report the results of measurements and
laboratory analyses to the sewer and water committee at such times and in such
manner as prescribed by said committee. The owner shall bear the expense of all
measurements, analyses and reporting required by the sewer and water committee.
At such times as deemed necessary, the sewer and water committee reserves the
right to take measurements and samples for analysis by an outside laboratory.
   B.   All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters
and wastes to which reference is made in this article shall be determined in
accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods For The Examination Of
Water And Wastewater", published by the American Public Health Association, and
shall be determined at the control manhole provided, or upon suitable samples
taken at said control manhole. In the event that no special manhole has been
required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream
manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is
connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to
reflect the effect of constituents upon the sewage works and to determine the
existence of hazards to life, limb and property. (The particular analysis
involved will determine whether a 24 hour composite of all outfalls of a
premise is appropriate or whether a grab sample or samples should be taken.
Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids analyses are obtained from
24 hour composites of all outfalls whereas pHs are determined from periodic
grab samples.) (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-12: SPECIAL AGREEMENTS:
No statement contained in this article shall be construed as preventing any
special agreement or arrangement between the village and any industrial concern
whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by
the village for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial
concern. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-13: INDUSTRIAL COST RECOVERY:
No industrial user may discharge sewage into any public sewer until the village
has adopted an industrial cost recovery system which:
   A.   Meets the requirements of section 204(b)(a)(B) of the federal water
pollution control act amendments of 1972 and applicable federal regulations.
   B.   Has been approved by the agency in accordance with the conditions of
any grant made to the village by the United States environmental protection
agency or by the state of Illinois for the construction of any part of the
sewer system or sewage treatment works of the village. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980;
amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-14: PROPERTY DAMAGE:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or equipment which
is a part of the sewage works. Any person violating this provision shall be
subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly conduct. (Ord. 483, 4-7-
1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-15: INSPECTIONS:
   A.   Entry Powers:
      1.   The representative of the sewer and water department, superintendent
and other duly authorized employees of the village, the Illinois environmental
protection agency and the U.S. environmental protection agency, bearing proper
credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all properties for
the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and testing in
accordance with the provisions of this article. The representative of the sewer
and water department, superintendent or his representatives shall have no
authority to inquire into any processes, including metallurgical, chemical, oil
refining, ceramic, paper or other industries beyond that point having a direct
bearing on the kind and source of discharge to the sewers or waterways or
facilities for waste treatment.
      2.   The representative of the sewer and water department, superintendent
and other duly authorized employees of the village bearing proper credentials
and identification shall be permitted to enter all private properties through
which the village holds a duly negotiated easement for the purpose of, but not
limited to, inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, repair and
maintenance of any portion of the sewage works lying within said easement. All
entry and subsequent work, if any, on said easement, shall be done in full
accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement pertaining to the
private property involved.
   B.   Disclaimer Of Liability: While performing the necessary work on private
properties referred to in subsection A1 of this section, the representative of
the sewer and water department, superintendent or duly authorized employees of
the village, the Illinois environmental protection agency and the U.S.
environmental protection agency shall observe all safety rules applicable to
the premises established by the company, and the company shall be held harmless
for injury or death to the village employees and the village shall indemnify
the company against loss or damage to its property by village employees and
against liability claims and demands for personal injury or property damage
asserted against the company and growing out of the gauging and sampling
operation, except as such may be caused by negligence or failure of the company
to maintain safe conditions as required in section
7-2C-11 of this article. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
7-2C-16: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
   A.   Notice Of Violation: Any person found to be violating any provision of
this article, except section
7-2C-12 of this article, shall be served by the village with a written notice
stating the nature of the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for
the satisfactory correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of
time stated in such notice, permanently cease all violations.
   B.   Permit Revocations: The village may revoke any permit for sewage
disposal as a result of any violation of any provision of this article.
   C.   Liability Of Violator: Any person violating any of the provisions of
this article shall become liable to the village for any expense, loss or damage
occasioned the village by reason of such violation.
   D.   Penalties: Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time
limit provided for in subsection A of this section shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and, on conviction thereof, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 483, 4-7-1980; amd. 1987 Code)
ARTICLE D. WATER AND SEWER RATES AND CHARGES
SECTION:
7-2D-1: Application For Service Required
7-2D-2: Rates And Charges
7-2D-3: Liability For Charges
7-2D-3-1: Water And Sewer Bills For Multi-Family Dwellings
7-2D-4: Billing Procedure
7-2D-5: Disposition Of Revenues
7-2D-6: Books And Accounts
7-2D-7: Rules And Regulations
7-2D-8: Enforcement
7-2D-1: APPLICATION FOR SERVICE REQUIRED:
No person shall make any connection to the water main or the sewer main of the
combined waterworks and sewerage system of the village except upon written
application to the village clerk and upon issuance of a permit for such
connection by said clerk. Each application shall state the name of the
applicant, the permit desired, the location to be used; and each application
shall contain such additional information as may be needed for the proper
guidance of the village officials in the issuing of the permit. (Ord. 517, 7-7-
1986)
7-2D-2: RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Water Service And Sewer Customer Charges: Water service and sewer
customers will be charged a fee as set by the governing body of the village.
For sewer customers that are unmetered, the fee will also be set by the
governing body of the village. (Ord. 622-02, 6-10-2002, eff. 7-1-2002; amd.
Ord. 676-06, 12-11-2006, eff. 1-7-2007)
   B.   Water Deposits: All new connections customers are required to deposit
the sum of one hundred twenty dollars ($120.00) for and as a water deposit.
Deposits are due on the date of water service connection. If the deposit is not
paid within thirty (30) days of the connection date, then the water shall be
shut off and water service terminated. If the water service is terminated
because of failure to pay required deposit or due to a delinquent bill, the
customer will be assessed a fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for turning the
water off. In addition, the customer will be assessed a fee of twenty five
dollars ($25.00) to have water service restored. Once service is terminated,
all delinquent amounts and service fees must be paid before water service can
be restored. (Ord. 568, 7-10-1995; amd. Ord. 631-03, 3-10-2003, eff. 4-1-2003)
      1.   Deposits paid by tenant customers for service to rental properties
shall be retained by the village for the term of the lease agreement. Deposits
shall be applied to final bills with remaining balances returned to customers.
      2.   Deposits paid by property owner customers shall be retained by the
village until four (4) continuous quarters of timely water and sewer service
payments have been made. Following the four (4) quarters of continuous timely
payments the deposit shall be returned to the depositor or his agent or may be
applied as a credit to the account for payment at the discretion of the
depositor. The deposit may be waived for property owners with good credit
histories moving from one service address to another within the village.
   C.   Water And Sewer New Connection Charges:
      1.   Water Service Connection And Inspection: Applicants for water supply
connection either within or without the corporate limits of the village shall
pay connection charges of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for connection to the
village water supply system. In addition to all other charges set forth herein,
an inspection fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) is required at the time the
connection charge is paid.
      2.   Sanitary Sewer System Connection And Inspection: Applicants for
sanitary sewer system connection either within or without the corporate limits
of the village shall pay connection charges of one hundred dollars ($100.00)
for connection to the village sanitary sewer system. In addition to all other
charges set forth herein, an inspection fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) is
required at the time the connection charge is paid.
   D.   Meter Validity Checks: When a service customer raises a question
concerning the accuracy of a village water metering device, and requests that
the metering device be checked, the metering device will be removed and tested
for accuracy by village employees of the water and sewer department.
      1.   If the metering device is found to be faulty it will be repaired
and/or replaced at no cost to the service customer.
      2.   If the metering device is found to be accurate a service fee of
thirty five dollars ($35.00) will be assessed for removal, testing and
reinstallation of the metering device.
      3.   Testing of special use meters for which the village does not possess
appropriate testing equipment will be charged on an actual cost basis as
charged by an outside testing service when testing reflects that meters are
working properly.
      4.   The village reserves the right to remove, test, reinstall or replace
metering devices on the water supply system at its own discretion. (Ord. 568,
7-10-1995)
7-2D-3: LIABILITY FOR CHARGES:
The owner of the premises, the occupant thereof and the user of the service
shall be jointly and severally liable to pay for the service on such premises
and the service is furnished to the premises by the village only upon the
condition that the owner of the premises, occupant and user of the service are
jointly and severally liable therefor to the village. The rates and charges for
water and sewer hereunder shall be a lien against the premises so served and
said lien shall remain with the property until paid in full. (Ord. 533, 10-2-
1989)
7-2D-3-1: WATER AND SEWER BILLS FOR MULTI-FAMILY DWELLINGS:
   A.   The owner of any multi-family residential dwelling or multi-user
commercial building shall be responsible for the payment of all water and sewer
fees associated with said unit due to the village of Franklin Grove on behalf
of himself, or any lessee, or other possessor of such unit.
      1.   No water or sewer service shall be provided to any multi-family
residential dwelling or multi-user commercial building until a person as the
owner or agent thereof shall execute an agreement in a form provided by the
village assuming personal responsibility for the cost of any water and sewer
services by himself or any lessee.
      2.   Any person having signed an agreement as provided herein shall
remain liable pursuant to said agreement until another person shall assume said
liability by executing a new agreement in a form provided by the village.
      3.   Failure to pay any water or sewer service within fifteen (15) days
of the due date shall result in a disconnection of all such services.
   B.   Upon transfer of ownership of said units it shall be the responsibility
of the seller(s) to notify the village clerk of identity and whereabouts of the
new owner(s).
   C.   Unless otherwise stated herein, a separate offense shall be deemed to
have been committed when transfer of ownership has taken place and the village
clerk has not been notified within ten (10) working days of sale or transfer.
   D.   A person found in violation of this section shall be subject to a fine
of not less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) nor more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). In addition to fines the chairman of the water
and sewer committee may order the discontinuation of water and sewer services
to the property. (Ord. 675-06, 1-8-2007, eff. 3-1-2007)
7-2D-4: BILLING PROCEDURE:
All water, sewer and garbage 1  bills will be mailed on January 20, April 20,
July 20 and October 20. All sums are due and payable at the Franklin Grove Bank
no later than the fifth day of the month following mailing. All bills not paid
by their due date will be assessed a late penalty in the amount of ten percent
(10%) of the total amount owed on the bill. All bills not paid within thirty
(30) days of the date the bill was mailed will be subject to termination and
once the water, sewer and garbage service is terminated, such services will not
be restored until the other provisions of this article are fulfilled, including
payment of the bill and all penalties. (Ord. 517, 7-7-1986; amd. Ord. 662-05,
11-14-2005)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 4, chapter 2 of this code.
7-2D-5: DISPOSITION OF REVENUES:
   A.   Funds To Be Kept Separate: All revenues and monies derived from the
operation of the combined waterworks and sewerage system shall be held by the
village clerk separate and apart from his private funds and separate and apart
from all other funds of the village, and all of said sums, without any
deductions whatsoever, shall be delivered to the village treasurer not more
than ten (10) days after receipt of the same, or at such more frequent
intervals as may from time to time be directed by the village president and
board of trustees.
   B.   Waterworks And Sewerage Fund: The village treasurer shall receive all
such revenues from the combined waterworks and sewerage system and all the
funds and monies incident to the operation of such system as the same may be
delivered to him and deposit the same in a separate fund designated as the
waterworks and sewerage fund of the village and the treasurer shall administer
such fund in every respect in the manner provided by the provisions of the
Illinois municipal code 1 . (Ord. 395B, 6-1-1959)
 
Notes
1 2. 65 ILCS 5/11-139 et seq.
7-2D-6: BOOKS AND ACCOUNTS:
The village treasurer shall establish a proper system of accounts and shall
keep proper books, records and accounts in which complete and correct entries
shall be made of all transactions relative to the combined waterworks and
sewerage system, and at regular annual intervals he shall cause to be made an
audit by an independent auditing concern of the books to show the receipts and
disbursements of the combined waterworks and sewerage system. (Ord. 395B, 6-1-
1959)
7-2D-7: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The president and board of trustees are hereby authorized to make such rules
and regulations consistent with this article for the connection and charges to
the waterworks and sewerage system and for garbage charges, and also specifying
penalties for failure to pay the assessed fees. (Ord. 517, 7-7-1986)
7-2D-8: ENFORCEMENT:
A copy of this article, properly certified by the village clerk, shall be filed
in the office of the recorder of deeds of Lee County, and shall be deemed
notice to all owners of real estate of their liability for service supplied to
any user of the service of the combined waterworks, sewerage and garbage system
of the village on their properties, and it shall be the duty of the village
clerk and such other officers of the village to take all action necessary or
required by the laws of the state thereunto enabling to file all claims and
liens for money due to the village and to prosecute and enforce such claims in
the manner, form and time as permitted by laws of the state. (Ord. 517, 7-7-
1986)
TITLE 8
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE C. BEES
SECTION:
5-1C-1: Keeping Bees Prohibited
5-1C-2: Beehives Declared A Nuisance
5-1C-3: Penalty
5-1C-1: KEEPING BEES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to keep or harbor any bees in the village. (Ord. 445, 8-7-
1972)
5-1C-2: BEEHIVES DECLARED A NUISANCE:
Any beehive used or occupied by bees is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and
it shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any such hive in the village. (Ord.
445, 8-7-1972)
5-1C-3: PENALTY:
Whoever shall be guilty of keeping or harboring bees or keeping or maintaining
any beehive in violation of this article, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 445, 8-7-1972)
CHAPTER 2
DANGEROUS BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES
SECTION:
8-2-1: Dangerous Conditions To Be Remedied; Appeals
8-2-2: Notice Of Dangerous Condition Served
8-2-3: Failure To Comply
8-2-4: Penalties
8-2-1: DANGEROUS CONDITIONS TO BE REMEDIED; APPEALS:
   A.   Whenever the chief of the fire protection district or any officer or
member thereof shall find any building or other structure in the village which
shall have been damaged by fire, decay or otherwise, to the extent of fifty
percent (50%) of the value thereof or which, for want of proper repair or by
reason of age and dilapidated condition, defective or poorly installed electric
wiring and equipment, defective chimneys, defective gas connections, defective
heating apparatus, or for any cause, is especially liable for fire and which is
so situated as to endanger other buildings or property, or so occupied that
fire would endanger persons or property therein, such officer shall order and
direct the owner or occupant thereof to repair or tear down, demolish and
remove such building or structure and to remedy all dangerous conditions
existing on said premises.
   B.   If such officer shall find in any building or upon any premises or
other place, combustible material or explosive matter, or dangerous
accumulation of rubbish, unnecessary accumulation of wastepaper, boxes,
shavings, or any other inflammable materials especially liable to fire and
which is so situated as to endanger property or shall find obstructions to or
on fire escapes, stairs, passageways, doors or windows, liable to interfere
with the operations of the fire protection district, or egress of occupants in
case of fire, such officer shall order and direct the same to be removed or
remedied, and such order shall forthwith be complied with by the owner or
occupant of such building or premises.
Provided, however, that if said occupant or owner shall deem himself aggrieved
by such order, he may within twenty four (24) hours, appeal to the village
president of the board of trustees who shall within ten (10) days investigate
the cause of complaint and review such order and file his decision thereon, and
unless the order is revoked or modified it shall remain in full force and be
forthwith complied with by said owner or occupant. (Ord. 225, 4-5-1915)
8-2-2: NOTICE OF DANGEROUS CONDITION SERVED:
The service of any such order shall be made upon the occupant of the premises
to whom it is directed by either delivering a true copy of the same to such
occupant personally or by delivering the same to and leaving it with any person
in charge of the premises, or in case no such person is found upon the
premises, by affixing a copy thereof in a conspicuous place on the door of the
entrance of said premises. Whenever it may be necessary to serve such an order
upon the owner of the premises, such order may be served either by delivering
to and leaving with the said person a true copy of the said order or, if such
owner is absent from the jurisdiction of the officer making the order, by
mailing such copy to the owner's last post office address. (Ord. 225, 4-5-1915)
8-2-3: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
An owner or occupant failing to comply with such order within ten (10) days
after said appeal shall have been determined or, if no appeal is taken, than
within ten (10) days after the service of said order, shall be liable to a
penalty as hereinafter stated. (Ord. 225, 4-5-1915)
8-2-4: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter or any of its
sections shall, upon conviction, forfeit and pay a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 225, 4-5-1915)
TITLE 9
ZONING
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS 1
SECTION:
9-1-1: Short Title
9-1-2: Interpretation
9-1-3: Zoning Map
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/11-13-1 et seq.
9-1-1: SHORT TITLE:
The ordinance codified in this title shall be known and may be cited as the
ZONING CODE FOR THE VILLAGE OF FRANKLIN GROVE, LEE COUNTY, ILLINOIS. (Ord. 609,
4-9-2001)
9-1-2: INTERPRETATION:
In their interpretation and applications, the provisions of this title shall be
held to be minimum requirements, adopted for the promotion of the public
health, morals, safety, or the general welfare. Wherever the requirements of
any other lawfully adopted rules, regulations or ordinances are at variance
with the requirements of this title the most restrictive, or that imposing the
higher standards, shall govern. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-1-3: ZONING MAP:
The current zoning map is on file in the village clerk's office at the village
hall. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
9-2-1: Generally
9-2-2: Definitions
9-2-1: GENERALLY:
Except where specifically defined herein, all words used in this title shall
carry their customary meanings. Words used in the present tense include the
future, and the plural includes the singular; "lot" includes "plot";
"buildings" includes "structure"; "shall" is intended to be mandatory;
"occupied" or "used" shall be considered as though followed by the words "or
intended, arranged or designed to be used or occupied". (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
ALLEY: A public service way providing a secondary means of access to abutting
properties.
APARTMENT HOUSE: A building arranged, intended or designed to be occupied by
three (3) or more families living independently of each other.
AREA, BUILDING: The total of areas taken on a horizontal plane at the main
grade level of the principal building and all accessory buildings exclusive of
uncovered porches, terraces and steps.
AREA HABITABLE: The building area minus square footage occupied by interior
partitions and exterior walls.
AREA, NET SITE: The total area within the property lines excluding exterior
streets.
AUTO WRECKING YARD: Any place where two (2) or more motor vehicles not in
running condition, or parts thereof, are stored in the open.
BASEMENT: A story partly underground, but having more than half its clear
height below finished grade.
BOARDING HOUSE: A private dwelling in which at least three (3), but not more
than six (6) rooms are offered for rent and table board is furnished only to
roomers, and in which no transients are accommodated.
BUILDING: Any structure having a roof supported by columns or by walls
permanently attached to the ground and intended for the shelter, housing or
enclosure of persons, animals or chattels.
BUILDING, ACCESSORY: A subordinate building or portion of the main building on
a lot, the use of which is customarily incidental to that of the main or
principal building.
BUILDING, DETACHED: A building surrounded by open space on the same lot.
BUILDING, FRONT LINE OF: The line of that face of the building nearest the
front line of the lot. This face includes sun parlors and covered, enclosed
porches, but does not include steps.
BUILDING, HEIGHT OF: The vertical distance measured from the average elevation
of the proposed finished grade at the front of the building to the highest
point of the roof for flat roofs, to the deck line of mansard roofs, and the
mean height between eaves and ridge for gable, hip and gambrel roofs.
BUILDING, PRINCIPAL: A building in which is conducted the main or principal use
of the lot on which the building is situated.
CAMP: Any area of land or water on which are located two (2) or more cabins,
trailers, tents, shelters, houseboats or other accommodations of a design or
character suitable for seasonal living purposes of other more or less temporary
living purposes, regardless of whether such structure or other accommodations
actually are occupied seasonally or otherwise.
CAMP TRAILER: A land or floor area occupied or designed for occupancy by two
(2) or more trailers or camp cars in use for living purposes.
CAMPING GROUND: A parcel of land used or intended to be used, let or rented for
occupancy by campers or for occupancy by or of trailers, tents or movable or
temporary dwellings, rooms or sleeping quarters of any kind.
COURT: An open unoccupied space bounded on two (2) or more sides by the
exterior walls and lot lines.
COURT, AUTO: A building or group of buildings, whether detached or in connected
units, used as individual sleeping or dwelling units designed primarily for
transient automobile travelers and providing for accessory off street parking
facilities. "Auto court" includes buildings designated as tourist courts, motor
lodges, motels and similar appellations.
COURT, INNER: A court enclosed on all sides by exterior walls of a building or
by exterior walls and lot lines on which walls are allowable.
COVERAGE: That percentage of the plot or lot area covered by the building area.
CURB LEVEL: The officially established grade of the curb in front of the
midpoint of the lot.
DUMP: A lot or land or part thereof used primarily for the disposal of waste
material of any kind.
DWELLING: A building designed or used as the living quarters of one or more
families. "Dwelling", "one-family dwelling", "multiple dwelling", "two-family
dwelling", or "dwelling group" shall not be deemed to include auto court,
rooming house or tourist home.
DWELLING, MULTI-FAMILY: A dwelling or group of dwellings on one plot containing
separate living units for three (3) or more families, but which may have joint
services or facilities or both.
DWELLING, ONE-FAMILY: A detached building designed for or occupied exclusively
by one family.
DWELLING, TWO-FAMILY: A detached building containing two (2) dwelling units.
EFFICIENCY, APARTMENT HOUSE: An apartment house in which the minimum dwelling
area shall be five hundred (500) square feet and which may house no more than
two (2) adults and one child under twelve (12) years of age in each dwelling
unit.
FAMILY: One or more persons occupying a dwelling unit and living as a single,
nonprofit housekeeping unit.
FARM: Any parcel of land containing at least ten (10) acres which is used for
gain in the raising of agricultural products, livestock, poultry and dairy
products. It includes necessary farm structures within the prescribed limits
and the storage of equipment used. It excludes the raising of furbearing
animals, riding academies, livery or boarding stables and dog kennels.
FILLING STATION: Any area of land, including the structures thereon, that is
used or designed to be used for the supply of gasoline or oil or other fuel for
the propulsion of motor vehicles and which may include facilities for cleaning
or servicing such motor vehicles.
FIRE HAZARD: Any area of land, including the structures thereon, that is used
or intended to be used for manufacturing processes of, or the storage use or
manufacture of materials or products of combustible nature. Such uses include,
but are not limited to, ammunition storage, bakeries, building material
establishment, cleaning plants, coal and coke yards, contractor's plant or
storage yards, foundries or forges, feed establishments, freight yards or
terminals, junkyards, laundries, lumberyards, paint stores and shops,
potteries, paper storage, welding shops, warehouses, wholesale houses and the
storage, use or manufacture of explosive gases, liquids or solids.
FLOOR AREA OF A BUILDING: The sum of the gross horizontal areas of the several
floors of a building and its accessory buildings on the same lot, excluding
basement floor areas not devoted to residential use, but including the area of
roofed porches and roofed terraces. All dimensions shall be measured between
exterior faces of walls.
GARAGE: An accessory building intended or designed to be used for the storage
of noncommercial motor vehicles. "Garage" includes the term "carport".
GARAGE, PUBLIC: Any garage not a private garage, and which is used for storage
or servicing of motor vehicles.
GASOLINE STATION: Any area of land, including structures thereon, that is used
for the sale of gasoline or other motor vehicle fuel and oil and other
lubricating substances, accessories, and which may or may not include
facilities for lubricating, washing or otherwise servicing motor vehicles.
GRADE, ESTABLISHED: The elevation of the centerline of the streets as
officially established by the village authorities.
GRADE, FINISHED: The completed surfaces of lawns, walks, and roads brought to
grades shown on official plans or designs relating thereto.
GREENBELT PLANTING STRIP: A cultivated strip of ground of width specified and
planted with such plant materials that will, at maturity, grow to an average
height or greater than the specified height.
HOME OCCUPATION: Any use customarily conducted entirely within a dwelling and
carried on by the inhabitants thereof, which use is clearly incidental and
secondary to the use of the dwelling for dwelling purposes and does not change
the character thereof. The conducting of a clinic, hospital, barbershop, beauty
parlor, tea room, tourist home, animal hospital or any similar use shall not be
a home occupation. Such home occupations, where permitted in a residential
district of any zoning type, shall be subject to the following conditions:
   A.   The occupation shall be conducted wholly within the principal building;
   B.   Only persons residing within the dwelling unit shall be employed in the
occupation;
   C.   No equipment shall be used in the occupation, other than that which is
customarily incidental to domestic use;
   D.   No outdoor storage in conjunction with the occupation shall be allowed;
   E.   No exterior display or exterior sign shall be permitted, except as
allowed by the sign regulations for each district;
   F.   No alterations of any kind shall be made to the dwelling which changes
its residential character;
   G.   No equipment or material or compounds used in such occupation shall be
of a dangerous, hazardous, poisonous, noxious or like nature.
HOSPITAL: A building used for the diagnosis, treatment or other care of human
ailments, unless otherwise specified.
HOTEL: A building containing rooms intended or designed to be used, rented or
hired out to be occupied or which are occupied for sleeping purposed by guests
and where only a general kitchen and dining room are provided within the
building or in an accessory building.
HOUSE TRAILER: Any portable or mobile vehicle used or designed to be used for
living purposes and with its wheels, rollers or skids in place.
JUNKYARD: Lot, land or structure, or part thereof, used primarily for the
collecting, storage and sale of wastepaper, rags, scrap metal or discarded
material; or for the collecting, dismantling, storage and salvaging of
machinery or vehicles not in running condition, and for the sale of parts
thereof.
LAUNDERETTE: A business premises equipped with individual clothes washing
machines for use of retail customers, exclusive of laundry facilities provided
as an accessory use in an apartment house or an apartment hotel.
LOADING SPACE, OFF STREET: A unit being ten feet (10') wide, thirty feet (30')
long and fourteen feet (14') high located within the structure, or within a
side or rear yard or within an access drive or aisle of a required off street
parking space.
LODGING HOUSE: A building in which two (2) or more rooms are rented and in
which no table board is furnished.
LOT: A parcel of land occupied or capable of being occupied by one building,
and the accessory buildings or uses customarily incident to it, including such
open spaces as are required by this title.
LOT, CORNER: A parcel of land at the junction of and fronting on two (2) or
more intersecting streets.
LOT DEPTH: A mean horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines,
measured in the general direction of its side lot lines.
LOT, INTERIOR: A lot other than a corner lot.
LOT LINES: The lines bounding a "lot" as defined in this section.
LOT WIDTH: The mean width measured at right angles to its depth.
MOTOR VEHICLE, REPAIR SHOP: A building, or portion of a building, arranged,
intended or designed to be used for making repairs to motor vehicles.
NURSING OR CONVALESCENT HOME: Any dwelling where persons are housed or lodged
and furnished with meals and nursing care for hire.
OPEN SPACE: An unoccupied space open to the sky on the same lot with the
building.
PARKING SPACE, OFF STREET: Each unit being eight feet (8') wide and twenty feet
(20') long exclusive of access drives and turning areas, located within an
accessory garage or in a side or rear yard, properly graveled, or paved and
maintained.
PLAT: A map, plan or layout of a parcel or parcels of land, indicating the
location and boundaries of individual properties.
SIGN: Any device for visual communication that is used for the purpose of
bringing the subject thereof to the attention of the public, but not including
any flag, badge or insignia of any government or government agency, or of any
civic, charitable, religious, patriotic, fraternal or similar organization.
STREET: A public way which affords principal means of access to abutting
property.
STREET GRADE: The officially established grade of the street upon which a lot
fronts or in its absence the established grade of other street upon which the
lot abuts, at the midpoint of the frontage of the lot thereon. If there is no
officially established grade, the existing grade of the street at such midpoint
shall be taken as the street grade.
STREET LINE: The dividing line between the street and the lot.
STRUCTURE: A combination of materials other than a building to form a
construction that is safe and stable and includes among other things platforms,
bleachers, towers, bins, fences and display signs.
TOURIST HOME: A dwelling in which overnight accommodations are provided or
offered for a transient guest for compensation.
TRAILER: See definition of House Trailer.
USE, ACCESSORY: A use incidental to the principal use of a building. In
buildings restricted to residence use, the office of a professional man,
customary family occupations and workshops not conducted for compensation shall
be deemed accessory uses.
USE, MANUFACTURING: Any building or lot used for making articles or products
and employing more than four (4) persons or consuming more than sixty (60) man
hours per week for manufacturing purposes.
USE, NONCONFORMING: A building, structure or use of land existing at the time
of enactment of the ordinance codified in this title, and which does not
conform to the regulations of the district or zone in which it is situated.
YARD: An unoccupied space open to the sky, on the same lot with a building or
structure.
YARD, FRONT: A yard on the same lot with the building between the front line of
the building and the front line of the lot and extending the full width of the
lot. As used in this title "front yard" applies to all buildings on the lot.
YARD, REAR: A yard on the same lot with the building between the rear line of
the building and the rear line of the lot and extending the full width of the
lot. As used in this title "rear yard" applies to principal buildings only.
YARD, SIDE: A yard on the same lot with the building situated between the
building and the side line of the lot and extending from the front yard to the
rear yard. Any lot line not a rear line or a front line shall be deemed a side
line. As used in this title "side yard" applies to principal buildings only.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 3
PLAN COMMISSION 1
SECTION:
9-3-1: Creation
9-3-2: Membership
9-3-3: Powers And Duties
9-3-4: Comprehensive Plan, Applicability
9-3-5: Comprehensive Plan, Procedures And Provisions
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/11-12-4 et seq.
9-3-1: CREATION:
A plan commission is hereby created. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-3-2: MEMBERSHIP:
Membership shall be as follows:
   A.   The plan commission shall consist of a chairman and six (6) other
members who shall be appointed by the village president and confirmed by the
village board. Initially, the village president shall appoint the chairman and
two (2) members for three (3) year terms, two (2) members for two (2) year
terms and two (2) members for one year terms. Thereafter, each successive
member and chairman shall serve two (2) year terms, unless appointed to serve
the remaining unexpired term of a member or chairman, and shall serve until
their successors have been appointed and qualified.
   B.   Members of the plan commission must reside within the corporate limits
of the village or within one and one-half (11/2) miles of such corporate
limits. At no time shall more than three (3) members of the plan commission
reside outside the corporate limits of the village. The chairman of the plan
commission must reside within the village's corporate limits. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
9-3-3: POWERS AND DUTIES:
The plan commission shall have the following powers:
   A.   To prepare and recommend to the village board a comprehensive plan for
the present and future development or redevelopment of the village. Such plan
may be adopted in whole or in separate geographical or functional parts, each
of which, when adopted, shall be the official comprehensive plan, or part
thereof, of the village. This plan may include reasonable requirements with
reference to streets, alleys, public grounds, and other improvements. The plan,
as recommended by the plan commission, and as thereafter adopted by the
village, may be made applicable, by the terms thereof, to land situated within
the corporate limits, and contiguous territory not more than one and one-half
(11/2) miles beyond the corporate limits, and not included in any other
municipality of this state.
      1.   Such plan may be implemented by recommendations for ordinances to be
adopted by the village, establishing reasonable standards of design for
subdivision and for re subdivisions of unimproved land, and of areas subject to
redevelopment in respect to public improvements. The plan may also establish
reasonable requirements governing the location, width, course, and surfacing of
public streets and highways, alleys, ways of public service facilities, curbs,
gutters, sidewalks, streetlights, parks, playgrounds, school grounds, size of
lots to be used for residential purposes, storm water drainage, water supply
and distribution, sanitary sewers, and sewage collection and treatment.
      2.   The plan may designate land suitable for annexation to the
municipality, and the recommended zoning classification for such land upon
annexation.
      3.   In the event that the plan is adopted by the village, the plan
commission may from time to time recommend changes thereof to the village
board;
   B.   To prepare and recommend to the village board, from time to time, plans
for specific improvements in pursuance of the official comprehensive plan;
   C.   To give aid to the municipal officials charged with the direction of
projects for improvements embraced within the official plan, to further the
making of such projects, and, generally to promote the realization of the
official comprehensive plan;
   D.   To exercise such other powers, consistent and germane to other powers,
granted by this chapter, and as may be conferred by amendment by the village
board from time to time.
   E.   To review all applications for amendment to the zoning code pursuant to
section
9-14-16 of this title and, prior to the public hearing before the village's
zoning board of appeals on such amendment, make a recommendation to the board
of appeals and the village board as to such application for amendment. (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-3-4: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN, APPLICABILITY:
The official comprehensive plan or any amendments thereof or additions thereto
proposed by the plan commission shall be effective in the village limits and
contiguous area only after its formal adoption by the village board. Such plan
shall be advisory and of itself shall not be construed to regulate or control
the use of private property in any way except as to such part thereof as has
been implemented by ordinances duly enacted by the village board. (Ord. 609, 4-
9-2001)
9-3-5: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN, PROCEDURES AND PROVISIONS:
   A.   The mayor and village board may initiate plans and maps by requesting
the plan commission to prepare an official comprehensive plan and recommend the
same, or may originate an official comprehensive plan, or a part thereof, or an
amendment thereto, and may refer same or suggested changes in an existing
comprehensive plan to the plan commission for its consideration and
recommendation thereon.
   B.   The village board may adopt parts of a comprehensive plan
recommendation by the plan commission without adopting the entire comprehensive
plan as recommended, or may modify or amend portions of a recommended
comprehensive plan without a rereference of same to the plan commission and may
adopt such comprehensive plan, as modified or amended. Such comprehensive plan,
when adopted, shall be the official comprehensive plan, or part thereof, of the
village.
   C.   Upon submission by the village board of any suggested comprehensive
plan, part thereof, or amendment to an existing comprehensive plan to the plan
commission for consideration and recommendation, the village board may require
a report thereon from the plan commission with its recommendation within ninety
(90) days from the date of such submission, and if the plan commission shall
fail to make such report within such ninety (90) days, then the village board
may proceed to consider such comprehensive plan, part thereof, or amendment to
an existing comprehensive plan, for adoption, including arranging for and
holding of a public hearing thereon in accordance with the provisions contained
in subsection D of this section in the same manner as if the plan commission
had made its recommendation.
   D.   Upon submission of a comprehensive plan by the plan commission, or a
proposed amendment to an existing comprehensive plan, the village board shall
schedule a public hearing thereon, either before the plan commission or the
village board. Not less than fifteen (15) days' notice of the proposed hearing,
and the time and place thereof, shall be given by publication in a newspaper of
general circulation in Lee County. The hearing shall be informal, but all
persons desiring to be heard in support or opposition to the comprehensive plan
or amendment shall be afforded such opportunity, and may submit their
statements orally, in writing, or both. The hearing may be recessed to another
date if not concluded, if notice of the time and place thereof is publicly
announced at the hearing or is given by newspaper publication not less than
five (5) days prior to the recessed hearing.
   E.   Within ninety (90) days after the conclusion of the hearing, the
village board, after consideration of the recommendation of the plan commission
and such information as shall have been derived from the hearing, shall either
adopt the comprehensive plan or amendment in whole or in part or reject the
entire comprehensive plan or amendment. If adopted, the village board shall
enact the ordinance including a map or maps as previously provided in this
chapter. In adopting an official comprehensive plan, the village board shall be
subject to the same limitations as to subject matter as apply to the plan
commission. If at the expiration of such ninety (90) days, the village board
has taken no formal action, the comprehensive plan or amendment thereto may
thereafter not be acted upon by the village board without again complying with
the notice and hearing conditions previously provided in subsection D of this
section.
   F.   No official map, or amendment or addition thereto, shall be grounds for
rejection of any plat of subdivision or resubdivision by the village board, if
application for final approval of such subdivision or resubdivision is filed
with the village board fifteen (15) days or more prior to the date on which the
ordinance approving the official map, or amendment or addition thereto, is
adopted.
   G.   The comprehensive plan or amendment shall become effective upon the
expiration of ten (10) days after the date of filing notice of the adoption of
such comprehensive plan or amendment with the Lee County recorder of deeds.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 4
DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED
SECTION:
9-4-1: Designation Of Districts
9-4-2: Zoning Map To Include Districts
9-4-3: Boundaries Interpretation
9-4-4: Application Of Regulations
9-4-1: DESIGNATION OF DISTRICTS:
For the purpose of promoting the public health, safety, morals and general
welfare of the village, the municipality is divided into the following types of
districts:
District no. 1 - One-family residential district
District no. 2 - Two-family residential district
District no. 3 - Multi-family residential district
District no. 4 - Highway frontage business district
District no. 5 - General business district
                C-1 Neighborhood business district
District no. 6 - Industrial district
                Historic preservation district
                Planned unit development district
 
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001; amd. Ord. 693-08, 9-10-2008)
9-4-2: ZONING MAP TO INCLUDE DISTRICTS:
The districts are bounded and defined as shown on the map entitled "zoning map
of the village of Franklin Grove, Illinois", which, with all explanatory matter
thereon, is made a part of this title. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-4-3: BOUNDARIES INTERPRETATION:
Where uncertainty exists with respect to the boundaries of any of the aforesaid
districts as shown on the zoning map, the following rules shall apply:
   A.   Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately following the
centerlines of streets or street lines, such centerline or street lines shall
be construed to be such boundaries.
   B.   Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately following the
lot lines, such lot lines shall be construed to be such boundaries.
   C.   Where district boundaries are so indicated that they are approximately
parallel to the centerlines or street lines of streets, such district
boundaries shall be construed as being parallel thereto and at such distance
therefrom as indicated on the zoning map. If no distance is given, such
dimension shall be determined by the use of the scale shown on the zoning map.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-4-4: APPLICATION OF REGULATIONS:
Except as hereinafter provided:
   A.   No building or land shall hereafter be used or occupied and no part
thereof shall be erected, moved, or altered unless in conformity with the
regulations specified in this title for the district in which it is located.
   B.   No building shall hereafter be erected or altered to:
      1.   Exceed the height;
      2.   Accommodate or house a greater number of families;
      3.   Occupy a greater percentage of lot area; or
      4.   Have narrower or smaller rear yards, front yards, side yards, inner
or outer courts than is specified in this title for the district in which such
building is located.
   C.   No part of a yard or other open space required about any building for
the purpose of complying with the provisions of this title shall be included as
part of a yard or other open space similarly required for another building.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 5
DISTRICT NO. 1 - ONE-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-5-1: Regulations Generally
9-5-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-5-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-5-4: Net Site Area
9-5-5: Coverage
9-5-6: Required Yards
9-5-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-5-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-5-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-5-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set out in this chapter shall apply in all No. 1 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
The principal permitted uses shall be:
Churches, or other places of worship, parish houses, convents and Sunday
schools.
Customary accessory uses and building, provided such uses are incidental to the
principal use and do not include any activity commonly conducted for gain. Any
accessory building shall be located on the same lot with the principal
building.
Customary agricultural operations, provided, however, that no odor or dust
producing substance or use shall be permitted within one hundred feet (100') of
any property line.
Customary home occupations, provided that any such occupation shall be
conducted in the principal building. There shall be no external evidence of
such occupations except a small announcement or professional sign not exceeding
one square foot in area, provided, that no such sign shall be illuminated.
One-family dwelling.
Public educational uses.
Public recreational uses, libraries and museums. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
Special permitted uses (see sections
9-14-1 and
9-14-2 of this title) shall be:
Cemeteries.
Hospitals.
Nonprofit cultural and recreational uses.
Parochial and private educational uses.
Public ownership uses.
Welfare uses. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-4: NET SITE AREA:
Net site area shall be not less than nine thousand (9,000) square feet and lot
width of not less than sixty six feet (66'), at the building line. (Ord. 609,
4-9-2001)
9-5-5: COVERAGE:
All buildings including accessory buildings shall not cover more than thirty
percent (30%) of the net site area. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
Each lot shall have front, side, and rear yards not less than the depths or
widths following:
   A.   Front yard depth shall be thirty feet (30') or average of established
front depth on block, whichever is less.
   B.   There shall be a side yard on each side of not less than ten percent
(10%) of the lot width, with a six foot (6') minimum, but need not exceed ten
feet (10').
      1.   Corner Lots: On corner lots there shall be maintained a side yard of
not less than twenty feet (20') on the side adjacent to the street which
intersects the street upon which the building or structure maintains frontage,
or average of established front yard depths on block, whichever is less.
      2.   Reversed Corner Lot: In the case of a reversed corner lot there
shall be maintained a setback from the side street of not less than seventy
five percent (75%) of the front yard required on the lots in the rear of such
corner lots, but such setback need not exceed thirty feet (30'), nor average of
established front yard depths on block. No accessory building on said corner
lot shall project beyond the front yard required on the adjacent lot to the
rear, nor be located nearer than six feet (6') to the side lot line of said
adjacent lot.
   C.   Rear yard depth shall be twenty five feet (25'), or as alternates:
twenty five (25) to thirty percent (30%) of the depth of the lot, or not less
than the height of the principal building. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
Height of the principal building shall not exceed two and one- half (21/2)
stories or thirty five feet (35'). (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
Accessory buildings shall not exceed fifteen feet (15') in height; not less
than ten feet (10') from the principal building if not attached to it; not less
than six feet (6') from the side lot line; not less than six feet (6') from the
rear lot line. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-5-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see chapter 13 of this title. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
CHAPTER 6
DISTRICT NO. 2 - TWO-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-6-1: Regulations Generally
9-6-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-6-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-6-4: Net Site Area
9-6-5: Coverage
9-6-6: Required Yards
9-6-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-6-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-6-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-6-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set forth in this chapter shall apply in all No. 2 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
Principal permitted uses shall be:
Any principal use permitted in district No. 1.
Accessory uses incident to the uses, provided such uses are incidental to the
principal use and do not include any activity commonly conducted for gain. Any
accessory building shall be located on the same lot with the principal
building.
Public ownership uses except landfills, incinerators, warehouses, storage yards
and disposal plants.
Two-family detached dwellings. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
Special permitted uses (see sections
9-14-1 and
9-14-2 of this title) shall be:
Home occupations.
Nonprofit cultural and recreational uses.
Parochial and private educational uses.
Private landfills.
Public ownership uses of any nature.
Welfare uses, hospitals and cemeteries.
Upon approval of the board of appeals acting under provisions outlined in
chapter 14 of this title, a special permit may be issued for the remodeling of
an existing structure into a two- family detached dwelling. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
9-6-4: NET SITE AREA:
Net site area shall be not less than nine thousand (9,000) square feet and lot
width of not less than sixty six feet (66'), at the building line. (Ord. 609,
4-9-2001)
9-6-5: COVERAGE:
All buildings including accessory buildings shall not cover more than thirty
percent (30%) of the net site area. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
Each lot shall have front, side and rear yards not less than the depths or
widths following:
   A.   Front yard depth shall be thirty feet (30') or average of established
front depth on block, whichever is less.
   B.   There shall be a side yard on each side of not less than ten percent
(10%) of the lot width, with a six foot (6') minimum, but need not exceed ten
feet (10').
      1.   Corner Lots: On corner lots there shall be maintained a side yard of
not less than twenty feet (20') on the side adjacent to the street which
intersects the street upon which the building or structure maintains frontage,
or average of established front yard depths on block, whichever is less.
      2.   Reversed Corner Lot: In the case of a reversed corner lot there
shall be maintained a setback from the side street of not less than seventy
five percent (75%) of the front yard required on the lots in the rear of such
corner lots, but such setback need not exceed thirty feet (30'), nor average of
established front yard depths on block. No accessory building on said corner
lot shall project beyond the front yard required on the adjacent lot to the
rear, nor be located nearer than six feet (6') to the side lot line of said
adjacent lot.
   C.   Rear yard depth shall be twenty five feet (25'), or as alternates:
twenty five (25) to thirty percent (30%) of the depth of the lot, or not less
than the height of the principal building. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
The height of the principal building shall not exceed two and one-half (21/2)
stories or thirty five feet (35'). (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
Accessory buildings shall not exceed fifteen feet (15') in height; nor be less
than fifteen feet (15') from the principal building if not attached to it; nor
be less than six feet (6') from the side lot line; nor be less than six feet
(6') from the rear lot line. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-6-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see chapter 13 of this title. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
CHAPTER 7
DISTRICT NO. 3 - MULTI-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-7-1: Regulations Generally
9-7-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-7-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-7-4: Net Site Area
9-7-5: Coverage
9-7-6: Required Yards
9-7-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-7-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-7-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-7-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set forth in this chapter shall apply in all No. 3 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
Principal permitted uses shall be:
Any principal use permitted in district No. 2.
Multi-family dwellings not exceeding four (4) dwelling units, efficiency
apartment houses, which shall contain no less than four (4) units per site and
no less than three (3) units per building. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
Special permitted uses (see sections
9-14-1 and
9-14-2 of this title) shall be:
All special permitted uses given for district No. 2.
Accessory uses.
Barbershops and beauty shops.
Boarding houses not conducted for gain, public service substations and
telephone exchanges.
Flower shops and greenhouses.
Funeral homes.
Multi-family dwellings exceeding four (4) dwelling units.
Real estate and insurance offices.
Transit passenger stations. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-4: NET SITE AREA:
No dwelling shall be established on a lot having an area or width less than
specified for district No. 2; provided, however, that each dwelling shall be
located on a lot having an area of not less than one thousand (1,000) square
feet for each family housed therein. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-5: COVERAGE:
All buildings including accessory buildings shall not cover more than forty
percent (40%) of the area of the lot. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
Yards of the following minimum depths shall be provided:
   A.   Front yard depth shall be thirty feet (30').
   B.   Side yards shall be one-third (1/3) the height of the building.
   C.   Rear yard depth shall be equal to the height of the building. (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
The height of the principal building may be three (3) stories, but not
exceeding forty feet (40'). (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
Accessory buildings shall not exceed fifteen feet (15') in height; nor be less
than twenty five feet (25') from principal building if not attached to it; nor
be less than six feet (6') from side lot line; nor be less than six feet (6')
from rear lot line, except that one-family dwellings and two-family detached
dwellings established in this district shall have accessory uses subject to
those regulations given in district No. 2. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-7-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see also chapter 13 of this title.
   A.   Distance Between Buildings On Same Plot: No principal building shall be
closer to any other principal building than the average of the heights of the
buildings.
   B.   Required Inner Court Dimension: The least dimension of an inner court
shall be not less than the full height of the walls enclosing such court, but
not less than fifty feet (50'). Each inner court shall have an open and
unobstructed passageway at grade level sufficient to permit the passage of fire
equipment. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 8
DISTRICT NO. 4 - HIGHWAY FRONTAGE BUSINESS DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-8-1: Regulations Generally
9-8-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-8-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-8-4: Net Site Area
9-8-5: Coverage
9-8-6: Required Yards
9-8-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-8-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-8-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-8-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set forth in this chapter shall apply to all No. 4 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
Principal permitted uses shall be:
All uses permitted in district No. 3 subject to all the provisions specified
for that district.
Drive-in refreshment stands.
Farm implement establishments including outdoor storage of vehicles for sale or
hire.
Garages and filling stations upon approval of the board of appeals and subject
to such conditions and safeguards as deemed appropriate by such board and upon
securing a permit therefor.
Motels and hotels.
New and/or used car sales establishments.
Restaurants.
Taverns.
Garages, filling stations and farm implement establishments are subject to the
following provisions;
   A.   No repair work is performed out of doors;
   B.   Pumps, lubricating or other devices are located at least thirty feet
(30') from the right of way of State Route No. 38 and at least twenty feet
(20') from any other street line;
   C.   All fuel, oil or similar substances are stored at least thirty five
feet (35') distant from any street or lot line.
   D.   All automobile parts, dismantled vehicles and similar articles are
stored within a building. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
Special permitted uses shall be any other uses which, in the opinion of the
board of appeals, are of the same general character as those listed as
principal permitted uses and which will not be detrimental to the district in
which they are located. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-4: NET SITE AREA:
The net site area shall not be less than four thousand eight hundred (4,800)
square feet and lot width shall not be less than sixty six feet (66'), at the
building line. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-5: COVERAGE:
All buildings including accessory buildings shall not cover more than forty
percent (40%) of the area of the lot. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
Each lot shall have front, side and rear yards not less than the following
depths:
   A.   Front yard depth shall be forty feet (40').
   B.   Each side yard shall be fifteen feet (15').
   C.   Rear yard shall be twenty five feet (25'). (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
The height of the principal building shall not exceed forty feet (40'). (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-8-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
Accessory building regulations are the same as district No. 3. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
9-8-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see chapter 13 of this title. Front and side
yards may be used for automobile parking. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 9
DISTRICT NO. 5 - GENERAL BUSINESS DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-9-1: Regulations Generally
9-9-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-9-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-9-4: Net Site Area
9-9-5: Coverage
9-9-6: Required Yards
9-9-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-9-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-9-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-9-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set forth in this chapter shall apply in all No. 5 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
Principal permitted uses shall be:
All uses permitted in district No. 4 subject to all the provisions specified
for that district except that new constructions for one-family detached and
two-family detached dwellings is not permitted.
Accessory buildings and accessory uses.
Animal hospitals and kennels, provided, that the animal hospitals and kennels
are reasonably soundproof and have only covered inside runs for the animals.
Banks, offices, studios.
Personal service shops, hand laundries.
Shops for custom work.
Shops for making articles or products to be sold at retail on the premises,
except manufacturing uses are not permitted.
Stores and shops for the conducting of any retail business.
Theaters, assembly halls, billiard or pool parlors, bowling alley.
Wholesale businesses, storage in bulk of, or warehouse for such material as:
Building material,
Clothing,
Contractor's equipment,
Cotton,
Drugs,
Dry goods,
Feed,
Food,
Furniture,
Hardware,
Ice,
Machinery,
Metals,
Oil and petroleum in quantities less than tank car lots,
Paint and paint supplies,
Pipe,
Rubber,
Shop supplies,
Tobacco or wood. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
Special permitted uses (see
9-14-1 and
9-14-2 of this title) shall be any other uses which in the opinion of the board

permitted uses and which will not be detrimental to the district in which they
are located. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-4: NET SITE AREA:
Any building used for residence on the first floor shall have a lot area and
lot width equal to that required in district No. 3. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-5: COVERAGE:
Any building used for residence on the first floor, and including accessory
buildings, shall not cover more than forty percent (40%) of the area of the
lot. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
   A.   Any building used for residence of the first floor shall have front,
side and rear yards not less than those specified for district no. 4.
   B.   Any building used for any other use as permitted above shall have
front, side and rear yards not less than the following depths:
      1.   Front Yard Depth:
         a.   For lots fronting on State Route 38: Forty feet (40');
         b.   For lots fronting on all other streets in this district: No front
yard required; (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
      2.   Side And Rear Yards: None required, excepting that where the general
business district adjoins a residential district, a minimum side and rear yard
of six feet (6') is required. (Ord. 642-03, 11-10-2003)
9-9-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
The height of the principal building shall not exceed forty feet (40'). (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
There are no accessory building regulations requirements. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-9-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see chapter 13 of this title. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
CHAPTER 9A
DISTRICT C-1 - NEIGHBORHOOD BUSINESS DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-9A-1: Neighborhood Business District
9-9A-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-9A-3: Special Uses
9-9A-1: NEIGHBORHOOD BUSINESS DISTRICT:
The neighborhood business district is established to provide a location for a
limited range of daily convenience oriented businesses and services principally
relying upon the patronage from the immediate surrounding neighborhoods in
appropriate locations in the village. The map symbol and short name for this
district shall be C-1 district. (Ord. 693-08, 9-10-2008)
9-9A-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
The following businesses shall be considered permitted uses in this
classification:
Apparel shop.
Art and school supply store.
Art gallery, studio.
Bakery shop, including the baking and processing of food products (when
prepared for retail use on the property only).
Barber shop, beauty parlor, or similar personal service shop.
Book and stationery store.
Candy and ice cream shops.
Custom dressmaking or tailoring or shoe sales or repair when conducted for
retail sales on the premises only.
Florist shop and conservatory for retail trade on the premises only.
Food and fruit stores.
Gift shops.
Jewelry store and watch repair.
Offices (i.e., medical clinic, insurance, law, psychologist, chiropractic,
optometrist, physician, administrative).
Restaurants, tearoom and cafe (when the establishment is not of the drive-in
type where food is served to occupants remaining in motor vehicles and fast
food restaurants).
Toy store.
Travel bureau and transportation ticket office.
Water pumping stations. (Ord. 693-08, 9-10-2008)
9-9A-3: SPECIAL USES:
Additional businesses may be considered as special uses and as such shall be
reviewed by the zoning board of appeals for appropriateness prior to such
classification. (Ord. 693-08, 9-10-2008)
CHAPTER 10
DISTRICT NO. 6 - INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-10-1: Regulations Generally
9-10-2: Principal Permitted Uses
9-10-3: Special Permitted Uses
9-10-4: Net Site Area
9-10-5: Coverage
9-10-6: Required Yards
9-10-7: Height Of Principal Building
9-10-8: Accessory Building Regulations
9-10-9: Supplementary Regulations
9-10-1: REGULATIONS GENERALLY:
The regulations set forth in this chapter shall apply in all No. 6 districts.
(Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-2: PRINCIPAL PERMITTED USES:
Principal permitted uses shall be:
Any use except auto wrecking yards, junk yards, open storage of junk and other
waste products or a structure used for dwelling purposes; provided, however,
the use complies with the following provisions:
   A.   Review By The Board Of Appeals: To assure compliance with provisions of
this title as they apply to this district, all plans and specifications of
proposed uses in this district must be submitted to the board of appeals for
their review prior to issuance of permit by enforcing official.
   B.   Noise And Shock: Any machines, presses, breaks, forges, hammers and
similar constructions shall be placed on suitable shock absorbing mountings and
on suitable, reinforced concrete footings; shall be muffled so as not to become
objectionable due to intermittence, beat frequency or shrillness; shall not be
loaded beyond capacity as prescribed by the manufacturer.
   C.   Glare And Heat: Any processes emitting glare and heat shall be
performed so as not to be seen from any point beyond the outside of the
property.
   D.   Smoke And Dirt: Smoke and dirt shall not exceed 0.3 grains per cubic
foot of flue gas at stack temperature of five hundred degrees Fahrenheit
(500°F), nor shall smoke emitted to atmosphere be more dense than Ringlemann
no. 1 for periods aggregating four (4) minutes in any thirty (30) minutes.
   E.   Odor And Gases: The emission of obnoxious odors of any kind shall not
be permitted nor shall any gas be emitted which is deleterious to the public
health, safety or general welfare.
   F.   Fire And Safety Hazards:
      1.   All tanks providing storage of flammable liquids aboveground shall
be located not less than one hundred feet (100') from property lines. All tanks
providing storage of flammable liquids belowground shall be located not closer
to the property line than the greatest depth to the bottom of the buried tank.
      2.   The storage of rags, wastepaper or similar products of combustible
nature, when enclosed in a building shall be enclosed in a building of four (4)
hours' construction, no part of which may be located closer than one hundred
feet (100') from any property line.
   G.   Open Storage: All such storage shall be enclosed within a tight,
unpierced fence made of materials similar to or architecturally compatible with
the construction materials of the principal building and not less than six feet
(6') in height, or enclosed within a greenbelt planting strip not less than six
feet (6') in width, and not less than six feet (6') in height, to normally
screen from view of stockpiles from any outside street; all fences are subject
to yard requirements of accessory buildings listed in section
9-10-8 of this chapter. The storage of lumber, coal or other combustible
material shall be provided with a roadway, graded, surfaced, and maintained
from the street to the rear of the storage area to permit free access of fire
trucks at any time.
   H.   Sewage Waste: No wastes shall be discharged in the public sewer system
which are dangerous to the public health and safety. Acidity or alkalinity
shall be neutralized to a pH of 7.0 as a daily average on a volumetric basis,
with a temporary variation of pH 5.0 to 10.0. Wastes shall contain no cyanides
and no halogens, and shall contain not more than ten (10) ppm of the following
gases: hydrogen sulfide, sulfur dioxide, and nitrous oxide. Wastes shall not
contain any insoluble substance in excess of ten thousand (10,000) ppm or
exceed a daily average of five hundred (500) ppm or fail to pass a No. 8
standard sieve, or have a dimension greater than one-half inch (1/2"). Wastes
shall not have a chlorine demand greater than fifteen (15) ppm. Wastes shall
not contain phenols in excess of 0.005 ppm. Wastes shall not contain any grease
or oil or any oily substance in excess of one hundred (100) ppm or exceed a
daily average of twenty five (25) ppm. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-3: SPECIAL PERMITTED USES:
For special permitted uses (see sections
9-14-1 and
9-14-2 of this chapter) see principal permitted uses in section
9-10-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-4: NET SITE AREA:
Net site area shall be of any area to satisfy requirements of coverage yards,
parking and other portions of this title which apply to this district. (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-5: COVERAGE:
All buildings including accessory buildings shall not cover more than thirty
percent (30%) of the net site area. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-6: REQUIRED YARDS:
   A.   Yard Depths: Each lot shall have front, side and rear yards not less
than the following depths:
      1.   Front Yards: Front yard depth shall be fifty feet (50').
      2.   Side Yards And Rear Yards:
         a.   Where yard abuts a zoning district other than industrial: Forty
feet (40');
         b.   Where yard abuts street other than street on which use fronts:
Thirty feet (30');
         c.   Where yard abuts another industrial use: Twenty feet (20');
         d.   Where yard abuts railroad right of way: None required.
   B.   Greenbelt Planting Strips: A greenbelt planting strip not less than six
feet (6') in width, and not less than six feet (6') in height shall be provided
and maintained along all zoning district boundary lines which border a more
restrictive zoning district and along all street lines except such greenbelt
planting strips may be omitted along front and side yards where such yards are
landscaped and maintained. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-7: HEIGHT OF PRINCIPAL BUILDING:
The height of the principal building shall not exceed thirty feet (30'). (Ord.
609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-8: ACCESSORY BUILDING REGULATIONS:
Accessory buildings shall be constructed of materials similar or
architecturally compatible with contraction materials of principal building;
nor be less than twenty feet (20') in height; nor be less than twenty feet
(20') from side and rear lot lines except where side and rear lot lines abut
railroad right of way, then no yards are required; and shall comply with
provisions listed under fire and safety hazards set forth in subsection 9-10-2F
of this chapter. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-10-9: SUPPLEMENTARY REGULATIONS:
For supplementary regulations see chapter 13 of this title. (Ord. 609, 4-9-
2001)
CHAPTER 11
HISTORIC PRESERVATION DISTRICT
SECTION:
9-11-1: Historic Preservation District; Purpose
9-11-2: Creation Of Historic Preservation Commission
9-11-3: Membership Of Historic Preservation Commission
9-11-4: Powers And Duties
9-11-5: Historic District Zoning Requirements
9-11-1: HISTORIC PRESERVATION DISTRICT; PURPOSE:
It is hereby stated that in the village of Franklin Grove there is to be
created an official historic preservation zoning district, the area or areas of
which shall be shown on the official village zoning map.
   A.   The purpose of the historic preservation district pursuant to division
48.2, article II of the Illinois municipal code, is to ensure the preservation
of areas, places, buildings, structures, works of art and other objects having
special historical, community, or aesthetic interest or value.
   B.   The historic preservation zoning district classification shall be
superimposed on or established in addition to other zoning district
classifications; regulations, use and other requirements shall apply as
specified. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-11-2: CREATION OF HISTORIC PRESERVATION COMMISSION:
An historic preservation commission is hereby created. (Ord. 609, 4-9-2001)
9-11-3: MEMBERSHIP OF HISTORIC PRESERVATION COMMISSION:
Membership shall be as follows:
   A.   Appointment And Terms: The historic plan commission shall consist of a
chairman and four (4) other members who shall be appointed by the village
president and confirmed by the village board. Initially, the village president
shall appoint the chairman for a three (3) year term, two (2) members for two
(2) year terms and two (2) members for one year terms. Thereafter, each
successive member and chairman shall serve two (2) year terms, unless appointed
to serve the remaining unexpired term of a member or chairman, and shall serve
until their successors have been appointed and qualified.
   B.   Residency: Members of the historic plan commission must reside within
the corporate limits of the village or within one and one- half (11/2) miles of
such corporate limits. At no time shall more than two (2) members of the plan
commission reside outside the corporate limits of the village. The chairman of
the historic plan commission must reside within the village's corporate limits.
   C.   Composition: The village president or one member of the village board
of trustees shall be an ex officio member of the commission. One member shall
be a member of the Franklin Grove area historical society, one member shall be
a member of Farming Heritage, Inc., and three (3) members shall be qualified
members of the community or surrounding contiguous area.
   D.   Removal From Office: An appointed member of the commission may be
