scope which addresses itself to the natural resources identified in the report
prepared by the Lee County soil and water conservation district, and which
determines potential ground absorption, runoff, flooding deficiencies, the
presence of unstable soils (or soils which may constitute problems for
conventional construction), the presence of subsurface rock that would affect
the installation of underground improvements on the provisions of aboveground
improvement. If, in the opinion of the village engineer, additional soil
investigations, borings or other soil tests are necessary to determine the
nature and extent of such questionable material, the subdivider shall perform
the needed investigation.
   H.   Preliminary engineering report(s) and plan(s), but not limited to the
consideration of the following:
      1.   Community or individual water facilities.
      2.   Streets and sidewalks.
      3.   Site grading and erosion and siltation control.
      4.   Storm sewers and drainage plan for the storage and controlled
release of storm water following a 100-year frequency storm. (The design
standards shall be according to those contained in the specifications for
required improvements, storm water control, on file with the village engineer.)
      5.   Community or waste water facilities. In areas where septic systems
are to be anticipated for the proposed method of waste disposal, evidence shall
be presented to indicate the suitability of soil for the purpose of septic
waste simulation.
   I.   Evidence of ownership of the land proposed to be subdivided. Where the
subdivider does not own such land, written notarized permission from the owner
shall be provided authorizing the subdivider to subdivide such land under the
provisions of this title.
   J.   Letter of approval from the mortgagor.
   K.   Letter of approval from each utility company utilizing the proposed
easements.
   L.   Text of protective covenants, deed restrictions, homeowners'
association contracts and other restrictions whereby the subdivider proposes to
regulate land use in the subdivision and otherwise protect the proposed
development.
   M.   Environmental, fiscal and transportation impact reports and other
information as requested by the plan commission.
   N.   Preliminary plan checklist, signed by the applicant indicating that all
items necessary for review have been submitted.
The plan commission or its representative shall examine the preliminary plan
documents at their next regularly scheduled meeting followings the submittal of
such documents. The preliminary plan shall be considered officially filed when
it is found to contain the information essential for the proper review by the
plan commission as is required by this title. Lack of information shall be
deemed cause for refusing official ruling. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-2-3: NOTIFICATION OF LOCAL GOVERNMENTS:
When satisfied that sufficient information is presented in the preliminary plan
and other supportive documents, the plan commission shall instruct a village
official or the applicant to transmit copies of the application for preliminary
plan approval to the following, not less than twenty (20) days prior to the
next meeting at which the plan is to be considered:
Village president.
Village engineer.
Chairman, zoning board of appeals.
Superintendent, School District #271.
Fire chief, Franklin Grove fire protection district. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-2-4: NOTIFICATION OF SURROUNDING PROPERTY OWNERS:
In order to allow property owners surrounding the proposed site to provide
information helpful to a proper review of the preliminary plan, one or both of
the following activities shall be undertaken as decided by the plan commission:
   A.   The applicant shall, not less than ten (10) days and not more than
thirty (30) days prior to the date of said meeting, serve written notice either
in person or by certified mail to the last known taxpayers as reflected in the
county records of all property within two hundred fifty feet (250') in each
direction of the location for which the subdivision is requested; provided the
number of feet occupied by all public roads, streets, alleys, rivers, creeks,
schools, parks and other public ways shall be excluded in computing the two
hundred fifty foot (250') requirement. The notices herein required shall
contain the address of the location for which the preliminary plat of
subdivision is requested, a brief statement of the nature of the request, the
name and the address of the legal and beneficial owner of the property, and
time and date on which said meeting shall be held. If, after a bona fide effort
to determine such by the applicant, the owner of the property on which the
notice is served cannot be found at his last known address or the mail notice
is returned because the owner cannot be found, the notice requirements of this
section shall be deemed satisfied. The applicant shall furnish, at the time of
said meeting, a written statement certifying that he has complied with the
requirements of this subsection. Attached to the written statement shall be a
copy of the notice sent and a list of all property owners notified in
accordance with the above. Also attached shall be the returned receipts of
those notices delivered and those notices which were undeliverable by the post
office; and/or
   B.   The village shall publish, in a newspaper of general circulation,
notice of the time and place where the public may comment on the preliminary
plan. The notice shall be published in said newspaper not less than ten (10)
days prior to the public meeting where comments may be given. (Ord. 610, 4-9-
2001)
10-2-2-5: CONSIDERATION BY PLAN COMMISSION:
The plan commission shall review the preliminary plan and other documents with
the subdivider, citizens and other local government official. In cases where
the subdivision of land involves a variation or exception from the zoning
ordinance or a special use permit, the plan commission shall direct the
applicant to submit the preliminary plan to the zoning board of appeals for
their review.
Within ninety (90) days of the official filing of the preliminary plan with the
plan commission, unless such time is extended by mutual consent, the plan
commission shall recommend to the village board for its action:
   A.   Approval or disapproval of the preliminary plan and shall submit its
written recommendations, which may include the recommendations of the village
engineer, village attorney, village planner, citizens and other government
officials, to the board of trustees and to the subdivider; or
   B.   Conditional approval of the preliminary plan, and shall submit its
recommendations and modifications to the board of trustees and to the
subdivider. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-2-6: FEES:
   A.   Review Fee: During the course of their review, the plan commission may
submit the preliminary plan to the village engineer, village planner and/or
other technical consultant in order to obtain assistance for the proper review
of said plan. The subdivider shall be notified that technical assistance has
been sought in accordance with these regulations. The village engineer, village
planner and/or other technical consultant shall submit their itemized bill for
services to the village which shall transmit a bill to the subdivider. Said
bill for services shall be set by the village at a rate normally charged for
such professional services and shall include all travel and other expenses
normally charged to the village. The subdivider shall pay the village for the
services rendered within ten (10) days after the submission of the bill from
the village to him.
   B.   Attorney Fees: In addition, the village and the applicant may enter
into an agreement for the payment of attorney fees required to properly
evaluate the preliminary plan and supportive documents. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-2-7: CONSIDERATION BY BOARD OF TRUSTEES:
The board of trustees shall approve, approve with conditions, or disapprove the
preliminary plan within thirty (30) days after its next regularly scheduled
meeting following the action of the plan commission, unless such time is
extended by mutual consent. The subdivider shall, within thirty (30) days
thereof, be notified in writing of any conditions of approval or the reasons
for rejection. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-2-8: EFFECT OF APPROVAL OF PRELIMINARY PLAN:
Approval by the board of trustees at this stage does not constitute acceptance
of the subdivision. Approval of the preliminary plan shall be:
   A.   Considered permission to prepare detailed plans and specification for
such proposed subdivision and for all public improvements therein;
   B.   Effective for no more than twelve (12) months from the date approval
was granted unless, upon application of the subdivider within the period that
such approval is valid, the board of trustees grants an extension of time
beyond such period. The application for such extension shall not require an
additional filing fee.
If a final plat has not been approved as required by the provisions of this
title within such twelve (12) month period, or any extension granted thereto,
the preliminary plan must be resubmitted to the plan commission as if such plan
had never been approved. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-3: INSTALLATION OF SURVEY MONUMENTS:
After approval of the preliminary plan and before undertaking other measures
leading to approval of the final plat, survey monuments and markers shall be
laid out and set according to the following:
   A.   Permanent monuments shall be placed at all corners and at points
tangent to curve lines along the boundary of the subdivision. Permanent
monuments shall be constructed of concrete, the minimum dimensions of which
shall be four inches by four inches (4" x 4") at the top of the monument and
six inches by six inches (6" x 6") at the bottom; such monument shall be a
minimum of thirty six inches (36") long, with an iron dowel at least three-
eighths inch (3/8") in diameter and two and one-half inches (21/2") in length
embedded in the top of such monument so that the dowel shall be flush with the
surface of the monument and placed in the center of the monument.
   B.   Where concrete monuments are not required to be placed, all corner
lots, the ends of all curves, all angle points in any line and all angle points
along a meander line shall be marked by galvanized or wrought iron pipe at
least twenty four inches (24") long and not less than one-half inch (1/2") in
diameter. The top of such pipe shall be set level with the established grade
for each lot.
   C.   For each twenty (20) acres or fraction thereof in such subdivision, one
permanent bench mark shall be established at a location designated by the
village engineer. This bench mark shall be constructed of concrete, four inches
by four inches (4" x 4") at the top, six inches by six inches (6" x 6") at the
bottom, and forty eight inches (48") in length with a brass plate securely
fastened to the surface. The brass plate shall be exposed about one inch (1")
above final grade and shall be inscribed with the number and elevation of the
bench mark.
All U.S., state, county or other official bench marks, monuments or
triangulation stations in or adjacent to the property shall be preserved in
precise position. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-4: PLANS AND SPECIFICATIONS FOR REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Preparation: After the installation of survey monuments and markers,
unless required sooner, and prior to the submission of a final plat, the
subdivider shall prepare detailed plans and specifications for all improvements
required to be constructed under the provisions of this title.
   B.   Preliminary Review: The plans and specifications for required
improvements shall be submitted to the plan commission. The plan commission
shall transmit said plans and specifications to the. village engineer for
review to determine their compliance with the provisions of this and other
applicable ordinances. Such plans and specifications shall also be reviewed by
appropriate state, county and local officials and utility companies concerned
with such improvements, and approval from these officials shall be given in
writing respecting their particular interests. Following the aforesaid review
by the village engineer and the other officials concerned, the plan commission
shall transmit said plans and specifications to the board of trustees,
accompanied by the recommendations of the village engineer and letters of
approval from the aforesaid officials where applicable.
   C.   Review Fees: Prior to the consideration of the plans and specifications
for required improvements by the village board, the subdivider shall reimburse
the village for the fees involved in the review and processing of said plans
and specifications.
   D.   Cooperation With Neighboring Jurisdictions: Where a proposed storm
water improvement may result in changes to an existing storm water carrying
system of neighboring upstream or downstream communities, copies of the storm
water improvement plans and specifications shall be submitted to the affected
communities. Where the proposed improvement may affect the storm water carrying
system of a site occupied by or planned for development by a school and/or park
district, copies of the plans and specifications shall be forwarded to the
affected districts.
The affected communities and/or taxing districts shall be given written
notification of such proposed improvements and shall be requested to respond to
the village having jurisdiction over the proposed improvements. Such response
shall be submitted in writing within fifteen (15) days upon receipt of such
request. If any alterations to the plans and specifications are requested by
the affected communities and/or taxing districts, and if such alterations are
in accordance with the plans and standards of such affected local governments,
the village having jurisdiction may require the applicant to revise the plans
and specifications in accordance with the requests of the affected governments.
   E.   Final Approval: If the board of trustees finds that the plans and
specifications for required improvements comply with the provisions of this and
other applicable ordinances, it shall grant final approval to such plans and
specifications. The village engineer and the village president shall thereupon
affix their signatures to the plans and specifications, then the village clerk
shall attest such signatures. Final approval, however, shall not constitute
acceptance of the improvements by the village. Such acceptance shall be
governed by the provisions of section 10-5-5 of this title. (Ord. 610, 4-9-
2001)
10-2-5: FINAL PLAT:
10-2-5-1: PREPARATION:
After the installation of survey monuments and markers, a final plat of
subdivision shall be prepared. The final plat may constitute only a portion of
the approved preliminary plan if it is determined acceptable by the plan
commission after consideration by the plan commission of the effect upon the
continuity of roads, utilities and services. The final plat shall be accurately
and legibly prepared with waterproof, nonfading ink on a tracing cloth or Mylar
reproducible print measuring no less than eight and one-half inches by fourteen
inches (81/2" x 14") but no more than thirty inches by thirty six inches (30" x
36") (24 inches by 26 inches preferred), at the same scale as the preliminary
plan, and shall be used as the original copy of such final plat for the
purposes of formal execution, approval and recording. The final plat shall
include the following information:
   A.   Date of preparation of the final plat and by whom prepared.
   B.   Seal and certification of land surveyor.
   C.   Scale, which shall be one hundred feet to the inch (1" = 100') or fifty
feet to the inch (1" = 50'), if the area of subdivision is less than forty (40)
acres.
   D.   North point.
   E.   Legal description.
   F.   Layout of streets, showing right of way widths, street names and the
length of all streets as measured at the centerline, and the location and
widths of all crosswalkways. The location, right of way widths and names of all
streets adjoining the plat shall also be shown.
   G.   All easements established for public use and utility rights of way,
with approval of the utility companies marked on the plat.
   H.   All block and lot numbers and lines, with accurate dimensions given in
hundredths of feet.
   I.   Proposed building setback lines on all lots and other sites.
   J.   Accurate outlines and legal descriptions of all areas dedicated or
reserved for public use, with the deed to be transferred included; and all
areas to be reserved by deed covenant for the common use of all property
owners, together with the proposed uses indicated thereon.
   K.   Water elevations of all lakes and streams within or adjoining the tract
at the date of survey and the approximate high and low water elevations of such
lakes or streams. All elevations shall be referred approximately to USGS datum.
If the subdivision borders on a lake or streams, the distances and bearings of
a meander line established not less than twenty feet (20') back from the
average high water mark of the lake or stream, as determined from flood hazard
maps or other data, with said distances noted.
   L.   Accurate angular and lineal dimensions for all lines, angles radii and
arcs used to describe all boundaries including perimeter survey of tract,
streets, alleys, easements, areas to be reserved or dedicated for public use,
and other important features. Error of closure of boundary line surveys shall
not exceed one in ten thousand (1 foot for each 10,000 feet) of perimeter
survey. Angular error shall not exceed plus or minus twenty (±20) seconds.
   M.   True angles and distances to the nearest established street lines and
official monuments (not less than 3), which shall be accurately described in
the plat by location, size and elevation, to which all dimensions, angles,
bearings and similar data on the plat shall be referred.
   N.   Municipal, township, county and section lines accurately tied to the
lines of the subdivision by distances and angles.
   O.   Certificates, as shown in section
10-2-6 of this chapter. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-5-2: FILING OF FINAL PLAT:
Within one year after approval of the preliminary plan, the subdivider shall
submit the following documents to the village clerk not less than ten (10) days
prior to the regularly scheduled meeting of the plan commission:
   A.   Fifteen (15) copies of the completed application for final plat
approval.
   B.   The original tracing cloth or Mylar of the final plat, which shall be
returned to the applicant upon final plat approval for recording with the
county recorder of deeds.
   C.   One copy of the final plat, drawn on sepia for future use by the
village in its planning and development activities.
   D.   Fifteen (15) copies of the final plat of subdivision to be used for
review by village officials.
   E.   Five (5) copies of the plans and specifications for all improvements
required under chapter 5 of this title.
   F.   Filing fee of fifty dollars ($50.00).
   G.   Reimbursement statement, whereby the subdivider agrees to reimburse the
village for all costs incurred by the village for the review of the final plat
submittals. Such fees shall be paid by the subdivider prior to final plat
approval.
   H.   Performance guarantee, in the amount equal to one hundred percent
(100%) of the estimated costs of the required subdivision improvements, as
approved by the village engineer, in order to ensure that the work is performed
according to the plans and specifications and according to good engineering
practices. Such guarantee shall be in accordance with subsection 10-5-1A1 of
this title.
   I.   Inspection statement, whereby the subdivider agrees to provide
inspection in accordance with subsection 10-5-3A of this title.
   J.   Text of protective covenants, deed restrictions, homeowners'
association contracts and other restrictions relating to any part of the
proposed subdivision, including, but not limited to, building restrictions, use
restrictions, building setback lines, buffer areas, common open space,
maintenance of improvements, etc.
   K.   Final plat checklist, signed by the applicant indicating that all items
necessary for review have been submitted.
   L.   The final plat shall not be considered until the following certificates
have been duly executed:
Owner's certificate.
Surveyor's certificate.
Certificate of special assessments.
County clerk's certificate.
The village clerk shall transmit the final plat and accompanying material to
the plan commission at its next regularly scheduled meeting following the final
plat submittal. The final plat shall be considered officially filed when the
plan commission determines that it contains all the information essential for
its proper review according to the provisions of this title. The plan
commission shall refer the final plat to the village engineer and others it
deems necessary in order to make such proper determination. (Ord. 610, 4-9-
2001)
10-2-5-3: CONSIDERATION BY PLAN COMMISSION:
When satisfied that sufficient information is presented in the final plat and
other supportive documents, the plan commission shall transmit the material to
the village engineer, village attorney and others it deems necessary for a
proper review. Within thirty (30) days from the date of final plat submittal,
unless such time is extended by mutual consent, the plan commission shall
determine if the final plat meets all applicable village requirements. If the
plan commission finds that the final plat is not in accordance with the village
requirements, it shall disapprove such plat and provide written notification to
the board of trustees stating the reasons for such disapproval. If the plan
commission determines that the final plat meets all applicable village
requirements, it shall affix upon the final plat the certifying signature of
its chairman and secretary, and shall submit the final plat and accompanying
documents to the board of trustees. The plan commission may also recommend that
the village board consider other provisions prior to final plat approval. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-5-4: CONSIDERATION BY BOARD OF TRUSTEES:
When final plat and accompanying documents have been forwarded to the board of
trustees by the plan commission, the board of trustees shall consider said plat
to be officially filed. Within sixty (60) days from the date of official
filing, unless such time is extended by mutual consent, the board of trustees
shall approve or disapprove the final plat. If the final plat is approved, the
chairman shall affix his signature to such plat in the space provided and the
village clerk shall attest such signature. If the final plat is disapproved,
the subdivider shall be given written notification of the reasons for such
disapproval. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-5-5: RECORDING:
Upon approval of the final plat by the village board, the final plat shall be
recorded within sixty (60) days thereof with the recorder of deeds of Lee
County, Illinois. If such recording is not effected within such time, the
approval by the village board shall become null and void, in which case the
deposits for surface improvements held by the village shall be refunded in full
to the depositor, without interest. The recording of the final plat is a
requirement for the selling of land or lots in the subdivision and for the
issuance of any building permit. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-2-6: PLAT FORMS:
The following plat forms shall be used to the extent possible as indicated:
   A.   Owner's Certificate: The final plat shall contain an owner's
certificate substantially as follows:

CHAPTER 3
DESIGN STANDARDS
SECTION:
10-3-1: General Provisions
10-3-2: Street Layout And Design
10-3-3: Alleys
10-3-4: Block Standards
10-3-5: Lot Standards
10-3-6: Easements
10-3-7: Sidewalks
10-3-8: Landscaping
10-3-9: Pathways
10-3-10: Street Lighting
10-3-11: Street Signs And Guardrails
10-3-12: Storm Water Drainage
10-3-13: Sanitary Sewer System
10-3-14: Water System
10-3-1: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
The subdivision of land, including the arrangement, character, extent, width,
grade and location of all streets, alleys, crosswalks, easements, sites for
parks, playgrounds and schools or other land to be dedicated for public use,
shall conform to the official plan and official map of the village of Franklin
Grove and approval of design standards shall be considered on the basis of
their relation to existing and platted streets, reasonable circulation of
traffic within the subdivision and adjacent land, topographic conditions,
runoff of storm water, public convenience and safety and appropriate relation
to the proposed land uses of the area to be served.
No land shall be subdivided which is unsuitable for subdivision by reason of
flooding, collection of ground water, poor drainage, adverse earth or rock
formation or topography. Land considered unsuitable for subdivision is defined
in the village comprehensive plan, which includes the China Township soil
survey map interpreted by use of the soil interpretation guide for urbanizing
areas. Soil limitation grounds R-1, R-2 and R-3 shall not be developed in the
absence of documentation that indicates that special problems posed by these
limitations have been properly considered and that proper engineering to
overcome these problems has been done and that such engineering is to be
provided by the subdivider. Such engineering plans shall be reviewed by the
village engineer and his report shall be a part of the plan commission record
prior to approval of the final plat.
Land which cannot be developed as indicated above shall not be developed but
shall remain as dedicated open space. Natural features such as trees, brooks,
hilltops and existing ground slopes shall be preserved whenever possible. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-2: STREET LAYOUT AND DESIGN:
   A.   Layout And Design:
      1.   New and proposed street arrangements within a subdivision shall
provide for the continuation of all existing streets into the area proposed to
be subdivided, unless topographical or other conditions make continuance or
conformance to existing streets impractical.
      2.   New and proposed street arrangements within a subdivision shall
allow for the future continuation of said streets into adjacent tracts
according to topographic conditions of said adjacent tracts and/or according to
the consideration of future traffic circulation.
      3.   Where a tract is subdivided into parcels larger than ordinary
building lots, such parcels shall be arranged to allow the opening of future
streets and further resubdivision in a logical and orderly manner.
      4.   All required streets shall conform to the table of minimum standards
for street design and the materials and specifications on file with the village
clerk.
   B.   Minor Streets: Minor streets shall be so laid out that their use by
through traffic will be discouraged.
   C.   Half Streets: Half streets shall be prohibited except where:
      1.   A dedicated half street exists adjacent to the parcel being
subdivided. Under this condition, the other half shall be platted and improved
according to the standards herein.
      2.   The plan commission and village board determine that it will be
practicable to require the dedication of a right of way on land not wholly
owned by the developer. Under this condition, the village may take such action
as is required to secure said right of way and the applicant shall pay such
costs as well as the costs of the required improvements.
   D.   Cul-De-Sac Streets:
      1.   The maximum length of a cul-de-sac shall be one thousand feet
(1,000') measured along the centerline from the intersection at origin through
center of circle to end of right of way.
      2.   Each cul-de-sac shall have a terminus of nearly circular shape with
a minimum diameter of at least one hundred fifty feet (150') from property line
to property line.
      3.   The minimum cul-de-sac right of way width shall be sixty six feet
(66') and the minimum pavement width shall be twenty four feet (24').
      4.   The use of cul-de-sac streets shall be prohibited in multi- family,
business or industrial districts.
   E.   Access To Primary Street: The following standards are established for
the purpose of providing protection for individual properties and to provide
for traffic safety and the efficient use of the primary street for its intended
function of accommodating through traffic.
      1.   A marginal access street may be required in commercial or industrial
zones, separated from a primary street by a planting or grass strip having a
minimum width of twenty feet (20') between the pavement of the primary street
and pavement of the marginal access street. Points of access from the frontage
road to the primary street shall be spaced at a minimum of one thousand three
hundred twenty feet (1,320').
      2.   In residential areas, access to primary streets shall be provided by
one of the following means:
         a.   The subdivision of lots so as to back onto the primary street and
front onto a local street; no access to individual lots shall be provided from
the primary street, and a landscaped screening, as approved by the plan
commission, shall be provided in a strip of land at least twelve feet (12')
wide along the rear property lines of such lots.
         b.   A marginal access street, separated from the primary street by a
planting or grass strip having a minimum width of twenty five feet (25')
between the pavement of the primary street and the pavement of the marginal
access street. Points of access from the frontage road to the primary street
shall be spaced at a minimum of one thousand three hundred twenty feet
(1,320').
   F.   Intersections: It must be evidenced that all street intersections and
confluences encourage safe traffic flow.
      1.   The intersection of more than two (2) streets at one point shall be
avoided except where otherwise impractical to secure a proper street system.
      2.   Streets shall intersect one another at an angle as near to the right
angle as possible and in no event shall such intersection be at an angle of
less than sixty degrees (60°).
      3.   Where street intersections are right angle intersections, such
intersections shall be rounded with a minimum radius of twenty feet (20') for
minor streets, twenty five feet (25') for other streets, as measured from the
back of the curbs. If an intersection occurs other than at a right angle, it
shall be rounded with a curve of a radius acceptable to the plan commission.
      4.   Proposed new intersections along one side of an existing street
shall, wherever practicable, coincide with any existing intersections on the
opposite side of such street. Street jogs with centerline offsets of less than
one hundred twenty five feet (125') shall be prohibited.
      5.   When connecting streets deflect from each other at any point by more
than thirty degrees (30°), they shall be connected by a curve with a radius
adequate to ensure a sight distance of not less than two hundred feet (200'),
and of such greater radii as the plan commission shall determine for special
cases.
   G.   Widening And Realignment Of Existing Roads: Where a subdivision borders
an existing narrow road or when the official map and/or official plan or zoning
setback regulations indicate plans for realignment or widening a road that
would require use of some of the land in the subdivision, the applicant shall
be required to improve and dedicate at his expense such areas for widening or
realignment according to the standards required by these regulations.
   H.   Bridges: Bridges of primary benefit to the applicant, as determined by
the plan commission, shall be constructed at full expense of the applicant
without reimbursement from the village. The sharing expense for construction of
bridges not of primary benefit to the applicant, as determined by the plan
commission, will be fixed by special agreement between the village and the
applicant.
   I.   Materials And Specifications: Standards and specifications for public
streets are on file with the village clerk.
   TABLE OF MINIMUM STANDARDS FOR STREET DESIGN
 
                                                                     Minimum
                                                Minimum    Minimum   Length Of
Street         ROW     Pavement Maximum Minimum Radius Of  Length Of Tangents

(major)

(collector)

access         60'     24'      7%                                ----
