and industrial 80-120' 37'+     5%             500'       300'a     200'
districts
 
      1.   Where streets adjoin areas zoned for commercial business or
industrial use, or where a petition for a change in zoning or in the official
plan is contemplated to permit commercial, business, or industrial in adjoining
areas, the above standards shall be increased by the amount necessary to
provide for the free flow of through traffic without interference from parked
vehicles and to provide for safe parking space for such commercial, business,
or industrial uses. This table does not constitute maximum standards which may
be required under site specific development conditions.
      2.   Right of way widths in excess of these standards shall be required
whenever, due to topography, additional width is necessary in order to provide
adequate earth slopes.
      3.   As measured from back of curb to back of curb, or edge of pavement.
         a.   But not less than 50 feet for each 1 percent algebraic difference
of grade.
         b.   But not less than 40 feet for each 1 percent algebraic difference
of grade.
Sight distance plans shall be submitted for critical intersections and other
points as determined by the village engineer.
      4.   The minimum grade of all streets shall be five-tenths of one percent
with curb and gutter, four-tenths of one percent with grass waterways (curb and
swale). All surface drainage ditches shall have a minimum slope of five-tenths
of one percent.
(Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-3: ALLEYS:
   A.   Alleys shall be permitted in residential districts. Such alleys shall
have a right of way of not less than eighteen feet (18') in width and shall
have full access to streets at each end.
   B.   In commercial, business and industrial districts, alleys shall be
permitted only where necessary to assure adequate off loading and unloading.
Such alleys shall have a right of way of not less than twenty four feet (24')
in width and shall have full access to streets at each end. (Ord. 610, 4-9-
2001)
10-3-4: BLOCK STANDARDS:
   A.   The length, width and shape of blocks shall be determined with due
regard to:
      1.   Provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special needs
of the types of use contemplated.
      2.   Zoning requirements as to lot sizes and dimensions.
      3.   Needs of convenient access, circulation, control and safety of
street traffic.
   B.   In residential areas, all blocks shall be not more than one thousand
five hundred feet (1,500') in length and shall be of sufficient width to
provide two (2) tiers of lots, except that one tier of lots may back onto a
limited access highway, major street, secondary street, or railroad right of
way; provided, that at least a twelve foot (12') landscaped planting, as
approved by the plan commission, is situated on a no access reservation along
the rear property lines of such block.
   C.   Blocks intended for commercial, business or industrial use shall be
designed for such use and the plat shall show adequate off street areas for
parking, loading docks and other facilities that may be required to accommodate
motor vehicles.
   D.   In blocks of eight hundred feet (800') or more in length, a public
crosswalk for pedestrian travel, at least ten feet (10') wide, may be required
by the plan commission where deemed essential to provide circulation or access
to schools, parks, shopping centers and other community facilities. (Ord. 610,
4-9-2001)
10-3-5: LOT STANDARDS:
   A.   Regular Lots:
      1.   The lot size, width, depth, shape and orientation shall be
appropriate for the location of the subdivision and for the type of development
and use contemplated. Due regard shall be shown for all natural features, such
as trees, watercourses, historic and scenic sites and similar conditions which,
if preserved, will add attractiveness and value to the proposed development.
      2.   Lot width and area shall conform to or exceed the requirements as
set forth in the zoning ordinance of the village or that of the appropriate
county in the areas beyond the village limits.
      3.   Each lot shall have its full frontage abutting a publicly dedicated
street.
      4.   Side lot lines shall be substantially at right angles or radial to
the street line.
      5.   Additional building setbacks may be required in the case of corner
lots to assure the proper development of intersection design and traffic
safety. Driveway locations on corner lots may be required to be shown on the
final plat and the location shown shall appear as a covenant running with that
lot.
      6.   In order to provide an adequate building site, additional lot width
and depth shall be required when more than ten percent (10%) of the minimum lot
area includes land within a drainageway, channel or stream or when less than
eighty percent (80%) of the minimum lot area is at least three feet (3') above
the highest ground water level as estimated from soil boring test data.
      7.   Double frontage lots are forbidden except where lots back upon a
limited access highway, a major street, a secondary street or a railroad right
of way. Double frontage lots shall not have vehicular access through such lots.
      8.   Lots proposed in heavy stands of mature timber shall be a minimum of
two (2) acres in order to prevent excessive destruction of the timber during
construction of residences, driveways and septic fields.
   B.   Hillside Regulations: A "hillside lot" as referred to herein is defined
as one with an average slope of more than fifteen percent (15%). The plan
commission shall determine which lots are to comply with the regulations
contained herein and said lots shall be so designated on the final plat.
      1.   Minimum Lot Size: No minimum size is established, but the lot shall
be of adequate size to comply with all regulations contained herein.
      2.   Erosion Control: Erosion controls such as retaining walls, cribbing
or vegetative cover may be required by the plan commission. When required by
the plan commission, plans must be submitted to the village engineer for
approval before starting on the plat as a covenant which will run with the
land.
      3.   Sewage Disposal: No subsurface sanitary waste disposal system may be
constructed on a hillside lot. Exceptions will only be made based on detailed
studies provided by the subdivider and approved by the plan commission.
      4.   Cuts And Fills: Major cuts, excavation, grading and filling will not
be permitted if it results in a slope of two and one- half to one (2.5:1) or
greater along adjacent lot lines except where adequate provision is made to
prevent slides and erosion. Where cuts or fills are required to provide a
building site, engineering data must be presented to show existing and proposed
topography, location of the building site and an analysis of the fill material
to be used.
      5.   Driveways: The maximum grade on driveways shall not exceed twelve
percent (12%). Each drive shall provide sufficient space and distance to turn
around before entering the street.
   C.   Commercial, Industrial, Business Lots: The lot width, area and depth
shall be as recommended by the plan commission and approved by the village
board. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-6: EASEMENTS:
   A.   Continuity: Easements shall be designed to provide continuity
throughout the entire subdivision.
   B.   Public Utility Easements: Utility distribution or transmission
installations serving the subdivision shall be located in easements and so
designated on the subdivision plat of record. Such easements shall be located
along the rear lot lines, side lot lines or front lot line. They shall occupy
not less than ten feet (10'), of which five feet (5') may be shown on each of
two (2) adjacent lots. Utility easements shall be indicated as such on the
final plat and shall not be used for drainage purposes except that they may be
graded as a drainage swale.
All utilities shall be underground and contained within easements or dedicated
rights of way. When utilities are within a right of way, the utility shall not
be located beneath a paved area other than sidewalks.
   C.   Village Utility Easements: Whenever it is necessary to install water
mains, sanitary sewers, storm sewers or other underground utilities to be
maintained by the village in areas other than public rights of way, easements
shall be established and so designated. Easements may not be less than ten feet
(10') wide, five feet (5') of which may be shown on each of two (2) adjacent
lots.
Whenever the village utilities and the public utilities follow a common route,
they may be in a common easement terming a utility easement. Said easements
shall be of adequate width for the purpose intended but in no case shall they
be less than fifteen feet (15').
   D.   Drainage Easements: Where a subdivision is transversed by a
watercourse, drainageway, channel or stream, there shall be provided a drainage
easement or right of way conforming substantially with the lines of such
watercourse, and further width as will be necessary for the purpose of
adequately maintaining or improving the watercourse. Said easements shall not
be used for any other purposes except that utilities may cross this easement,
provided that the crossing does not alter the intended use of the easement.
(Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-7: SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Requirements: Sidewalks shall be required on both sides of the street
for all commercial lots. Sidewalks may be required for industrial lots and
elsewhere if considered necessary by the plan commission for public safety. All
sidewalks shall be constructed of Portland cement concrete unless another
material is required by the village engineer.
   B.   Location: Unless otherwise directed by the village engineer, sidewalks
shall be located within the dedicated right of way and shall be laid one foot
(1') from the property line of abutting lots and along such line as extended at
intersections.
   C.   Dimensions: Sidewalks in residential subdivisions shall be not less
than four feet (4') in width, not less than four inches (4") in thickness, and
not less than six inches (6") in thickness where they intersect a driveway.
Sidewalks for commercial and industrial lots shall be not less than five feet
(5') in width and not less than five inches (5") in thickness.
   D.   Compliance: Sidewalks shall comply with the requirements of the
subdivision standards on file with the village clerk. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-8: LANDSCAPING:
   A.   Grass Seeding Or Sod: All unpaved areas within street rights of way
shall be seeded or sodded with a Kentucky bluegrass mixture or with such other
grass mixture as approved by the village engineer. Before the release of the
maintenance bond can be recommended by the village engineer, all unpaved areas
between the edge of the road pavement and the right of way line must have an
adequate mat of grass.
   B.   Trees: Existing trees should be preserved and protected during
construction.
   C.   Screen Planting: Protective screen planting may be required to secure a
reasonable effective physical barrier between residential properties and
adjoining uses to minimize adverse conditions of sight and sound. The screen
planting plan shall be prepared by a landscape architect and shall meet the
approval of the plan commission. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-9: PATHWAYS:
The plan commission may require the provision of a pathway system at
appropriate locations upon consideration of the safety of pedestrian and
bicycle access to public areas. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-10: STREET LIGHTING:
Street lighting shall comply with the requirements of the subdivision standards
on file with the village clerk. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-11: STREET SIGNS AND GUARDRAILS:
Street signs and guardrails shall comply with the requirements of the
subdivision standards on file with the village clerk. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-12: STORM WATER DRAINAGE:
   A.   Storm water drainage including storm water detention facilities shall
comply with the requirements of the subdivision standards on file with the
village clerk.
   B.   As a condition of approval of a final plat of subdivision, or of a
final plat of a planned unit of development, each subdivider shall be required
to construct storm water detention facilities and dedicate land on which those
facilities are located including access; or cash contribution in lieu of the
actual construction of the storm water detention facilities (including land
dedication); or a combination of both, at the option of the village in
accordance with the following criteria and formula.
   C.   Storm water detention facilities shall be designed in accordance with
the requirements of the subdivision standards on file with the village clerk.
Where the development is small and the resulting storm water detention
facilities would be too small to be practical and where storm water detention
facilities could be deleted or deferred without causing adverse impacts, the
village, at its option, may require the subdivider or developer to pay a cash
contribution in lieu of constructing the storm water detention facilities and
dedicating land for those facilities. The cash contribution in lieu of storm
water detention facilities shall be held by the village to be used for storm
water and drainage facilities and improvements.
The amount of the cash contribution in lieu of construction of storm water
detention facilities shall be computed as follows:
      1.   The volume of the storm water detention pond which would be required
shall be calculated in accordance with the requirements of the subdivision
standards on file with the village clerk.
      2.   The amount of cash contribution shall be fifteen thousand dollars
($15,000.00) per acre-foot of storm water detention volume which would have
been required. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-13: SANITARY SEWER SYSTEM:
Sanitary sewer system improvements, where applicable shall comply with the
requirements of the subdivision standards on file with the village clerk. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)
10-3-14: WATER SYSTEM:
Water system improvements shall comply with the requirements of the subdivision
standards on file with the village clerk. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
ARTICLE A. STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS FOR PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
10-3A-1: Engineering And Administrative Procedures
10-3A-2: Streets
10-3A-3: Sidewalks
10-3A-4: Street Lighting
10-3A-5: Street Signs, Guardrails And Landscaping
10-3A-6: Storm Water Drainage
10-3A-7: Sanitary Sewer Systems
10-3A-8: Water Systems
10-3A-1: ENGINEERING AND ADMINISTRATIVE PROCEDURES:
A major share of what eventually becomes publicly owned improvements are
designed and constructed by private interests. This article establishes
processing requirements and a uniform design criteria for ensuring that such
improvements will result in construction meeting the standards of the village.
Where improvement plans and specifications are submitted as a part of a plat of
subdivision, the processing requirements shall be as contained in the
subdivision regulations of the village. In any case, the design and
construction of street improvements, streetlights, street signs, storm water
drainage, sanitary sewer system and water system shall be in accordance with
the design regulations contained in this article. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-2: STREETS:
Minimum construction requirements for streets shall be as follows:
   A.   General References: It is intended that all public streets shall be
constructed in accordance, as far as applicable, with the most recently adopted
edition of the state of Illinois, department of transportation, "Standard
Specification For Road And Bridge Construction", including current highway
standards, special provisions and supplemental specifications as issued by said
department. These shall be referred to as the "state standard specifications"
hereinafter.
   B.   Subgrade: The subgrade of all public streets shall be prepared in
accordance with section 212 of the state standard specifications. It is
required that the soil composing the subgrade have a minimum soil support value
of 3.0 as determined by the IBR (Illinois bearing ratio) test procedures used
by the Illinois department of transportation. When, in the opinion of the
village engineer, evaluation of the suitability of the subgrade to support the
proposed pavement is warranted, a competent soils engineer approved by the
village and retained by the developer at his expense shall perform the
necessary soil tests to ensure that a stable subgrade as specified is being
provided.
   C.   Design Of Pavement, Procedure: The required thickness of the pavement
shall be determined in accordance with the current Illinois department of
transportation "Manual Of Instruction For The Structural Design Of Bituminous
Pavements Of Projects Involving MFT, FAS, FUS And TOPICS Funds" or Illinois
department of transportation design manual section 7.
The anticipated traffic volumes, the composition of the traffic, and the
subgrade support strength provided by the roadbed soils shall be considered in
the design of the pavement. This information is subject to the review and
approval of the village.
      1.   Minimum Design Criteria: Not less than the minimum requirements
listed below shall be permitted in the design of streets.
         a.   No street shall be designed for an average daily traffic count of
less than two hundred (200).
         b.   The percentage of multiple unit vehicles shall be five percent
(5%).
         c.   The percentage of single unit vehicles shall be thirty five
percent (35%) for class IV streets and twenty five percent (25%) for class III
streets.
         d.   Soil support values for the subgrade shall be based upon
laboratory tests conducted on soil samples collected within thirty feet (30')
of the proposed centerline of pavement and at intervals along the centerline
not exceeding five hundred feet (500').
         e.   Traffic count and soil support values shall be submitted to the
village engineer for approval prior to preparing the pavement design.
         f.   The design period shall be twenty (20) years.
         g.   Gravel is not acceptable for an aggregate base course.
         h.   Street shall be surfaced with a class B bituminous binder having
a minimum thickness of one and one-half inches (11/2") and a class B bituminous
wearing surface having a minimum thickness of one and one-half inches (11/2").
         i.   Minimum thickness of the base course shall be:
      Aggregate   8 inches
      Pozzalanic   7 inches
      Bituminous stabilized   6 inches
         j.   Base course shall be supplemented with a subbase course when
necessary to compensate for poor subgrade soil conditions.
         k.   All materials shall be certified by the supplier to meet the
standard specifications for road and bridge construction published by the
Illinois department of transportation.
         l.   No base course material shall be placed before the subgrade has
been inspected and approved for grade and compaction by the village engineer.
Unsatisfactory subgrade shall be excavated and replaced with approved subbase
material.
         m.   After approval of the subbase and subgrade, no vehicular
construction equipment traffic, except for road construction equipment, shall
be permitted on the streets before the base course and bituminous binder course
have been completed.
         n.   The bituminous wearing surface course shall be completed within
one year after installation of the binder course or when approximately sixty
percent (60%) of the construction traffic tributary to the street due to
housing or building construction has been completed.
         o.   The village reserves the right to request curb and gutter or
paved ditches. Curb and gutter or paved ditches shall be used when slopes
exceed seven percent (7%), or in other areas where flowing water might initiate
drainage failure, or in areas where ground water conditions will tend to
promote extended periods of flow. Curb and gutter shall be state of Illinois
type B (mountable) in residential areas, and shall be state of Illinois type B
6.12 barrier type in commercial and industrial areas. Paved ditches shall be
state of Illinois standard type A. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-3: SIDEWALKS:
   A.   All sidewalks shall be air entrained Portland cement concrete and a
minimum of six (6) bag mix, five inches (5") thick over three inches (3") of
grade CA 16 pea gravel or compacted CA6 coarse aggregate, Illinois standard
specifications.
   B.   Sidewalks shall be elevated not less than one-fourth inch per foot (1/
4"/1') from the edge of street to the edge of sidewalk.
   C.   Sidewalks shall be located one foot (1') off the property line on both
sides of the street, and shall be not less than four feet (4') in width.
   D.   Sidewalks shall comply with the requirements of the subdivision
standards on file with the village clerk. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-4: STREET LIGHTING:
   A.   Residential street lighting facilities shall be provided in
subdivisions at all street intersections and at closer intervals if the gross
density of the subdivision is three (3) dwelling units per acre or more.
   B.   The subdivider shall bear all the necessary expense and responsibility
of providing all street lighting materials per the current existing
specifications or requirements of the Commonwealth Edison Company and/or
village.
   C.   The subdivider shall arrange for and pay all installation costs
required by the Commonwealth Edison Company for the erection of the required
streetlights.
   D.   The subdivider shall bear all expense and responsibility for any street
lighting alteration or corrections needed to ensure the maintenance acceptance
agreement by Commonwealth Edison Company. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-5: STREET SIGNS, GUARDRAILS AND LANDSCAPING:
   A.   Street signs of the type approved by the village shall be installed on
two (2) diagonal corners of each intersection and shall indicate the street
names as shown on the final plat.
   B.   Wooden timber guardrails shall be placed along the shoulder of any
street where street construction has resulted in an embankment greater than six
feet (6').
   C.   All unpaved street rights of way shall be seeded or sodded. Provisions
shall be made to assure the growth of all landscaping. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-6: STORM WATER DRAINAGE:
   A.   Surface water drainage improvements consisting of storm sewers and/or
detention facilities shall be designed and constructed to adequately drain the
area being developed and also all of such other areas which naturally drain
through the area being developed.
   B.   If the surface water drainage will be changed by the construction of
the subdivision, adequate provision shall be made for collection and diversion
of such surface waters into public areas or drains which the subdivider has a
right to use, and such surface waters shall not be deposited on the property of
adjoining landowners.
   C.   Design and planning of surface water drainage facilities shall be
performed by or under the supervision of a professional engineer, registered in
the state of Illinois. Basic design methods and computations shall be as
outlined in an ASCE manual or reports on engineering practice no. 27, WPCF
Manual No. 9, "Design And Construction Of Sanitary And Storm Sewers". Design
computations conforming to the above manual or other methods subject to the
approval of the village shall be submitted to demonstrate that the requirements
herein are met.
   D.   Unless engineering evidence is presented to the village warranting
exceptions, a combination of facilities providing for storage and controlled
release of storm water, for all commercial or industrial developments exceeding
ten (10) acres in area and for all residential developments exceeding ten (10)
acres, shall be provided. The release rate of storm water from all developments
requiring detention shall not exceed the storm water runoff rate from the area
in its natural, undeveloped state.
   E.   Storm water detention facilities shall be designed in accordance with
the "Information Pamphlet: Design Capacity Of Storm Water Detention Reservoirs"
as presented by the Metropolitan Sanitary District of Greater Chicago; and
"Information Pamphlet: Detailed Steps For Determining Allowable Release Rate
And Required Flood Storage" as presented by the Metropolitan Sanitary District
of Greater Chicago.
   F.   In addition to requirements for detention, drainage facilities will be
designed and constructed to meet the following criteria:
      1.   All improvements will be designed to handle runoff from a storm
having a 5-year frequency (not to be exceeded more than 20 times in 100 years).
Storm water conduit drains that discharge to open channels shall terminate with
suitable outlet structures to control soil erosion and to prevent progressive
failure of the conduit in an upstream direction.
      2.   Inlets, catch basins, where curb and gutter is required, shall be
spaced at no greater distance than five hundred feet (500') apart and shall be
so located that in no case will water be required to flow across a street, or
be retained outside the center ten feet (10') of the drainage utility easement.
They shall be designed to receive the runoff from a storm of 5-year frequency
for residential areas and 10-year frequency in highly developed commercial and
industrial areas.
      3.   Storm sewer slopes shall be such that a minimum velocity of two and
one-half feet (21/2') per second is maintained when the pipe is flowing full
without surcharge. In cases where it is impractical to obtain the above minimum
velocity, modification shall be subject to approval by the village engineer.
      4.   Manholes with a minimum diameter of four feet (4') with cast iron
frames and grates, approved by the village, shall be installed at any abrupt
change in direction, size or grade of the sewer and at all other locations
necessary to limit the distance between manholes to five hundred feet (500'). A
greater distance will be allowed if it makes the manhole more accessible. This
greater distance is subject to the approval of the village. All sewers shall
have straight barrels.
      5.   Joints for storm sewer conduit may be mortar joints or bituminous
joints complying with paragraph 30.3.02 B or paragraph 303.02 C respectively,
as specified in the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main
Construction In Illinois", second edition, dated September 1976, or the latest
revision thereof.
      6.   Capacity of inlets, catch basins and storm sewers shall be not less
than 1.40 cubic feet per second per acre. (Rational formula for 5-year
frequency, 20 minute inlet time and 40 percent runoff coefficient.)
      7.   Provisions shall be made in the design of streets, easements and
drainage facilities so that storm water equal to 1.80 cubic feet per second
(equivalent to 25-year frequency, 20 minute inlet time and 40 percent runoff
coefficient) per acre can be carried by the drainage system and by overland
flow in streets and/or easements to a natural outlet without flooding streets
above the curb line. If such provision is not made, the exception shall be
noted by the professional engineer responsible for design.
      8.   It will be the responsibility of the subdivider to provide grade
control for rear lot drainage to each homeowner, as the homes are constructed.
It will be the homeowner's responsibility to maintain the drainage course and
to keep it free from features that restrict natural drainage.
      9.   Open channel swales will be considered in lieu of storm sewers
provided that the maximum depth of water flow does not exceed eighteen inches
(18") and velocity does not exceed two feet (2') per second, under all storm
conditions up to 100-year frequency. Swales shall have a minimum side slope of
three feet horizontal to one foot vertical (3':1'), shall include a flat bottom
not less than two feet (2') wide. The flow line and two feet (2') up the side
slope of all swales shall be sodded.
      10.   Culverts shall be state of Illinois standard CMP and shall be sized
to carry not less than a storm of 5-year frequency. Minimum culvert size shall
be twelve inches (12"). Culverts shall be installed at all driveways,
intersections and crossroads as required to carry natural drainage.
      11.   The combination of storm sewers, swales and culverts shall be
designed to convey the 100-year storm without inundating, damaging or flooding
private or public property. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-7: SANITARY SEWER SYSTEMS:
   A.   Where improvements and extensions to the sanitary sewage collection
system are required in order to serve the needs of a development, the developer
shall bear all costs in the sewer system installation.
   B.   Prior to proceeding with construction, the developer shall prepare and
submit plans, profiles and specifications to all federal, state, county,
township and other governmental agencies as required by law. Permits or
approvals shall be received from all appropriate agencies. The contractor shall
also submit plans and specifications to the village and shall obtain written
approval from the village board before proceeding with construction. The
following requirements shall be met:
      1.   Plans and specifications submitted shall bear the seal of a current
registered professional engineer.
      2.   Sewers shall be not less than eight inches (8") in diameter.
      3.   Manholes shall be set at each intersection and at intervals not to
exceed four hundred feet (400') (whichever results in closer spacing).
      4.   Curved sewers shall not be allowed.
      5.   Sewers shall be televised and shall reveal a straight, unbroken,
tight, flawless barrel. Sewers shall be lamped for straight barrel, the actual
lamp shall be visible, not the reflection. Sewers shall be tested by
infiltration, exfiltration or air testing in accordance with standard
procedures. Manholes shall be watertight.
      6.   Manholes shall be poured monolithic or shall be precast concrete
rings, sealed watertight.
      7.   Sewer pipe shall be vitrified clay ASTM C-700. Concrete pipe ASTM C-
14 or C-76 or cement asbestos ASTM C-428. Due care in pipe selection shall be
given through design based upon laying conditions, depth of cover and soil
type.
      8.   Sewers shall be buried such that finished grade will provide not
less than eight feet (8') of cover and not greater than sixteen feet (16') of
cover, except where specifically allowed by the village.
      9.   Sewage collection systems shall be designed, installed and tested in
accordance with the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Construction
In Illinois".
      10.   When in any subdivision now within the village or within one and
one-half (11/2) miles of the village limits, which normally would require an
eight inch (8") size sewer, but which for the purpose of complying with the
plan of development of the village's sewage collection not only to the
particular subdivision but also to subdivisions which in the future may become
a part of the village and where the village engineer has determined that sewers
of a larger diameter than eight inches (8") and the size thereof shall be
installed, then the village engineer shall inform the subdividers, builders and
developers of the subdivision by a written notice of that fact and require them
to install such oversized sewers and at the same time, in said notice, inform
them of the size to be installed. Upon being so notified as provided for
herein, no subdivider, builder or developer shall install any sewer in such
subdivision of any size other than that specified to him by the aforesaid
notice.
   C.   At such time as the installation of said oversized sewer pipe shall
have been completed in accordance with the plans and specifications submitted
to the village for such installation, and also in accordance with the notice
specified in this section, and all such installations shall have been inspected
and approved by the village as provided for by the ordinances of the village,
then the village will pay any such subdivider, builder or developer who has
installed oversized sewer pipe, as above provided, the difference of the cost
at current prices as of the time of said installation between the eight inch
(8") pipe which was originally planned to be used and the cost of the oversized
sewer pipe which the village directed to be used. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-3A-8: WATER SYSTEMS:
   A.   Where improvements and extensions to the water distribution system are
required in order to serve the needs of a development, the developer shall bear
all costs in the water main installation.
   B.   Prior to proceeding with construction, the developer shall prepare and
submit plans and specifications to all federal, state, county, township and
other governmental agencies as required by law. Permits or approvals shall be
received from all appropriate agencies. The contractor shall also submit plans
and specifications to the village and shall obtain written approval from the
village board before proceeding with construction. The following requirements
shall be met:
      1.   Plans And Specifications: Plans and specifications submitted shall
bear the seal of a current registered professional engineer.
      2.   Water Main Size: Water mains shall be not less than eight inches
(8") in diameter. Water mains shall be of sufficient size to furnish water in
quantity and pressure as indicated by the Insurance Services of Illinois, or
the Factory Mutual Insurance Company provided velocities do not exceed eight
feet (8') per second during estimated fire demand plus domestic demand.
      3.   Fire Hydrants: Fire hydrants shall be set at each intersection and
at intervals not to exceed three hundred feet (300') (whichever results in
closer spacing).
Fire hydrants as approved by the village engineer shall be installed throughout
the entire water system so that there is a hydrant located at all street
intersections and intermediate hydrants evenly spaced so the interval between
hydrants is not more than three hundred feet (300').
All fire hydrants shall be Clow, Eddy, Traverse City, having a six inch (6")
barrel and shall be provided with two and one-half inch (21/2") hose
connections and one 41/2-inch steamer connection and shall be equipped with
break flange and individual auxiliary valve. The threads on the hose connection
shall be national standard thread. Hydrants shall be set plumb with the center
of the steamer connection set eighteen inches (18") above the finish grade.
All hydrants shall be individually flow tested and meet the capacity indicated
by the following table. Hydrants shall be painted to provide a high level of
daytime visibility and nighttime reflectivity with the hydrant top and nozzle
caps color coded in accordance with the following table:
 
Class Flow Capacity        Color Of Tops And Nozzle Caps
A     1,000 gpm or greater Green
B     500 – 1,000 gpm    Orange
C     Less than 500 gpm    Red
 
      4.   Water Main Material: All water mains shall be ductile iron pipe,
suitable for pressures of at least one hundred fifty (150) psi operating
pressure. Ductile iron pipe shall be AWWA approved, thickness class 51 or
better.
All piping and fittings shall be capable of withstanding an internal working
pressure of one hundred fifty (150) pounds per square inch for forty five (45)
minutes. Pipes shall be designed for a cover of five and one-half feet (51/2')
below finish grade. All pipes shall have a modified cement mortar lining and
shall conform to the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main
Construction In Illinois" (most recent edition).
Alternative materials such as PVC pipe will be considered on a case by case
basis. If approved, PVC pipe shall be AWWA approved and shall be Certainee
"Vinyl Iron", Johns Manville "Blue Brute" or approved equal.
When located within the service area of a public water supply system, water
distribution mains of size listed below shall be installed:
         a.   Single-family residential areas: Eight inch (8") diameter.
         b.   Other than single-family residential developments: Minimum eight
inch (8") diameter water main.
         c.   The above are minimum considerations for water main sizing. This
does not preclude the developer from providing adequate water supplies as will
be necessary under the computations for adequate domestic and industrial and
fire protection purposes, and if such designs require larger size mains, it
shall be the developer's responsibility to provide these mains.
         d.   Gridiron.
            (1)   Each eight inch (8") diameter water main shall be looped at a
distance not to exceed one thousand feet (1,000').
            (2)   Ten inch (10") diameter water mains shall be looped at
distances not to exceed one thousand eight hundred feet (1,800').
            (3)   Twelve inch (12") and larger water mains shall be looped at
distance not to exceed three thousand feet (3,000') by twelve inch (12") or
larger mains.
      5.   Oversized Water Mains: When in any subdivision, which normally would
require an eight inch (8") size water main, but which for the purpose of
complying with the plan of development of the village's water system to provide
an adequate water supply, not only to the particular subdivision but also to
subdivisions which in the future may become a part of the village, and where
the village engineer and superintendent have determined that water mains of a
larger diameter than eight inches (8") and the size thereof shall be installed,
then the village engineer or superintendent shall inform the subdividers,
builders and developers of the subdivision by a written notice of that fact and
require them to install such oversized water mains and at the same time in said
notice inform them of the size to be installed.
Upon being so notified as provided for in this subsection, no subdivider,
builder or developer shall install any water main in such subdivision of any
size other than that specified to him by the aforesaid notice.
At such time as the installation of said oversized water main pipe shall have
been completed in accordance with the plans and specifications submitted to the
village for such installation, and also in accordance with the notice specified
in this section, and all such installation shall have been inspected and
approved by the village as provided for by the ordinances of the village, then
the village will pay any such subdivider, builder or developer who has
installed oversized water main pipe, as above provided, the difference of the
cost at current prices as of the time of said installation between the eight
inch (8") pipe which was originally planned to be used and the cost of the
oversized pipe which the village directed to be used, said payment to be made
at such time as may be designated by a properly executed recapture agreement.
All water main extensions shall be designed, installed and tested in accordance
with the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main Construction In
Illinois".
      6.   Valves: All valves shall be AWWA approved gate valves and shall be
located in valve boxes and covers.
Valves shall be installed at eight hundred feet (800') intervals and the system
shall be designed and valves installed so that with any one section shut down
the rest of the system will maintain an adequate water supply.
Main water line gate valve boxes, shutoff boxes and service boxes are to be
located in a lawn area of the right of way, where possible, and installed at
final finished lawn grade. Main gate valves installed in streets, roadways,
driveways or sidewalks are to be installed in a standard forty eight inch (48")
precast manhole. All valves and shutoff devices shall be protected from frost.
      7.   Customer Services: Customer water service lines shall be constructed
to connect with the utility service mains located within any street or
thoroughfare to service each adjoining lot, tract or building site. Such
service lines shall extend from the main to a point one foot (1') inside the
right of way lines. All such customer service lines shall be located at the
approximate centerline of each lot. Customer services shall not be less than
three-fourths inch (3/4") type K copper and shall include a corporation stop
and curb valve, box and cover. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 4
DEDICATION OF PUBLIC AREAS
SECTION:
10-4-1: Dedication Of Lands For School Sites, Parks And Other Public Areas
10-4-2: Criteria For Requiring School Site Dedication
10-4-3: Criteria For Requiring Park And Recreation Land Dedication
10-4-4: Criteria For Requiring A Contribution In Lieu Of Park And School Sites
10-4-5: Dwelling Unit Population Formula
10-4-6: Reservation Of Additional Land
10-4-7: Combining With Adjoining Developments
10-4-8: Topography And Grading
10-4-9: Improved Sites
10-4-10: Title To Sites
10-4-11: Dedication Or Contribution As A Condition Of Annexation
10-4-12: Cash Contribution For Library Purposes
10-4-1: DEDICATION OF LANDS FOR SCHOOL SITES, PARKS AND OTHER PUBLIC AREAS:
As a condition of approval of a final plat of subdivision, or of a final plat
of a planned unit development, each subdivider or developer shall be required
to dedicate land for school sites and park and recreational purposes, to serve
the immediate and future needs of the residents of the development; or cash
contributions in lieu of actual land dedication; or a combination of both, at
the option of the village in accordance with the following criteria and
formula. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-2: CRITERIA FOR REQUIRING SCHOOL SITE DEDICATION:
   A.   Requirements And Population Ratio: The ultimate number of students to
be generated by a subdivision or planned unit development shall bear directly
upon the amount of land required to be dedicated for school sites. The land
dedication requirement shall be determined by obtaining the ratio of: 1)
estimated children to be served in each such school classification over the 2)
maximum recommended number of students to be served in each school
classification as stated herein, and then applying such ratio to the 3) said
minimum recommended number of acres for a school site of each school
classification as stated herein. The product thereof shall be the acres of land
deemed needed to have sufficient land for school sites to serve the estimated
increased children in each such school classification.
   B.   School Classifications And Size Of School Site: School classifications
and size of school sites within the village shall be determined in accordance
with the following criteria:
School Classification By Maximum Number Of Students Minimum Number Of Acres Of
Grades                   For Each Such School       Land For Each School Site
                         Classification             Of Such Classification
School Classification By Maximum Number Of Students Minimum Number Of Acres Of
Grades                   For Each Such School       Land For Each School Site
                         Classification             Of Such Classification
Elementary schools
Grades kindergarten      600 students               11 acres
through 5
Junior high schools
Grades 6 through 8       900 students               22 acres
High schools
Grades 9 through 12      2,300 students             48 acres
 
   C.   Location: The official plan of the village and the standards of the
affected school district shall be used as guidelines in locating sites. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-3: CRITERIA FOR REQUIRING PARK AND RECREATION LAND DEDICATION:
   A.   Requirement And Population Ratio: The ultimate density of a proposed
development shall bear directly upon the amount of land required dedication.
The total requirement shall be six (6.0) acres of land per one thousand (1,000)
of the ultimate population in accordance with the following standards by types
of recreation and park areas:
Types Of Recreation Area Size Range (Minimum) Minimum Acres Per 1,000
                                              Population
Types Of Recreation Area       Size Range (Minimum) Minimum Acres Per 1,000
                                                    Population
                                                   
Play lot                       8,000 square feet    Not applicable
                                                   
Neighborhood park              3.5 acres            1.0
                                                   
School - park (neighborhood    6 acres              1.5
playground)
                                                   
Communitywide recreation       12 acres             1.5
park
                                                   
District - township recreation 15 acres             2.0
park
                                                  Total: 6.0 acres of and per
                                                    1,000 people
 
   B.   Location: The official plan of the village and any plans and standards
adopted by the affected park district shall be used as guidelines for locating
sites. A park site adjoining all elementary school sites of not less than five
(5) acres shall be considered a requirement. A central location which will
serve equally the entire development is most desirable. In large developments,
these sites can be located throughout the development according to
establishment standards for park distances.
   C.   Credit For Private Open Spaces And Recreation Areas: When subdividers
or developers provide their own open space for recreation areas and facilities,
it has the effect of reducing the demand for local public recreational
services.
Depending on the size of the developments, a portion of the park and recreation
area in subdivisions or planned unit developments may, at the option of the
village board, be provided in the form of "private" open space in lieu of
dedicated "public" open space. The extent of sale shall be determined by the
village board, based upon the needs of the projected residents and in
conformance to the total park and recreational land for the general area.
In general, a substitution of private open space for dedicated parks will imply
a substantially higher degree of improvement and the installation of
recreational facilities, including equipment by the developer as part of his
obligation. Detailed plans of such areas, including specifications of
facilities to be installed, must be approved by the village and before any
credit is given for private recreational areas, the subdivider or developer
must guarantee that these private recreational areas will be permanently
maintained for such use by the execution of the appropriate legal documents.
Private swimming clubs are included in this provision. When an adjustment for
private recreation areas is warranted, it will be necessary to compute the
total park land dedication that would have been required from the subdivision
or planned unit development and then subtract the credit to be given. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-4: CRITERIA FOR REQUIRING A CONTRIBUTION IN LIEU OF PARK AND SCHOOL SITES:
Where the development is small and the resulting site is too small to be
practical, or when the available land is inappropriate for park and
recreational purposes or a school site, the village shall require the
subdivider or developer to pay a cash contribution in lieu of land dedication
required. The cash contribution shall be held by the village to be used solely
for the acquisition of park and recreational land as hereinbefore classified to
serve the immediate or future needs of the residents of that subdivision or
developments, or the improvement of other existing local parks and recreational
land which already serves such need. The cash contributions in lieu of school
sites shall be collected by the village and forwarded semiannually (January 1
and July 1) to the school district to be used solely for the use in the
acquisition of land for a school site to serve immediate or future needs of
children from that subdivision or development, or for the improvement to any
existing school site which already serves such needs, but not for the
construction of any school buildings or additions thereto.
   A.   Fair Market Value: The cash contributions in lieu of land shall be
based on the "fair market value" of the acres of land in the area improved as
specified herein, that otherwise would have been dedicated as park and
recreation and school sites. It has been determined that the present "fair
market value" of such improved land in and surrounding the village is thirty
nine thousand dollars ($39,000.00) per acre and such figure shall be used in
making any calculation herein unless the subdivider or developer files a
written objection thereto. In the event of any such objection, the developer
shall submit an appraisal showing the "fair market value" of such improved land
in the area of his development or other evidence thereof and final
determination of said "fair market value" per acre of such improved land shall
be made by the village board based upon such information submitted by the
subdivider or developer and from other sources which may be submitted to the
village board by the park district, school district or others.
   B.   Criteria For Requiring The Dedication And A Fee: There will be
situations in subdivisions or planned unit developments when a combination of
land dedication and a contribution in lieu of land are both necessary. These
occasions will arise when:
      1.   Only a portion of the land to be developed is proposed as the
location for a park or school site. That portion of the land within the
subdivision falling within the park or school location shall be dedicated as a
site as aforesaid, and a cash contribution in lieu thereof shall be required
for any additional land that would have to be dedicated.
      2.   A major part of the local park or recreation site or school site has
already been acquired and only a small portion of land is needed from the
development to complete the site. The remaining portions shall be required by
dedication and a cash contribution in lieu thereof shall be required. (Ord.
610, 4-9-2001)

In the event a subdivider or developer files a written objection to the table
of estimated ultimate population listed above, he shall submit his own
demographic study showing the estimated additional population to be generated
from the subdivision or planned unit development and, in that event, final
determination of the density formula to be used in such calculations shall be
made by the village board based upon such demographic information submitted by
the subdivider or developer and from other sources which may be submitted to
the village board by the school district or others. It is recognized that
population density, age distribution and local conditions change over the
years, and the specific formula for the dedication of land or the payment of
fees in lieu thereof, as stated herein, is subject to periodic review and
amendment if necessary. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-6: RESERVATION OF ADDITIONAL LAND:
Where the comprehensive plan or the standards of the village call for a larger
amount of park and recreational land or school sites in a particular
subdivision or planned unit development than the developer is required to
dedicate, the land needed beyond the developer's contribution shall be reserved
for subsequent purchase by the village or other public body designated by the
village, provided that such acquisition is made within one year from the date
of approval of the final plat, or if an agreement between the developer and the
village is recorded outlining specific conditions for the conveyance of such
property. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-7: COMBINING WITH ADJOINING DEVELOPMENTS:
Where the subdivision or planned unit development is less than forty (40)
acres, public open space or a school site which is to be dedicated should,
where possible, be combined with dedications from adjoining developments in
order to produce usable recreation areas or school sites without hardship on a
particular developer. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-8: TOPOGRAPHY AND GRADING:
The slope, topography and geology of the dedicated site as well as its
surroundings must be suitable for its intended purposes. Grading on sites
dedicated for park and recreational uses shall not differ greatly from
surrounding land unless approved by the village board. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-9: IMPROVED SITES:
All sites shall be dedicated in a condition ready for full service of
electrical, water, sewer and streets (including enclosed drainage, curb and
gutter) as applicable to the location of the site, or acceptable provision made
therefor. The sidewalks and trees normally included within the definition of
"improved" sites may be deleted due to the delay time between dedication of any
such school site and construction of school facilities thereon. (Ord. 610, 4-9-
2001)
10-4-10: TITLE TO SITES:
All sites shall be conveyed to the village, or other public body designated by
the village, either by warranty or trustee's deed. The subdivider or developer
shall be responsible for conveying good, merchantable title to such sites, and
shall be responsible for payment of all real estate taxes to the date of
conveyance, including any agricultural roll back taxes which might be extended
or levied against such sites, for any tax years or periods prior to the time of
conveyance. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-11: DEDICATION OR CONTRIBUTION AS A CONDITION OF ANNEXATION:
The dedications of land or cash contributions as required by this chapter shall
also be required as a condition to the annexation of any land to the village
and provisions therefor shall be incorporated in any preannexation agreement
governing such land. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-4-12: CASH CONTRIBUTION FOR LIBRARY PURPOSES:
In addition to the dedication of lands for school sites, parks and other public
areas as provided in section
10-4-1 of this chapter, and the provisions of section
10-4-4 of this chapter calling for contributions in lieu of park and school
sites, there shall be a cash contribution for library purposes in the amount of
seventy five dollars ($75.00) per subdivided residential lot to be paid by a
subdivider or developer on all lots improved within the village. This
contribution for library purposes shall be collected at the time that all
building permit fees and development fees are collected from the developer or
subdivider and shall be passed along to the Franklin Grove Public Library (or
any legal successor thereto) at the times and in the manner determined
appropriate by the corporate authorities of the village. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 5
REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
10-5-1: Assurance For The Completion Of Required Improvements
10-5-2: Installation Of Required Improvements
10-5-1: ASSURANCE FOR THE COMPLETION OF REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Performance Guarantee: No work shall be started on any improvement
until the applicant has posted a guarantee in the amount equal to one hundred
percent (100%) of the estimated costs of the subdivision improvements as
approved by the village engineer, in order to ensure that the work is performed
according to the plans and specifications and according to good engineering and
installation practices. The guarantee shall also be sufficient to secure all
lot improvements on the individual lots of the subdivision as required in these
regulations, and shall be conditional upon the installation of the required
improvements within two (2) years from the date that the final plat is approved
by the board of trustees. The performance guarantee shall comply with all
statutory requirements and shall be satisfactory to the village attorney as to
form and manner of execution, and shall be approved by the village board as to
amount and surety and conditions satisfactory to the village board. Such
guarantee shall be secured by either:
      1.   A certificate of deposit with or an escrow account at a federally
insured bank or savings and loan association with resources of at least ten
million dollars ($10,000,000.00) under the provisions of an escrow agreement,
approved in form by the village attorney, in an amount equal to one hundred
percent (100%) of the estimated construction cost as approved by the village
engineer and subject to draw by the village to install subdivision improvements
if they are not installed by the subdivider in accordance to the plan and
specifications and/or according to good engineering practices; or
      2.   A clean, nondeclining, irrevocable letter of credit in such form as
approved by the village attorney, issued by a federally insured bank or savings
and loan association with resources of at least ten million dollars
($10,000,000.00) in an amount equal to one hundred percent (100%) of the
estimated construction cost as approved by the village engineer. The letter
shall provide that funds be drawn only by the village.
   B.   Reduction Of Performance Guarantee: A performance guarantee shall be
reduced only upon recommendation of the village engineer and approval by the
village Board upon application for payout by the subdivider in amounts such
that funds or credit remaining will always equal one hundred percent (100%) of
the value of the uncompleted work, as determined by the village engineer; and
such that not more than ninety percent (90%) of the guarantee amount is
released prior to the acceptance of the improvements by the village in
accordance with section 10-5-5 of this chapter.
   C.   Release Of Performance Guarantee: The village shall not release the
performance guarantee until there has been filed a maintenance guarantee in
accordance with section 10-5-4C of this chapter and not until there has been an
acceptance of improvements by the village in accordance with the provisions of
section 10-5-5 of this chapter. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
10-5-2: INSTALLATION OF REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Proposed Subdivision: The developer of a proposed subdivision shall
install or cause to be provided the following facilities in accordance with the
standards set forth in chapters 3 and 4 of this title and other engineering
specifications on file with the village engineer:
      1.   All roadways, private drives, alleys, gutters and street drainage
facilities.
      2.   All sidewalks located within public areas.
      3.   A waterline connection for each lot of the proposed subdivision.
Such water supply lines shall be connected to the village water system at least
at the two (2) most advantageous locations as determined by the village
engineer, taking into account the size of the village water main at such
locations and the expected demands of the proposed subdivision. Dead end water
mains shall be prohibited. Additional standards and specifications are on file
with the village engineer.
      4.   Fire hydrants of the type and quality specified in standards on file
with the village engineer.
      5.   A sanitary sewer line connection for each lot. Such sanitary sewer
line shall be connected to the sanitary sewer system of the village at such
point or points as the village engineer shall determine based upon the location
and size of the village sanitary sewer system in relation to the estimated flow
of the sanitary sewers of the proposed subdivision. Additional standards and
specifications are on file with the village engineer. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
CHAPTER 6
AMENDMENTS
SECTION:
10-6-1: Amendments To Title
10-6-1: AMENDMENTS TO TITLE:
   A.   The village board may from time to time on its own motion, or on
petition, or on recommendation of the plan commission amend, supplement, or
repeal the regulations and provisions of this title.
   B.   Every such proposed amendment or change whether initiated by the
village board or by petition shall be referred to the board of appeals for
report thereon resulting from public hearing as provided in subsection C of
this section.
   C.   The board of appeals, by resolution adopted at a stated meeting, shall
fix the time and place of public hearing on the proposed amendments and cause
notice to be given not more than thirty (30) days nor less than fifteen (15)
days before the hearing by publishing a notice thereof at least once in one or
more newspapers published in the municipality, or, if no newspapers are
published therein, then in one or more newspapers with a general circulation
within the municipality. (Ord. 610, 4-9-2001)
